# Resident Advisor Best Of Lists Archive

Total articles archived: 112
Total items found: 1950

## [Best Music 2025](https://ra.co/features/4425)
Date: 2025-11-04T17:00:11.000Z

### keiyaA â€“ hooke's law (XL Recordings)
> Bad blood. Depression. Snide landlords. And then there's all the fun in between. Written during a time of deep self-reflection, hooke's law follows keiyaA as she tears everything and everyone up only to emerge more invigorated than ever. Following her beloved debut album, these 19 tracks are a remarkable crossover between R&B, ambient and the kind of experimental music you might expect from genre-adverse producers like Klein and DJ Haram. Soulful and sexy, scornful and weird, the album charts an explosive period of emotional growth.

### DJ SWISHA â€“ FIRST HAND SMOKE (Self-Released)
> On his debut album, New York club king DJ SWISHA samples house, R&B and pop, folding his encyclopedic music knowledge into a pointedly North American package. Here, Baltimore club meets Jersey club, and footwork and juke beats rearrange the soulful molecules of R&B. There's nothing quite as earth shattering as "CLUB MEGAMIXXX" (RA's best track of 2023), but these are dance floor tools refined for the album format, meaning there's plenty of living-room listenability.

### DJ Babatr â€“ Root Echoes (Hakuna Kalula)
> Carefully selected from more than 700 archived works made between 2003 and 2007, Root Echoes documents raptor house at its subversive peak. With each sweaty, speeding track, DJ Babatr redefines the genre with a watertight mission: amplifying Afro-Venezuelan voices.

### Various â€“ Techno KayÅ Vol. 1 - Japanese Techno Pop 1981 - 1989 (Compiled by Dubby & Antal) (Rush Hour)
> Dubby, one of the curators of Japanese Techno Pop 1981 - 1989, recently told Magazine Sixty that techno pop has a "rather cheesy and slightly tacky image" in Japan. This compilation aims to correct that narrativeâ€”and how. Focusing on the genre's niche and experimental branches, it takes listeners from the cosmic funk of TPO and Linda's "Rock The Hour" to the leftfield sound collage of Kazuo Ohtani's "Last Battle."

### Blawan â€“ SickElixir (XL Recordings)
> These 14 brutal tracks judder from industrial hip-hop to syncopated sludge, redefining what a techno LP can be. But what really gives this record its otherworldly feel is Blawan's voice. Twisted into a monstrous rasp through layers of filters, it's the first thing we hear and it holds everything together from there on out.

### Carrier â€“ Rhythm Immortal (Modern Love)
> As a producer, Carrier specialises in white space. On Rhythm Immortal, the UK artist's use of percussion is the centrepiece, but the gaps he leaves in between the beats are the most compelling. Dub techno, ambient, industrial and jazz motifs unite in perfect harmony. Just listen to "Offshore," where slithering synths and hiccuping drums are tempered by saxophone and piano chords that gleam quietly like little spots of sun.

### Various â€“ Rhythm 2 Revolt Solidarity Compilation (Hood Rave)
> BAE BAE's Hood Rave party is one of Los Angeles' best. Why? Because of its outspoken commitment to liberation. The platform's first compilation splits proceeds between the Gaza Mutual Aid Solidarity Fund and NDLON's Immigrant Defense Fund, featuring songs that skitter between ambient, techno and East Coast club. Daniel Pineda's "Do Something" captures the sense of urgency underlining both politics and dance floors right now. Note the blaring siren, club breaks and a voice echoing, "Do something to stop the killing."

### Felicity J Lord â€“ FJL (STROOM.TV)
> Although technically released in late September, this album is catnip for fans of Voice Actor, Klein and Dean Blunt. A 26-track LP might seem like overkill these days, but FJL's vignettes are made for the ADD generation. These short songs loop familiar pop and R&B samplesâ€”cozy and familiar playgrounds from which emerge the most chaotic spoken word you'll hear on a record this year.

### Charmaine Lee â€“ Tulpa (Kou Records)
> This is the kind of record that will deeply satisfy experimental music enthusiasts who wait patiently every year for cutting-edge festivals like Unsound and Dripping. The New York artist's dark ambient soundscapes blanket intense, complex vocal processing that turns quick breaths, hums and tongue clicks into shuddering rhythms.

### CRRDR â€“ LATINCORE LEGEND (LATINCORE)
> BogotÃ¡'s CRRDR doesn't take his title of "Latincore legend" lightly. The genre he champions takes the speeding BPMs and blistering intensity of hardstyle, blending it with guaracha, reggaeton and dembow. Throughout his debut album, bachata meets Jersey club ("Te Gusta Mi Bachata"), Eurodance fuses with guaracha ("Oh Baby") and IDM synths glimmer over a reggaeton beat. Tapping vocalists from Ecuador, Puerto Rico, Colombia, Mexico, Venezuela and Chile, this a sublime representation of the Latincore movement.

### Dania â€“ Listless (Somewhere Press)
> Smoky drums, slushy guitar and a delicate voice that whispers through the darkness. Comprising seven tracks written after midnight, Dania's Listless takes the mystery of the witching hour and infuses it into this superb journey through shadow-filled trip-hop and fantastical ambient.

### JasmÃ­n â€“ Bite The Hand That Feeds You (Hessle Audio)
> On her first fully fledged recordâ€”and Hessle Audio's 50th releaseâ€”JasmÃ­n continues to explore the label's techno-dubstep roots. This is a wicked batch of searing techno that snakes between Latin American rhythms, industrial and the deep blare of dubstep.

### Beatrice M. â€“ Midnight Swim (Tectonic Recordings)
> Another hit from an artist who can't stop making them. Rippling from dubstep to dub techno, Beatrice M. creates tracks with the quiet dynamism and depth of an ocean. It's so detailed that it's less of a soundscape than an entire new world of slippery bass and minuscule sounds, urging you to climb inside.

### Qemist â€“ The New Juke Tape (Moveltraxx)
> Juke and footwork were born in Chicago but they maintain a strong grip beyond the Midwest. Based out of Memphis, Tennessee, Qemist takes these genres and puts them into a blender, resulting in a high-BPM fusion of unwieldy, banging East Coast club, jungle and R&B.

### Full Circle â€“ Beyond Knowhere (Good Morning Tapes)
> Following a corrective Goa trance compilation aiming to give the Indian-born psychedelic dance sound its flowers, Parisian duo Full Circle continue their focus on the misunderstood genre on Beyond Knowhere. This is progressive house indebted to the psychedelia of Goa trance, featuring plenty of reverbed sitar and detailed acid. "Painting Noise" even has a trip-hop chug.

### De Grandi â€“ Testa Dura (Tratratrax)
> This full-throttle EP takes cues from dubstep, techno and club music, looping twisty, squelchy basslines and heaving drums to explosive effect. The record flies out the traps: the opening title track plows through a monstrous bassline and quick-fire drums. The remixes do the blistering tunes justice, with Call Super and Parris bringing a quirky, drum-forward house touch on their "Yeah But Still" version.

### Wata Igarashi, Polygonia â€“ Cross Passage (Reclaim Your City)
> Polygonia and Wata Igarashi approach hypnotic ecstasy from different angles: the former goes for blissed-out baubles; the latter embraces the growl of blazing arpeggios. On their latest collaborative EP, you can hear Polygonia's melodic brightness, while the grimey deepness sounds like the handiwork of Igarashi. Cross Passage is a gold mine for psychedelic techno enthusiasts.

### NTS - 100% D'Angelo 
> Few artists have reshaped modern soul as profoundly as D'Angelo. Following his death in October, Shy One offers a heartfelt tribute tracing the arc of his genius, from the church-rooted warmth of Brown Sugar to the fractured funk of Black Messiah. Moving through hits, deep cuts and collaborations, this two-hour mix celebrates an artist who was forever chasing the divine through groove, analogue grit and a one-of-a-kind lyricism.

### Closing Set at Sustain-Release 2025 
> As autumn settles across the northern hemisphere, a wave of festival recordings return to remind us of summer's glow. Among the standouts from this year's romp in Camp Kennybrook is a luminous two-hour journey from Mia Koden, RA's Breaking Through artist of 2024. Rooted in a deep love of Black diasporic music, she moves from dubstep to hip-hop, drifting from Commodo and Daweh Congo to Bahamadia and Minnie Riperton. According to one RA staffer on the dance floor, there were "tears everywhere" and a voice periodically yelling, "What the fuck, Mia?!"

### Sugar Free at Selectors - Dekmantel 2025 
> A Sugar Free set lands differently. There's a sleazy allure to her take on techno, house and breakbeat, and her vinyl-only sets honour the tradition of the format while always sounding strikingly fresh. The Madrid-based DJ has a knack for uncanny blends: hypnotic grooves meet elastic basslines and trippy, late-night textures weave between deep techno, minimal and psychedelic trance. For her Dekmantel debut, she delivered what she does best: deep, headsy, timeless dance music.

### NTS 
> Nine years since his last NTS Radio appearance, Henry Rollins returns with his trademark intensity intact. The LA iconâ€”who has donned the role of band frontman, actor, essayist and more throughout his polymathic careerâ€”spends two hours digging through punk, hardcore and new wave treasures. It's an essential look into Rollin's unique, far-reaching collection.

### Live At Dripping 
> Seattle's Succubass is a pillar of the US DIY underground, and for their Friday night set at Dripping, they turned The Barn into a fever dream of bass and distortion. Moving from Zvvra's tactile techno and the dub of Gil.Barte to the heady steppers of Commodo & Gantz, Succubass stitches together something raw, cinematic and deeply physical. Each drop makes it feel like the music was testing the limits of the small room.

### MNMT 488 
> Listen to any set from Kia, Priori or Cousin and you'll likely hear the dubbed out productions of Mexican-Jamaican producer Andy Martin. Based in Guadalajara, he has become a quiet force in the global underground, uniting sci-fi techno with the rhythmic sensibilities of the Caribbean and Latin America. For Norway's Monument Festival, he delivers a transportive set that moves from the weightless dub pressure of Bukkha and Abstract Man into sleek, hypnotic techno from Oscar Mulero and Unbalance. Here's an hour of music laced with deep bass, subtle psychedelia and shimmering percussive detail.

### IT.podcast.s14e07 
> Scott Zacharias has long been one of Detroit's best-kept secrets. His singular, offbeat taste has made his No Way Back sets the stuff of legend. This year's closing in the Outer Space Room was among his most personal yetâ€”as Zacharias recounts in the description, his partner joined him on-stage at the end of the set to celebrate her pregnancy. Anchored by the spirit of Arthur Russell's "In The Light Of The Miracle," the set drifts through everything from cosmic dub and art-pop melancholia to ambient techno and ecstatic house over the course of five hours.

### Making Time 2025 
> As cofounder of experimental label SLINK, K Wata has become one of New York's most exciting new producers, known for slinky micro-dubs and bass music that messes with perception. His set from this year's Making Time âˆž follows that same thread: psychedelic, dubstep-adjacent and full of pressure, threading tracks from Deadbeat, Wata Igarashi and Paleman into something that feels somehow both heavy and weightless. It's club music that breathes, flexes and rearranges the air around you.

### Malibu â€“ Vanities (YEAR0001)
> French electronic artist Malibu is known for her transcendental performances. When paired with white beams of light that circle her audience, her wordless live sets become deeply surreal. Vanities, her filmic debut album, aims to transport you to that otherworldly state. While it draws from the soothing chords and glittery instrumentation of New Age and baroque music, the silvery pop melodies steal the show. This is weighty, elegant ambient that should be listened to with a proper sub, so that its immersive waves of sound envelop you.

### Paul St. Hilaire â€“ Paul St. Hilaire - w/ The Producers (Kynant Records)
> Paul St. Hilaire (AKA Tikiman) has contributed his sweet, sinuous vocals to dub techno records since his early work with Basic Channel. His latest album is a treat to longtime fans, featuring a host of top-drawer producers. Shinichi Atobe's lurid house bubbles under Hilaire's reverbed vocals; Priori's zippy tech house meets his heavily distorted asides. This is collaborative experimentation at its finest.

### Acopia â€“ Blush Response (Scenic Route)
> Rich with shoegazey guitars, simmering electronica and frontwoman Kate Durman's most plaintive vocals to date, Blush Response luxuriates in rock elements that lingered in the margins of previous Acopia albums. The rawness of the instrumentation, peppered with tiny textural details, distinguishes this LP from the group's signature dream pop. By unpixelating their previous sound, Acopia reach the perfect balance between gut-wrenching drama and understated surrender.

### james K â€“ Friend (AD 93)
> On her hotly anticipated new LP, Friend, james K sets herself loose inside a carefully constructed assemblage of drum & bass, trip-hop and shoegaze, carving offbeat shapes from the contemporary resurgence of all three genres. The album is crisper, cleaner and more complex than any of her back catalogue, drawing from crystalline pop and rock while maintaining her characteristic enigma. Full of lush, expansive pads and skittering microbeats, these songs sound like half-remembered dreams.

### Sammy Virji â€“ Same Day Cleaning (Polydor)
> If you like Sammy Virji's radio-friendly, vocal-heavy UKG, you're going to love Same Day Cleaning. There's a real musicality to the album, which spans garage house, speed garage and more, with the warmth of acoustic instruments occasionally squeezed in. In tandem with some of the UK's most in-demand MCs and vocalistsâ€”Flowdan, Skepta, Issey Crossâ€”Virji totally steps up, showcasing songwriting agility that explains the current hype and glut of sold-out shows.

### Joanne Robertson â€“ Blurrr (AD 93)
> Joanne Robertson is widely known for her vocal cameos on records by Dean Blunt and Elias RÃ¸nnenfelt. But her latest solo album, Blurrr, establishes her as an artist in her own right. Written in between painting sessions and caring for her toddler, the gorgeous LP features drumless guitar ballads alongside contributions from cellist Oliver Coates. Most arresting, though, are the moods she conveys. Achieving a compositional yin-yang, she somehow scores both the euphoria of depression and the grief of joy.

### Kelman Duran â€“ Scorpio Falling (Scorpio Red)
> Dembow experimentalist Kelman Duran makes shadowy music that conjures scenes of sodden tunnel paths at nightfall. Beneath his shrouded pads are distinctly Caribbean sounds, like dancehall and reggaeton. Scorpio Falling, his first album since 2021's Night In Tijuana, is a gritty journey through jazz, Memphis rap and dark ambient with spurts of spritely dembow breaking the meditative lull.

### Titanic â€“ HAGEN (TAR / MM / UOH)
> Titanic, the avant-garde project from producer and guitarist I. la CatÃ³lica and cellist Mabe Fratti, returns with punkish elegance on HAGEN. The chords are brighter, Fratti's vocals more dynamic and the ascendent alternative pop swells to new heights. The instrumentation is raw and brash, and Fratti fits right into the mould, her voice bearing visceral emotions with fascinating lightness.

### Lucrecia Dalt â€“ A Danger To Ourselves (RVNG Intl.)
> The past few years have been intense for Lucrecia Dalt. The Colombian artist has experienced several seizures and an eight-second stop to her heart since her last album, Â¡Ay!. She also fell head over heels in love. Her latest alt-pop album, A Danger To Ourselves, is full-on haunting, as she whispers through a hall of tip-toeing cello and guitar plucks. Tracks like "stelliformia" carry the immersive lyricism that you'll want to listen to alone in your room. A Danger To Ourselves bristles with the kind of eerie love poems that only Dalt could write.

### YS â€“ Burn (ERF)
> Breezing through laidback trip-hop, luminescent IDM and mellow vocal samples, Burn captures the understated cool that characterised trip-hop's golden era. On "Moth," Janet Jackson exhales through delightfully broken drums. "End" skews slightly darker, featuring a pitched-down vocal announcing that "the end of the world is coming" over sparkling beats. Wherever you end up on this masterpiece, you'll find a goldmine of sophisticated textures.

### LÃ‰O LA NUIT â€“ LE DON DES LARMES (Knekelhuis)
> On LE DON DES LARMES, Franco-Algerian vocalist LÃ‰O LA NUIT is accompanied by guitar, cello and the swirl of her own harmonised vocals. Written for her newborn child, these lilting folk lullabies are inspired by her Kabyle upbringing surrounded by Algerian chaabi. This is a strikingly beautiful portrait of her wispy vocals, which don't need much enhancement to make you feel like you've fallen into a world in which everything has suddenly and blissfully slowed down.

### Skepta, Fred again.. â€“ Skepta .. Fred (Epic Records)
> Although Skepta still hasn't released his long-awaited album Knife and Fork, he's put out a flurry of extremely good singles and even stepped in to replace Deftones at Glastonbury with a much talked-about performance. For his next trick, he gives Fred again.., the super-producer of mixed reputation, some underground cred. The tracks are a welcome, sub-blowing display of 140 BPM club music, making even Fred again..'s most dedicated critics struggle to deny their fun.

### Maara â€“ Revenge from the Penthouse EP (Ancient Records)
> Maara is an exceptionally versatile producer. Her debut album, The Ancient Truth, reveled in slow, chuggy trip-hop, followed by a motley of cheeky, sapphic singles like "Mind The WAP" and, more recently, "I Wanna Scissor Ft. My Hot Ex." But really, her specialty is in building hypnotic, multi-textural worlds. Revenge from the Penthouse does this by barrelling through shades of progressive house, trance and breakbeats, keeping us completely locked across all five tracks.

### TYGAPAW â€“ IMMIGRANT (Tresor)
> The connection that Jamaican artist TYGAPAW has to their queerness and home country is written all across their raucous, politically charged techno. On their new EP, IMMIGRANT, they portray the immigrant experience in post-Trump America as oppressive and repetitive. "Black Trans Masculine Experience" gives the floor to Kings-Lee Rose, who discusses the societal isolation of Black trans masculine people before a flood of percussion fills the soundscape. In TYGAPAW's hands, deep feelings are meant to be released through the hipsâ€”you'll hear Jersey club, dancehall and techno rhythms skitter across "M32."

### JSPORT â€“ No Turning Back (JSPORT WORLD)
> From the moment you step off the ledge of its misty opener, No Turning Back situates you in banger after banger. The club rhythms are fierce and unrelenting, speeding through Jersey club beats, dancehall and red-hot R&B samples, all with the iciness of grime. The liner notes couldn't have said it better: "These aren't tracks you playâ€”they're tracks that play you."

### Sam Goku â€“ Explorations 02 (Permanent Vacation)
> Explorations 02 is a frolic through dub techno, fuzzy breakbeats and psychedelic deep house. The rhythms are effervescent and the drums occasionally go hard. But the one trait that stays consistent throughout is the record's glistening aura, made possible by birdsong, muted pads and chiming melodies. This EP is as close to nature as the dance floor.

### NEW YORK â€“ Push (nypop)
> Push sounds eerily familiar. In many ways, it's reminiscent of the late '00s, a time when artists like Chairlift, MGMT and Owl City ruled the radio with glitchy beats that seemed to blast euphoria into listeners' veins. NEW YORK builds on this template with a punkish haze, whispering into the mic as bleeps burst around them.

### Croft â€“ Sanctuary / Shifty (Hang Tough)
> On this two-track EP, Nottingham's Croft offers twisted, hypnotic tech house. Metallic dings penetrate the busy soundscape, as plasticky noises contort across shuffling broken beats. These are the kinds of trippy curveballs that force crowds to stick around.

### Jessy Lanza â€“ "Slapped By My Life" (Hyperdub)
> Jessy Lanza wrote "Slapped By My Life" while her husband was undergoing cancer treatment and she longed to escape into an emotion that felt miles away from her everyday sadness. This track is pure optimism, carried by a sweet hook ("I miss you when you go") and colourful beats flying by at 158 BPM. It's one for the lovers.

### Kia b2b Bitter Babe - Climate of Fear 
> On paper, Kia b2b Bitter Babe shouldn't really work. The former loves supple shades of dub, IDM and techno, while the latter leans towards hazy, sensual and high-energy tunes. But this recording from Berlin party Climate of Fear proves otherwise. Across two hours of molten techno, trance and pan-Latin dance music, the duo showcase their command of complex rhythmsâ€”and why they're two of the best in the game right now.

### Gavsborg - Kiosk Radio 
> Jamaican dance music producers don't get the same recognition as their peers in Detroit, Chicago or Berlin. Hailing from East Kingston, Gavsborg carries the torch for this generation. The Berlin-based Equiknoxx founder has spent more than a decade reshaping dancehall with a leftfield sensibilityâ€”first breaking through with Busy Signal's charting single, "Step Out," before collaborating with everyone from reggae dub prince Addis Pablo to hip-hop icon Missy Elliott. On Brussels' Kiosk Radio, Gavsborg dropped a scorching mix of dancehall, jungle, zouk and dub, laced with the playful surrealism that defines his productions.

### EMA - subglow/Live 6 per:sona 
> There's a new generation of dubstep kids in town pushing the sound forward in thrilling directions. EMA, founder of the dub-focused Woozy label, is a key force in the movement alongside the likes of Beatrice M. and Mia Koden. For CCL's subglow series, she shared a recording from her kaleidoscopic set at French festival per:sona. Much like her wider work, it's adventurous and unpretentious, with two hours of tightly wound techno, modern steppers and snarling drum & bass grounded in spooky bassweight.

### Short Span - Theory Therapy 82 
> Across its eight-year run, Blowing Up The Workshop tested the limits of the online mix format, giving artists space to experiment and shaping a generation of adventurous listeners along the way. That same curatorial spirit runs through this new Theory Therapy session, which sees BUTW founder Matthew Kent digging into forgotten '00s CDs to piece together a loose set of dubbed-out ambient and downtempo house, with plenty of clicky percussion reminiscent of minimal's dominant era.

### Keanu Nelson - NTS Radio (13th September 2025) 
> Broadcasting from Papunya, one of Australia's most isolated communities, Luritja artist Keanu Nelson offers a rare window into the music and voices of the Northwestern territory. For his latest NTS Radio show, he drifts from ancestral chants and spectral atmospheres to desert rock and jazzy synth pop. The mix moves gracefully between the celebratory and the contemplative, its remarkable range making for a perfect morning listen.

### Maito & Kuba'97 - Live at Klub Dramatik Festival 
> Klub Dramatik is part of a new wave of Belgian parties putting the country's scene on the map. The first entry in its live series comes from two locals at the heart of the action: Maito and Kuba'97. Over three hours, they weave understated house, techno and psychedelia with the patience and flow that comes from years spent on the dance floor, beautifully capturing the exploratory spirit that has Belgium abuzz right now.

### Spurge - Nowadays Nonstop: 06-21-25 
> For his Nowadays debut during Juneteenth weekend, New York DJ and musician Spurge paid homage to his definition of Black sonic excellence. Featuring a range of mostly Black artistsâ€”K-HAND, Bad Brains, Princess Peggie, DJ Spanish Flyâ€”it's a danceable, thought-provoking showcase of Black artistry across noise, ambient techno and peak-time club.

### Camille Mandoki - Series 029 
> Mexico City vocalist Camille Mandokiâ€”who features on Lucrecia Dalt's new albumâ€”makes powerful sound art. Her gauzy compositions and choral voice carry serious emotional weight, shaking listeners to their core. Her contribution to local mix series Lapi + Filia is just as poignant, featuring delicate jazz, ambient and folk that evoke introspection and fulfillment.

### DJ K â€“ Radio Libertadora ! (Nyege Nyege Tapes)
> Radio Libertadora ! takes bruxaria, a maniacal strain of Brazilian baile funk, and imbues it with the sound of political discordance. Deteriorating synth lines buzz like digital waste and sirens bleat endlessly towards societal collapse. The album plays with genres such as techno, house and '00s hip-hop to bring its messages home. Like the directors of the most exhilarating action films, DJ K specialises in organised chaos. Resilience has rarely sounded so electrifying.

### Blood Orange â€“ Essex Honey (RCA)
> More than being an excellent producer, Dev Hynes, AKA Blood Orange, is a master of various styles. He's produced experimental R&B with Solange, composed for films and worked with the London Symphony Orchestra. His first album in six years brings his experimental edge to the fore, with a hefty features list including Mabe Fratti, Caroline Polachek and Tirzah. These are gorgeously gentle and stripped-back guitar- and piano-led pieces.

### Valesuchi â€“ Futuro Cercano (Discos Nutabe)
> On Futuro Cercano, Valesuchi's newfound love of higher BPMs is on full display, featuring not just techno and electro but also dubstep ("L.O.S."). Just about every synthline is in a minor key and evokes the imagery of a Halloween house of mirrors. Still, there are plenty of beautiful moments of elation. Just wait for when trance chords turn "Regreso" into a sunset anthem.

### Nourished By Time â€“ The Passionate Ones (XL Recordings)
> Nourished By Time's second album, The Passionate Ones, ponders love, loneliness and late-stage capitalism over an impeccable blend of electro funk and breezy indie pop. Its soulful sound, driven by cruising guitars and euphoric synths, buffs up his candid lyrics, making his verses (which channel the extreme honesty of 2013-era Tyler, the Creator) all the more relatable. This is music for when you're down and out, and you just need a good tune to get you through the day.

### Amaarae â€“ Black Star (Interscope Records)
> Featuring cameos from Black luminaries like PinkPantheress, Naomi Campbell and Bree Runway, Black Star embraces the Black electronic music that formed Amaarae's youth. These sounds wafted from the streets to her ears in Accra at the age of six, then at eight in Atlanta, then New Jersey when she was 11. At its best, Black Star shows an artist amplifying Afrodiasporic club traditions with modern verve, unlocking a new wave of Black pop stardom along the way.

### Kaytranada â€“ AIN'T NO DAMN WAY! (RCA)
> Kaytranada's surprise new album, AIN'T NO DAMN WAY!, is the star's finest since 99.9%. It bottles the nonchalant sex appeal and restrained production of his 2016 debut, then distills it, cutting out the featured vocalists and paring down the runtime. The result: a dextrous blend of soul, R&B and old-school hip-hopâ€”styles that he's only previously explored with singers or rappersâ€”packaged in his signature dance MO.

### Stone â€“ Dream Curtain Eternally Gentle (3XL)
> Dream Curtain Eternally Gentle adds chugging, perfectly sedate trip-hop beats to Stone's already blissfully organic ambient and squiggly IDM. "Tiny" wraps emotion into reverbed guitar and vocal blips. "Pixie" is light and pensive, with synth work and chimes that land like gentle pebbles against misty lily pads. This is one for overcast mornings and late-night drives.

### Kloke â€“ Lucidity (Mindgames)
> On Lucidity, Kloke delivers another excellent survey of modern jungle and drum & bass. Take "Invisible City," which transitions from soaring pads to angry breaks. The album's musicality, shown on the sweet, soulful melodies of "Spaces" and "The Man Who Began To Suspect He Was Made Of Glass," is balanced by some of the nastiest basslines you've ever heard.

### Oli XL â€“ Lick The Lens / Pt.1 (Warp)
> Six years after the release of his cherished debut album, Rogue Intruder, Soul Enhancer, Oli XL returns with another LP highlighting his glitched-out soundscapes and delightful, pitched-up vocals. This time he brings an all-star roster of guests, including james K, Chanel Beads and Ecco2k, making for a sound that leans closely to glitch pop.

### Susumu Yokota â€“ Skintone Edition Volume 1 (Lo Recordings)
> Seven albums tracing the genre-expansive genius of Japanese ambient legend Susumu Yokota. Get lost in the delicate triumph written into the skipping piano on "Morino Gakudan," groove to the loose, hand drum-driven house of "Pegasus Man" and lollygag to the guitar-laced ambient of "23 Degrees Dream."

### Various Artists â€“ kwia 4eva (kwia)
> In Kiana Mickles' nightlife column, Office Hours, Berlin ambient bar kwia was described as "a soft playground made for sensitive people." Now that the venue is facing the threat of closure, kwia 4ever is a sonic time capsule of the original soft club. Regular DJs Nick LeÃ³n, River Moon and mobilegirl contribute a relaxing medley of ambient, glitch and guitar music. Perfect for sinking into a plush couch.

### Guedra Guedra â€“ MUTANT (Smugglers Way)
> Guedra Guedra brings together an impressive assortment of Pan-African influences on MUTANT. Asymmetrical beats meet traditional instruments; bass music meets ancient rhythms. It's the kind of memorableâ€”and extremely danceableâ€”album that pushes the boundaries of every genre it touches.

### Skee Mask â€“ E (Self-released)
> Skee Mask impresses again on his surprise album, E. Intricate breakbeat science plays out on tracks like "Untitled 1017" and "501v2." Elsewhere, techno is rough-edged and deconstructed, with distorted beats lumbering forward like they're being pulled downhill.

### Florian TM Zeisig â€“ A New Life (STROOM)
> Awe-inspiring ambient that will instantly transport you to every peaceful moment you've experienced. Waves lap up against soaring saxophone on "Eternal Shore," the delicate layers of harmonies on "Die GroÃŸe Natur" recall the jubilation of the first day of spring, and on "Life's A Spiral," harp trickles down a celestial soundscape like rays of sunlight.

### keiyaA â€“ "Stupid Prizes" (XL Recordings)
> Play stupid games, win stupid prizes. keiyaA returns with her first song since the release of her cherished 2020 debut album, Forever, Ya Girl. This sneak peek at new music brings a haunting aura to her typically soulful R&B, and gives us a lot to look forward to in this new era.

### Paurro â€“ Sea Bunny (aanjel)
> Paurro's first EP on aanjel, her label with Valeriana, is a psychedelic journey through submerged basslines and progressive house squiggles. Listen closely as subtle layers of new sounds are introducedâ€”a flash of a breakbeat, a trickle of a hand drumâ€”and spritely vocals ooze out of the spaces between each curvilinear rhythm.

### JiaLing â€“ WUPS! (Sorry Records)
> JiaLing adds a little bit of everything to the Baltimore club formula: across these four tracks, there are nods to ballroom, diva house, dubstep and electro. The EP is bouncy, filled with cartoonish sound FX that channel the silly energy conveyed through a title like WUPS!

### Tracey â€“ Sleazy (AD 93)
> With 8-bit synths and scrappy lyrics, "Sleazy" has the deranged feel of an Adult Swim theme tune and the innovation of a SOPHIE song. Glitch by glitch, the mysterious duo paint a scandalous scene. Even if you're not quite sure what's going on, you'll be at the edge of your seatâ€”and loving it.

### Sofia Kourtesis â€“ Volver (Ninja Tune)
> Volver doubles down on Sofia Kourtesis's strengths. Recorded while caring for her late mother in Peru and working with queer and trans advocates, the EP offers many iterations of her joyful noise. "Canela Pura" has a bit of the old French Touch ooh la la filter that she often threads into her DJ sets, along with a skippy bassline and the backspin goofball energy of Eris Drew. Much of these tracks sound like a body in pleasure: on the ecstatic piano house of "Nitzan and Aminaa," percussion tickles the ears like a welcome hand on your back.

### Unsound Podcast 107: DJ E / Chuquimamani-Condori 
> First tested at the opening of last year's Unsound in KrakÃ³w, this mix captures the singular, hyper-charged style that has made Chuquimamani-Condori (AKA DJ E) one of electronic music's most unpredictable forces. It feels like a dispatch from an oasis far removed from the parameters of experimental music as we know it. Across 48 minutes, Andean folk, cumbia and country music are bent and spliced into a delirious wall of sound, stitched together with the Bolivian-American artist's signature soundboard FX.

### naffcast010 â¦¾ JasmÃ­n ð”ŒÕž. .Õžð¦¯ à­­ Ëš. áµŽáµŽ 
> For the tenth edition of NAFF's mix series, former De School resident JasmÃ­n swaps her usual broken bass sound for minimal house and techno. Recorded during a summer heatwave, the set layers faint voices, distorted drums and low-end pressure into a feverish atmosphere. Spanning long-time favourites (DJ Koze, Ricardo Villalobos) and recent digital finds, she leans into long, subtle blends, tapping into the ongoing resurgence of minimal's hypnotic pull.

### Animix One Hundred & Seventy Nine: Agonis 
> Basel's amenthia recordings may have carved out a niche with its leftfield, slow-burning techno, but label cofounder Agonis shows the vibes needn't be austere. Here, the Swiss DJ and producer delivers 66 minutes of colour and warmth for Kia's beloved Animalia series. Groovy, trippy selections are threaded with vocals and trance flourishes. It's a reminder that hypnotic techno can move with both depth and vibrancy, balancing ritual intensity with playful, body-driven momentum.

### ITPS119 LIMITED NETWORK 
> Max Watts is elusive. The Detroit-based artist once wiped his entire discography from the internet, which only made the buzz around him grow louder. Known for peak-time tracks and vinyl turntablism that recall legends like Claude Young, he's quietly become one of techno's most compelling underground voices. For the latest Ilian Tape Podcast, he dives into aquatic shades of techno and electro, teasing the upcoming release on his label, Limited Network.

### GQOM MIX TAPES E67 | AUGUST 2025 w/ MAMTHUG 
> "Archiving gqom, one mix at a time," reads the tagline for Oroko Radio resident Mamthug's GQOM MIX TAPES series. Emerging from Durban's townships in the early 2010s, gqom quickly became one of South Africa's most influential party genres, defined by heavy bass, stripped-back percussion and a brooding intensity. On this episode, Mamthugâ€”usually drawn to jazzy breakbeatsâ€”leans fully into gqom's vast spectrum, moving from sensual cuts to sub-rattling bangers, highlighting both the intimacy and force of a genre that remains as vital as ever.

### Transmissions 001: Sunju Hargun 
> Transmissions, the excellent London party spotlighting psychedelic club music, books hypnotic techno experimentalists such as DJ Nobu, Polygonia and Donato Dozzy. For those unable to attend the raves IRL, the crew has started a new mix series, launching with Bangkok-based DJ and label owner Sunju Hargun. A recording from FOLD's cosier second space, the Steam Room, the session opens with ceremonial chants. Vocals twirl around body-rattling bass and eerie synth lines, eventually giving way to two hours of Hargun's unique take on trippy techno.

### In Focus: DJ Medhi (mixed by Antonine Scali) 
> NTS Radio's latest In Focus celebrates DJ Mehdi, a hip-hop-kid-turned-house-DJ who defined a generation of Paris nightlife in the early 2000s. Raised on the outskirts of the French capital by Tunisian parents, he began producing mixtapes and beats inspired by J Dilla, before emerging as an unlikely icon of the Paris party scene. His radiant selections helped stitch together disparate worlds, from Daft Punk and Justice to MC Solaar. This hour-long mix captures that alchemy: rugged, sample-heavy productions for 113, Rohff and Mafia K'1 Fry sit alongside glossy, synth-driven anthems like "Pocket Piano," culminating in the euphoric climax of Thomas Bangalter's edit of "Signatune."

### StrÃ¸m Mixx 044 - Mbizo 
> Mbizo spins an hour of his own productions for StrÃ¸m Festival, Copenhagen's long-running celebration of electronic music and sound culture. While the Danish city has in recent years become known for high-BPM techno, Mbizo carves out a different path, grounding his set in old-school steppers, digi-dub and meaty dubstep (listen out for the cheeky JME edit). It's a refreshing counterpointâ€”and a seriously impressive showcase of Mbizo's studio skills.

### DJ Haram â€“ Beside Myself (Hyperdub)
> Beside Myself is a masterfully precise debut album that revels in its harshness: glowering verses, wailing strings, field recordings of a bustling New York (footsteps, incoming trains, old apartment buzzers) that crackle and simmer. The LP feels like a whirlwind night out, with influences running the gamut from Tennessee rap to Kim Gordon. It refuses to settle, sweeping listeners up into its galvanising clamour.

### Qur'an Shaheed â€“ Pulse (Leaving Records)
> Both building on and breaking down the refined neo soul of her 2020 EP, Process, Qur'an Shaheed's first full-length flourishes in the space between craftsmanship and creativity, bucking structure for improvisational freedom. Her blend of pitch-shifted, syncopated spoken-word, fluttering hums and lo-fi glitch FX evokes the boundless jazz fusions of artists like duendita and keiyaA. Shaheed's warm timbre is versatile enough to leap from the latter's trademark looped harmonies to Outkast-esque skits.

### Various (Tectonic) â€“ Tectonic Sound (Tectonic Recordings)
> Tectonic's latest compilation represents a compelling snapshot of where dubstep and dubstep-adjacent music stand right now. There's shuffly, soulful broken beat (2562's "Overcome"), weighty half-step skankers (J.Sparrow's "Genesys") and bassy techno tools (Pinch & Neffa-T's "This Is This Isn't"). Listening to Tectonic Sound from start to finish feels like microdosing the label's entire back catalogue.

### Hieroglyphic Being â€“ The Sound Of Something Ending (Mathematic Recordings)
> In Jamal Moss's expression as Hieroglyphic Being, there are no bum notes or wrong ideas. On The Sound Of Something Ending, gritty blips and elysian arpeggios constitute the album's beating heart. Through both analogue and digital manipulation, he uses a staggering array of synth textures to convey everything from shivering anxiety to spiritual ecstasy.

### Slikback â€“ Attrition (Planet Mu)
> Attrition, Slikback's first album on Planet Mu, explores themes of transition and reflection. Written during a relocation to Poland and the expectant arrival of the musician's first child, it's his most mature and realised work to date. The drums strike first. Violent and chaotic, his mutant programming often feels like he's flipping through a rolodex of trap and hard dance sub-genres at an accelerating pace. And yet, the LP's softer moments are among its most compelling.

### Stars of the Lid â€“ Music for Nitrous Oxide (Artificial Pinearch Manufacturing)
> Stars of the Lid's 1995 debut album is regarded as a classic within the ambient and drone world for a reason. The record is dense enough to wrap around and colour an environment, but never too imposing. This 30th-anniversary reissue highlights the pioneering drone duo's staying power. The smudged guitar flickers on "Down" gently speak to the current moment. In the era of Spotify's anodyne functionality playlists, the majesty of a slowly undulating drone piece like "Goodnight" feels like a brilliantly comical riposte to the idea of easy-listening music. But those subtle challenges have guided Stars of the Lid from the beginning.

### Madonna â€“ Veronica Electronica (Warner Records)
> It makes sense that Madonna is still exploring the world she created with 1998's Ray of Light. The rest of us are, too. This year alone has seen pop divas like FKA twigs and Addison Rae summon its spirit both reverentially and referentially. The LP's long-awaited remix album, Veronica Electronica, is pleasant nostalgia for the golden era of late-'90s dance music, a compact insight into who Madonna was listening to, inspired by and collaborating with when she wrote her magnum opus.

### rRoxymore â€“ Juggling Dualities (!K7 Records)
> Inspired by New Age music and the spacey, mind-expanding work of Carl Craig in the late '90s, rRoxymore imbues her latest album with driving hooks and gorgeous swathes of pads. From the glittering techno of "Moodified" to the alien chug of "Solace," this is an album that will guide you through trippy visions across all tempos.

### Two Shell â€“ IIcons (Young)
> On IIcons, anonymous trickster duo Two Shell find a happy medium between their newer hyperpop-influenced sound and the UK bass that defined their early career as producers on Livity Sound. The album (likely named in reference to their 2022 EP, Icons) swings from poles with an almost comical severity. "beeep" sounds straight out of the London underground, lurching forward with skippy drum programming and blustering sub-bass, while "w a k e u p" pulls from Eurodance, all chintzy synths and zooming melodies.

### Sugar Free â€“ Disociando (Icelab)
> Sugar Free's debut EP mirrors her provocative DJing style. Borrowing from prog house, electro-soldered techno and '80s sleaze, Disociando is one of the year's best club 12-inches. Its darkness is most palpable on the B-side. "Vale" starts with skippy, Perlon-style drum programming, only to morph into the claustrophobic techno that's become synonymous with the Montevideo scene. "Mentalizate" merges DJ Nobu's psychedelia with contemporary minimal. It feels weightless, as if you've entered a gravity-free chamber.

### Danny L Harle, PinkPantheress â€“ Starlight (XL Recordings)
> Danny L Harle's 2021 Harlecore LP was a post-pandemic work that fed off internet rave as much as happy hardcore and early '00s Eurodance. He brought it to life with alter ego MC Boing, whose high-pitched voice bore a striking resemblance to the CGI-animated Crazy Frog. He's since worked with real-life artists such as Caroline Polachek, Oklou and now PinkPantheress. Opening with ominous choral pads, "Starlight" makes use of PinkPantheress's saccharine, Auto-Tuned vocals, creating a misty atmosphere amid the relentless energy.

### FKA twigs â€“ Perfectly (Young)
> A Eusexua deluxe LP appears to be on the way. It doesn't take long to deduce that the pop auteur's new single, "Perfectly," is an alternate version of album cut "Perfect Stranger." The charging chords of the original are underpinned by a torrent of techno kick drums, turning the garage pop song into the kind of track that would fill a concrete dance floor at your favourite rave.

### Siavash Amini â€“ Caligo (Room 40)
> Anchored by spectral snippets of two of the earliest piano recordings in Iran's history, Caligo is a reconfiguring of a historical document that shifts between dark ambient and noise, burying deep into the brain. Water droplets flood piano plinks ("Spiraling P.M.") and the sound of tape unraveling hisses through clattering instruments ("Sanguis Stilla"). Moments of quiet are eventually uprooted, unveiling the chaos lurking underneath.

### Command D, Zara â€“ Gravity Reset (Butter Sessions)
> Command D makes dub techno with tight, pointillist drum programming that adds a distinct sharpness to his sludgy, sub bass-driven atmospheres. Zara makes tactile IDM with intricate sound design you can get lost in. Together, the two producers combine the heaviness of Command D's work with the squirming needlepoint embellishments of Zara's catalogue.

### tiro! â€“ Mountain Loop // Forest Loop EP (Self-Released)
> tiro! was gifted with a fascinating ear for loops. His music is bubbly and life-affirming, carrying the laid-back groove of second-generation Chicago house even though he's based on the other side of the world in Johannesburg. "Went on a hike and got inspired," he shares on the two-track EP's liner notes. The lush, repetitive churn of life experienced on those nature walks are all over this record, from the sunny synths on "Forest Loop" to the melody on "Mountain Loop," which flies between flangered chords and woody percussion.

### Patrick Holland â€“ In Memory (Verdicchio Music Publishing)
> Patrick Holland's recent records have been about slowing down; cruising house tracks that pack more melody than kick. This EP's opener, "Fast Forward," marks a noticeable shift in energy level, with a glitchy drum pattern and revved-up acidline. "Classless Act" tempers the A-side's peak-time palette, grooving to a restful pace with dubby pads and chirpy house drums.

### Pangaea â€“ ManÃ­a / Neuromance (Hessle Audio)
> Is there a vocal Pangaea can't work with? The Hessle Audio cofounder makes dance floor destroyers with undeniable roots in UK bass, and "ManÃ­a" is another banger on the docket, making use of Jazz Alonzo's seductive Spanish vocals over high-octane grooves. "Neuromance," pitched at 155 PM, features a storming synth pop melody that's enough to excite even the moodiest clubber. The cherry on top? Chipmunk vocals.

### Jubilee â€“ FreaQE (Magic City)
> On FreaQE, Jubilee plays a game: how many genres can you fit into a three-track EP? "Ford Focus" merges Miami bass's 808s, the slithery synth lines of UK bass and East Coast club amen breaks. The title track bounces with the fervour of Jersey club, while acid house synths and dubstep subs create a ferocious energy. And "FreaQE (NIGELTHREETIMES' HORNY OPERATOR REMIX)" is the drum & bass edit DJs will want to keep in their back pocket.

### 8 Deck Technical Mix 
> Neffa-T's 8 Deck Technical Mix is a stunning showcase of the continued potential of mixing records. Never one to rest on his laurels, the CDJ wizard's latest filmed session is 80 minutes of jaw-dropping skill. More than just a numbers stunt, his use of eight decks and two mixers allows for razor-sharp cuts and the spontaneous recomposition of tracks in real time, blurring the line between DJing and live performance. Almost constantly moving, it's as transfixing to watch as it is to listen to. Much like Jeff Mills' seminal Exhibitionist series, this is a vulnerable, high-wire act of solo mastery that will be talked about for years. Just remember the popcorn.

### Heaven is in You 
> ADAB is one of the US's best (and most underappreciated) DJs. On the latest instalment of their NTS Radio residency, the Philadelphia-based artist explores some of their favourite contemporary amapiano cuts from the likes of Thebelebe, Lowbass Djy, Jazza MusiQ and Bukzin Keyz. ### Hessle Audio - 30 June 2025 
> "It's experimental music that people have to move to." So said Ben UFO back in 2016 when reflecting on A Made Up Sound's unique appeal. For a decade, the musician's catalogue was home to a wild alchemy of soundsâ€”take "Afterhours," a lurching, 12-minute hybrid of dubstep and Detroit technoâ€”that inspired total awe in his contemporaries. Though the Dutch producer has kept a low profile in recent years, his latest project, ex_libris, proves that his guiding ethos of innovation has only deepened. His two-hour Hessle Audio takeover, which explores a range of personal favourites and early influences (Mary J. Blige, Krust), is a markedly intimate offering from an artist who's long thrived on bending boundaries in every direction.

### NTS Iran Special

### The Lot Radio 06-27-2025 
> Last month, after travelling stateside on a ship, Nono Gigsta made a stunning debut at Dripping. Afterwards, she headed to The Lot Radio to prove why she's got the widest range in the game. ### Good Work â€“ 12 July 2025 
> Loidis has an uncanny ear for deep tech house gems, the kind with slippery grooves, punchy synths and foggy dub rhythms. ### Timeless Series #52 
> This ambient and downtempo session is a mental massage for knotty thoughts. Ethereal pads, lush soundscapes and nature noises (frog ribbits, the plink of water droplets) seem to capture a time-lapse of a tropical ecosystem. Over the rhythmic chug of distorted synth lines, hissing melodies and barely there vocal samples, Moopie soundtracks a rainforest in transition, taking listeners across the seasons. It's an hour of pure, contemplative blissâ€”and a critical ear cleanse.

### Truancy Volume 353 
> In the hands of james K, music becomes emotional architecture. Layering melancholy, surrender and longing alongside murkier feelings such as anxiety, the New York-based artist builds sets like an urban planner of the heart. This 74-minute trek across mediative downtempo, drum & bass and sample-based experimentalism finds through lines between artists on the opposite sides of the dance music spectrum, from the delicate piano notes of Tristan Arp to Marco Shuttle's quiet percussion. It ends on a bittersweet note with the IDM pop of Cybermission's "Deep Hard," which james K described as her "current favourite feeling" because "it's fun, beautiful and real."

### Black Sites â€“ R4 (Tresor)
> On R4, Helena Hauff and F#X recapture their legendary live-wire energy for the breeziest club record in Hauff's discography, and the danciest in F#X's. The albumâ€”the duo's first release in 11 yearsâ€”provides plenty of opportunities for them to break out, like the crushingly heavy electro of "II," with its Nine Inch Nails-style distorted kick drums and curdled synths. "707," all jagged edges and jutting angles, sounds like they tried to make the ugliest acid track possible.

### Introspekt â€“ Moving the Center (Tempa)
> For her debut album on the storied dubstep label Tempa, Introspekt commits to actualising dubstep's sensual potential by incorporating elements of house, Detroit techno, UK garage and East Coast club. Her convergence of influences, from soulful shuffle to garage-grime, evokes Big Apple Records and early FWD>> parties, but without becoming bogged down in bland revivalism. Just listen to the thick, rolling riffs of wobble bass on "Make Me Dance" and "Respect," which channel the broodiness of Plastician's early tunes.

### Lyra Pramuk â€“ Hymnal (7K!)
> While working on her third album, Hymnal, Lyra Pramuk was moved by the beauty of the nature that surrounded her. Collaborating with a string quartet for the first time, she included flute, double bass and raw, improvised vocal harmonies that contrast with sleek electronic production. The resulting LP is multitudinal: tactile and knotty yet fluid and trance-like, offering all the forward-looking potential of electronic music while also drawing from generations of folk traditions.

### Nadah El Shazly â€“ Laini Tani (One Little Independent)
> Spanning past and present with a singular unearthliness, Nadah El Shazly's filmic scope on Laini Tani reveals the intense curation of an auteur. The album opens with a deceptively dream-pop bent before blossoming into a genre-spanning ride of industrial, classical and trip-hop. Her lyrics come alive with the hustle and bustle of Cairo (her hometown), her interiority and the interplay between the two.

### DJ Bone â€“ DJ Bone XXXV: The End of Never (FURTHER)
> In late May, DJ Bone decided to put out a whopping six releases to celebrate his accomplishments: five years of his FURTHER label, 30 years of his Subject Detroit label, 35 years in the music industry and, most importantly, his 55th birthday. The End of Never, the first of the six, offers more energy than his previous LPs, crackling with the futurism and thrust of the best Detroit techno. Take "Critical," which consists of little more than drums, a squelchy, two-chord Juno stab and hip-hop-coded vocals. It feels like mainlining a double espresso.

### Polygonia â€“ Dream Horizons (Dekmantel)
> Polygonia's latest unfolds like the sci-fi film Annihilation, where the DNA of living organisms is refracted and reconstituted into forms that are mutated and haunting yet somehow still gorgeous. Her soft-focus atmospheres offer moments of introspection, while earthly textures become anchors as she observes her ephemeral worlds. In these dreamscapes, highlights like "Gate To Amygdala" and "Hidden Blue" reveal just how intricate the Munich-based act's sonic craftsmanship is.

### Purelink â€“ Faith (Peak Oil)
> Purelink's new album of glitch and ambient techno rewards listeners willing to sit with quiet. Over time, the record slowly reveals intricate networks of sound amid an unwavering blanket of echo and barely-there feedback. The group also fold vocals from selected vocalistsâ€”Loraine James and poet Angelina Nonajâ€”into the mix. Opening track "Looked Me Right In The Eye" conjures a soporific sense of nightfall. On "Circle Of Dust," it almost sounds like the trio is volleying a ball between them, a technique more befitting a jam band than an electronic group.

### Nick LeÃ³n â€“ A Tropical Entropy (TraTraTrax)
> When Joan Didion set her sights on Miami during its mid-'80s heyday, she looked past the pastel-hued condos to find a new form of hybridised decayâ€”attempts to mask state-sanctioned corruption behind the veneer of a tropical paradise. It's an unexpected yet totally apt point of reference for Nick LeÃ³n, a proud ambassador of Miami's dance music scene. But A Tropical Entropy is far from a dour outing. "Ocean Apart," for instance, almost becomes a full-blown EDM rager, but backs away before the catharsis of a major drop.

### naemi â€“ Breathless, Shorn (28912)

### Facta â€“ GULP (Wisdom Teeth)

### Isabella Lovestory â€“ Vanity (Giant Music)

### Simo Cell â€“ FL Louis (TEMET Music)

### Lauren Duffus â€“ Can's Gone Warm (Select Few)

### bastiengoat â€“ Liquor Store Lime (Self-released)

### Surusinghe â€“ i can't remember the name of this, but that's ok (dh2)

### The Wednesday Alternative Mix 
> Look for an apt description of FFAN's style, and "adult-oriented disco" might fit best. Across the hour-long mix, the Seoul-based DJ maintains a medium tempo, blending dark, flamboyant elementsâ€”from gothic synths and vocals to acid flourishes and suspense-filled drum arrangements.

### GYSTMIX-030

### Everything reminds me of dubstep pt. III - curated by livwutang

### Rio 015 - Adi (recorded live at Bonanza 2025) 
> Set in the lush surroundings of Buritaca, Colombia, Bonanza Festival has quietly become a key meeting point for Latin America's electronic community. Adi, born in BogotÃ¡ and now based in Brussels, has built a steady following for her blends of trippy house, electro and techno, tinged with acid. Taking over from Nicolas Lutz at 7:30 AM, she kept up the momentum with nimble rhythms and just the right amount of sleaze, squelch and restraint.

### IT.podcast.s14e04: BMG at No Way Back 2025 
> If Detroit's Movement Festival is a pilgrimage, then No Way Back is its sacred ritual. The annual Tangent Gallery gathering is special for everyone involved, chiefly the DJs, who always go the extra mile. Motor City legend BMG is no exception. This year, he debuted fresh hardware remasters and exclusive edits of Pink Floyd, 808 State and Aphex Twin, alongside forthcoming releases on Interdimensional Transmissions. As he said himself: "We start at the Tangent and end up travelling to the other side of the universe."

### Erika de Casier â€“ Lifetime (Independent Jeep Music)
> The alt-R&B artist's fourth album crystallises her tastemaking without ever sacrificing style for substance. ### Kara-Lis Coverdale â€“ From Where You Came (Smalltown Supersound)
> Kara-Lis Coverdale's first album in eight years draws heavily from programmatic music, a classical style that gained traction in the Baroque period. Each song shares dozens of small stories, filled with enough peaks and troughs to fill out a beat sheet for the next season of The White Lotus.

### PinkPantheress â€“ Fancy That (Warner Records)
> Fancy That is a cheeky romp through UK dance pop history, sipping from everything on the Y2K singles chartsâ€”from the digital glut of Spiceworld to the trance vortexes of Frankfurt producer Spicelab. Colours get dialled up to maximum saturation as PinkPantheress splashes into full-hearted, unguarded pop for the first time.

### Model/Actriz â€“ Pirouette (True Panther Sounds)
> Casting aside their previously hard-edged bravado, New York band Model/Actriz embrace vulnerability with confidence and a newfound lightness on Pirouette. They've dubbed it a dance pop album, manually aping drum machines and introducing earworm hooks. The LP still has the band's no wave dissonance and twisted bacchanalian throb, but some seriously operatic vocal moments demonstrate a real willingness to take the armour off.

### Surgeon â€“ Shell~Wave (Tresor)
> What does techno mean to a 30-year-plus stalwart of the sound? For Surgeon, it's a spiritual collaboration between humans and technology, past and future. Shell~Wave bottles his personal experiences with his machines and delivers it to listeners with the improvisation of a free jazz musician.

### Various â€“ Road Fever: New Generation Carnival Riddims From St. Lucia And Dominica (Soundway Records)

### Shanti Celeste â€“ Romance (Method 808)
> "Can we get closer?" So asks Shanti Celeste over a shimmery bassline on "Unwind." On her second album, the British-Chilean producer puts her vocals front and centre for the first time, fusing garage, R&B and her signature house with a disarming sense of intimacy, both on and off the dance floor.

### OSSX â€“ WORLD KEEPS TURNING (Self-released)
> Prolific New Jersey trio OSSX are keenly attuned to the needs of the dance floor. ### Smerz â€“ Big city life (ESCHO)

### J. Albert â€“ Return To Sender (Self-Released)

### Ron Trent â€“ Lift Off (Rush Hour Music)

### Anthony Naples â€“ Scanners (ANS Recordings)

### Colombian Drone Mafia, Gibrana Cervantes â€“ Memoria (Ambieâ€”TÃ³n)

### Stereolab â€“ Instant Holograms On Metal Film (Warp Records)

### Thom Yorke, Mark Pritchard â€“ Tall Tales (Warp Records)

### Tracey â€“ Tracey (AD 93)

### Verraco â€“ Basic Maneuvers (XL Recordings)

### GIDEÃ–N, Rush Davis â€“ The Two Houses EP (HOMO-CENTRIC RECORDS)

### SHERELLE â€“ WITH A VENGEANCE (Method 808)

### Skrillex â€“ F*CK U SKRILLEX YOU THINK UR ANDY WARHOL BUT UR NOT!!<3 (Atlantic)
> Surprise-released on April Fools' Day, Skrillex's chaotic, tongue-in-cheek fourth album plays like a seamless, drop-heavy mix rather than a traditional LP. Returning to his early-'10s brostep roots, Skrillex includes the roaring drops and dopamine hits that defined the eraâ€”but this time he corrects history, including dubstep veterans like Majestic and Joker.

### Jane Remover â€“ Revengeseekerz (deadAir)
> On Revengeseekerz, Jane Remover's surprise third record, they race through their earliest, long-abandoned digicore work with newfound dexterity. Noise columns meet otherworldly, loosely stacked guitar notes. Standout "Professional Vengeance" could've been a Pixies song in another life, if the group played so hard and fast that the studio imploded. At their best, these songs join traditional emo with overblown electronics so seamlessly that you forget the American musician once debated choosing between the two.

### Barker â€“ Stochastic Drift (Smalltown Supersound)
> On the excellent follow-up to his debut album, Utility, Barker adds acoustic warmth to his well-worn arpeggios. The LP flits between the icy, mathematical precision of a Y2K-era IDM album and woody live instrumentation. A true thing of beauty.

### Nazar â€“ Demilitarize (Hyperdub)
> War is a central theme of Nazar's work. The lasers that blast through the redlining sub-bass of "Warning Shots," off his debut EP Enclave, were an early taste of what the Amsterdam-based producer would later call "rough kuduro." His delicate and sometimes downtrodden Dawuna-esque vocals are the most striking development of his second album, Demilitarize. Nazar's voice often steps lightly, casting glimmers of brilliance over the LP's murky kuduro waters.

### Red Pig Flower â€“ Practice Love (Sound Of Vast)
> Practice Love is the debut album from Red Pig Flower, the Korean-Japanese artist based between Berlin and London. Here, she touches nearly every inch of the global house scene. There's the New York musicality of "Sax and Drugs;" springy prog-house on "Thisiz House Music," reminiscent of the '00s Melbourne scene; and the effusive positivity of the title track, which channels the energy of Eris Drew's Motherbeat philosophy. Practice Love is best summed up by the unifying message of the closer: "No Genre, Only Music."

### Hieroglyphic Being â€“ Dance Music 4 Bad People (Smalltown Supersound)
> Chicago producer Hieroglyphic Being has been partying for a long time. "40 years later," he said about the club scene in Dance Music 4 Bad People's liner notes, "it's drastically differentâ€”everybody's angry!" His latest album is an attempt to change that. In the distorted, crunchy haze that typically defines his music, he brings out funky, wayward synth lines and drums. This is the kind of adventurous house that only Hieroglyphic Being can create, with each delightfully strange track centred around a perfect loop.

### Katarina Gryvul â€“ SPOMYN (Subtext)
> Fans of Arca and BjÃ¶rk will love Katarina Gryvul's third albumâ€”a haunting collection of choral pop bludgeoned with mechanical kicks and horror-style digital detritus. ### Ploy â€“ It's Later Than You Think (Dekmantel)
> London-based producer Ploy has consistently put out bassy, percussive dance music that many now think of as "UK techno." But on new album, It's Later Than You Think, he makes a hard left turn to take on the vast spectrum of house. There's the hardgroove-meets-house of "Admirer," and "Monsters," a throwback to the early-'90s drum work of DJ Pierre and Zip's '00s minimal. "Stringz" balances the old and new Ploy: mixing his new love of hard house with wormhole techno.

### Djrum â€“ Under The Tangled Silence (Houndstooth)
> Djrum's last album, Portrait With Firewood, weaved sombre acoustic instruments into spacious ambient and IDM. "Out Of Dust" contains even more surprises, a shapeshifting patchwork of vocal snippets, drums and piano notes.

### Avi Loud, Liano â€“ BAPE TAPE (Heck World Radio)

### Various Artists â€“ Pattern Gardening (Wisdom Teeth)

### PinkPantheress â€“ Tonight (Warner Records)

### Hiroshi Yoshimura â€“ Flora (Temporal Drift)
> Hiroshi Yoshimura was a revered figure in kankyÅ ongaku, Japan's environmental music scene, known for creating artfully unobtrusive works like Surround and the seminal Music for Nine Post Cards. ### aya â€“ hexed! (Hyperdub)
> The cosmic darkness of aya's debut album, im hole, is best captured by its lead single, "Emley lights us moor." The song is terrifying, comprising macabre field recordings and uneasy synths that soundtrack a mind seemingly caught between psychosis and epiphany. Three years on, the most surprising aspect of aya's follow-up, hexed!, is just how deliberately it functions as a sequel: eerie spoken-word morphs into screams, while drums and lasers clatter together relentlessly. On hexed!, she draws from metalcore, IDM and hardstyle, ditching cloistered inwardness for a cathartic expulsion of energy.

### Unspecified Enemies â€“ Romance in the Age of Adaptive Feedback (Numbers.)
> Louis Digitalâ€”AKA Unspecified Enemiesâ€”has always looked ahead with a cynical eye. His scattered discography often references the late urban theorist Mike Davis, namechecking his interrogations of systems of power, explored in books like City of Quartz and Ecology of Fear. Louis Digital moulded the first Unspecified Enemies album from puzzle pieces of synths, samples and sequences made in the early '00s. Romance in the Age of Adaptive Feedback flips Davis's pessimism to transmit the hopeful mood of the new millennium.

### Logic1000 â€“ DJ-Kicks: Logic1000 (!K7)
> Logic1000's DJ-Kicks entry dips into a startlingly intimate headspace. Though decades separate the release dates of her selections, her transitions grow together with preternatural symbiosis. Entries from the actual '90sâ€”a quick excerpt from Dettinger's 1999 ambient pop touchstone Intershop, the intro to Wamdue Kids' 1996 deep house LP These Branching Momentsâ€”knit into contemporary Y2K throwbacks, like the smouldering trip-hop of a.s.o.'s "Somebody" and the ethereal downtempo of Moon Holiday's "Definitely."

### Sandwell District â€“ End Beginnings (The Point Of Departure)
> When Silent Servant died in 2024, the tragedy triggered an outpouring of sorrow from the artists, fans and friends he touched, both as a solo artist and part of techno collective Sandwell District. End Beginnings is a masterclass in devastatingly uncompromising techno, completed by surviving members Function and Regis. Their reverb-heavy loops have always been melancholic at their core, but here, they recede further into the darkness. It's a beautiful elegy.

### Yetsuby â€“ 4EVA (Pink Oyster Records)
> 4EVA is by far the most vibrant and dance floor-oriented of Yetsuby's solo records, finding common ground in the torrent of breaks and bass that build its rhythmic core.
