### Los Thuthanaka â€“ Los Thuthanaka (Self-Released)
> At long last, the follow-up to Joshua Chuquimia Crampton's Estrella por Estrella and Chuquimamani-Condori's DJ E is here. The experimental sibling duo have joined forces on their debut album as Los Thuthanaka. The LP makes excellent use of Joshua's emotional, drone-like bass guitar work, while Chiquimamani-Condori's blown-out collages of ronroco, teclas and bombo italaque make even the most granular moments swell with hope, wonder and spirituality.

### Time Cow â€“ Scaring 1100 Chickens To Death (Kullijhan Records)
> As a founding member of Jamaica's Equiknoxx crew, Time Cow has spent many years reinvigorating dub and dancehall for a modern generation. Recently, the producer has made a new home for his solo and collaborative work in Kullijhan Records. Scaring 1100 Chickens To Death, his debut album for the label, isn't as scary as its title suggests: clicky percussion dribbles through weighty low-end on "Guns Drugs and 800 Parrots" and synths squawk like screeching parrots on "Soca Numa."

### 8ULENTINA â€“ SURPASSING DISASTER (SILLAGE)
> 8ULENTINA's debut LP comes after more than a decade of helping steer the Bay Area and New York underground. SURPASSING DISASTER as informed by industrial and dark ambient as the artist's Turkish roots. Arab acoustic instrumentation is threaded into haunting corridors of crushed bass and blistering kicks. The cursive whispers of a ney meld into cinematic synths on "Devotional," while rich-toned hand drums and cymbals punctuate the sinister synthline on "Desire Ruse." A spellbinding work.

### DJ Narciso â€“ Diferenciado (PrÃ­ncipe)
> PrÃ­ncipe showcases another impressive configuration of Lisbon's thriving batida scene with DJ Narciso's debut LP. The producer, who's also the brain behind the collective Rs ProduÃ§Ãµes, carves out a sound that carries a lilting danceability (perfectly demonstrated on "Pipipi" or "5 Do Jo") while "Underground dos Loucos" and "30 Paus" champion the more choppy, experimental edges of club music.

### Various Artists â€“ SueÃ±os en la Tormenta (Headroom Records)
> BogotÃ¡-born producer CRRDR has been one of the loudest supporters of post-pandemic Latin-made club musicâ€”a movement he playfully dubbed "Latincore." This compilation he curated highlights an exhilarating blend of UK hardcore and rhythmic club sounds that fold in elements of raptor house, speed dembow and cumbia. This is music to make the floor shakeâ€”from the lightning-fast baile funk of LAZA's "PerturbaÃ§Ã£o" to the steamy guaracha of Noro$t's "DÃ©jela Sonar."

### Whatever The Weather â€“ Whatever The Weather II (Ghostly International)
> Loraine James's fragmented music puts a heartfelt bent on glitchy IDM, gilded atmospherics and hushed, intimate vocals. But when she debuted her Whatever The Weather alias in 2022, she leaned further into her long-standing guitar and ambient influences, such as on the frigid, delicate chords of "0Â°C" and the skipping, airy pads of "30Â°C." Her second album under this name evokes images of arid terrain and sun-dappled dirt, with productions that shine with golden hues.

### DJ Python â€“ i was put on this earth (XL Recordings)
> DJ Python's Luis alias has long been a vessel for his '90s chillout stylings, and has increasingly bled into other areas of his discography. 2023's Natural Wonder Beauty Concept project with Ana Roxanne, for example, showcased less of the "deep reggaeton" he made his name with, instead presenting a gorgeous world of detuned keys, breakbeats and melodic IDM. Python's latest solo EP, i was put on this earth, feels like a natural progression, making elegant use of bleeps, burling guitar and the low-key vocals of Isabella Lovestory and Jawnino. A meditative beauty.

### SoFTT â€“ HaRDD (PAN)
> Rising Miami duo SoFTT make trance that conjures images of air-brushed crop tops and sweaty pool parties. On HaRDD, vocalist Kablito's sugary tone coats driving synthlines, but she completes her pop star arc with hooky songs like "Cera El Cielo." On the more vulnerable "Linda, Triste, Una Pop Star," she ponders traditional family life in Spanish, before she remembers with a laugh, "my boyfriend and I, we're DJs."

### Actress â€“ Grey Interiors (Smalltown Supersound)
> Actress originally made Grey Interiors for Berliner Festspiele. The piece, recorded as a continuous 20-minute track, is now available to the wider public. Grey Interiors slips in and out of immersive white noise, occasionally opening up little pathways of clear-eyed melodies. Surreal piano and chimes break through, then dissolve into the darkness once again. It's the soundtrack for a scene in constant motion.

### Maara â€“ Big Whoops (Ancient Records)
> As a sapphic experience, Big Whoops is an EP that exists in the slinky continuum between cuddly slumber parties and late-night raves. Undecipherable whispers flower in the cracks of proggy rhythms; gasps of delight echo through the mix. As proven time and again with Maara's work, it's the little details that make for the grandest displays of seduction.

### MoMA Ready â€“ MR001 (Self-released)
> The agenda of MoMA Ready's first record of 2025? Gritty, romantic house. The New York producer leaves behind samples to put his own words front and centre, bringing earnest poetry to songs like "Suddenly," where love begets feelings of self-acceptance ("I feel like I belong / And there's nothing wrong"). The emotional tone of the EPâ€”and the ecstasy it chases afterâ€”is no less driving than his peak-time anthems. On "Feel Like That," over a nasty bassline that slithers close to the floor, he asks, "How do you feel?"

### 1OO1O â€“ BREAKBEAT BOUTIQUE (DistroKid)
> Mexico-based producer 1OO1O makes hardgroove inspired by the Latin rhythms around him. BREAKBEAT BOUTIQUE pays tribute to his US influencesâ€”tracks like "Jupiter Jazz" (sharing a name with the song by '90s Detroit techno group Galaxy 2 Galaxy) pay tribute to techno's origins while adding a playful touch of disco and funk. "Derby City Classic" pushes the envelope further, creatively connecting the dots between hoover, hardgroove and garage.

### Jlin â€“ B12 (Jlin Metalabel)
> Sydney's Powerhouse Museum is home to half a million objects. Its new initiative, Sounding the Collection, allows musicians to access this archive and use samples recorded at the museum to create their own original musical responses. On B12, Jlin makes use of a talking robot, an Irish harp and a wire-tying machine, with hazy melodies grounding the rhythmic chaos. This might just be the closest thing to hip-hop she's worked on in recent years.

### Pixl & Peeb â€“ Old Citrus (Future Retro London)
> Tim Reaper's Future Retro label is a place for the jungle producer to release the work of peers he deeply respects. Projects are formed out of conversations about music, or in Pixl & Peeb's case, music that Reaper plays on his NTS Radio shows. After a year of being sent Pixl & Peeb's music, Reaper decided to release Old Citrus, a collection of soulful jungle with harmonies shrouded in R&B melodies.

### Jorg Kuning â€“ Elvers Pass (Wisdom Teeth)
> Welshpool-based producer Jorg Kuning puts house, bass, techno and electro through the blender. His latest EP for Wisdom Teeth is replete with burbling, groovy tracks that sound delightfully froggy. The synths are bright and flashy, but the slippery beats and thumping subs deepen the mood and bring listeners closer to the dance floor. A real treat.

### The Dubstep-Tech House Connection (Beatrice M. & Appleblim)
> The Paris-based BAIT label boss Beatrice M. has emerged as a key figure in reshaping dubstep in the 2020s, picking up where pioneers like Peverelist and Pinch left off. Their fascination with "techy" dubstep and the history of crossover sounds, dating back to the early 2000s, informs this NTS Radio broadcast, which is part mix, part talk show. Beatrice M. blends tracks with insights from Appleblim, and discusses the genre's evolution from dubstep's deeper, soulful roots to its influence on minimal and tech house.

### 8ËšC (Richard Akingbehin)
> Unless you've been living under a rock, you've likely heard whispers that dub techno is back. Richard Akingbehin, the expert in our recent history of vocal dub techno, dives deep into the genre with a 90-minute mix that immerses you in its signature reverb and hypnotic depth. The Kynant Records boss puts it best in the accompanying interview: "One of my most used words to describe the feeling of a track is 'underwater.'"

### The OONTS Show (Kojay & P-Lucas)
> Rinse FM residents Kojay and P-Lucas continue their stellar run on The OONTS Show, rolling out an hour of blissful and bumping house. Keep an ear out for Jovonn's deep house masterpiece "Little Drummer Boy," straight from the vinyl collection of Kojay's father.

### BFC ADE 2024: RADION Saturday (Marcel Dettmann & OgazÃ³n)
> Last October, two generations of techno collided as OgazÃ³n and Marcel Dettmann went head-to-head for four electrifying hours at Breakfast Club's ADE takeover of RADION. The real star of the show was the crowd, who lapped up the world-class house and groove-driven techno. As OgazÃ³n reflected, the duo were so deeply connected to the audience that it felt like "a homecomingâ€”warm, familiar and charged with energy." of the audience that it felt like "a homecomingâ€”warm, familiar and charged with energy."

### Baalti - NTS (Baalti)
> Just before releasing their outstanding new EP Mela last month, New York duo Baalti went deep on India's sound system music for NTS Radio. A bespoke blend of Indian and UK club music, it's a hi-octane hour of unreleased originals and hard drum highlights that are as loud as they are proud. (Full disclaimer: OK, we know this dropped in February, but it was too good to leave out.)

### Live At Podlasie Chicago (Lefto Early Bird & Marco Weibel)
> Brussels-based DJ Lefto Early Bird and New York's Marco Weibel played a rowdy back-to-back at Podlasie Club in Chicago earlier this month, delivering just over an hour of peak-time madness. They kept each other on their toes, stitching together grime, disco, subby techno and heart-warming deep house.

### Live @ The Spookathon (DJ Sweet6teen)
> It's hard to believe that DJ sweet6teen only started collecting records during the pandemic. Just take one listen to this 98-minute recording from spooky season's unofficial mascots, The Ghost Halloween, and you'll see what we mean. Designed to feel like "someone breaking into your house," it's wicked stuffâ€”a haunted house soundtrack, but in Ibiza. Sleek deep house and rolling tech-y grooves give way to punchy, spine-tingling electro, keeping things tense yet effortlessly cool.

### Carnaval Novo Affair âœ¿ SÃ£o Paulo (Kontronatura & Nick LeÃ³n)
> Kontronatura, resident at SÃ£o Paulo's Mamba Negra party, went back-to-back with Nick LeÃ³n to close out Novo Affair's Carnival celebration with a tour de force of contemporary club music. They built the vibe with patience, moving from murky, percussive cutsâ€”66's "Alarma (Sylvere Bouyon Edit)" and DJ Fucci & Jensen Interceptor's "Manita de Gato"â€”into a string of sharp, driving selections, from storming electro (Identified Patient's "My Way [Hilton Mix]") and pop-infused club (LSDXOXO's remix of Kelela "Soft") to Baltimore club (Ase Manual's "Senzu").

### Marie Davidson â€“ City of Clowns (Deewee)
> In 2022, Marie Davidson became obsessed with Shoshana Zuboff's groundbreaking book, The Age of Surveillance Capitalism. So much so that Zuboff's alarming arguments about human exploitation informed the mechanical breaks and electro arpeggios of the Canadian artist's sixth LP. Nevertheless, Davidson's furiously winking humour remains the star of the showâ€”just listen to tracks like "Sexy Clown" and "Push Me Fuckhead."

### Traxman â€“ Da Mind Of Traxman Vol.3 (Planet Mu)
> Chicago legend Traxman has seen his city's dance music scene through numerous iterationsâ€”from funky proto-house to ghetto house to footwork. Since 2012, the ever-prolific producer has been archiving his discography in the Da Mind Of Traxman series. After a ten-year hiatus, he returns with a collection that highlights his ghetto house past as much as his footwork present.

### Oklou â€“ choke enough (True Panther Records)
> Oklou's debut album lures her away from the Stockholm syndrome of the internet. choke enough sees the Parisian singer venture outsideâ€”in a world so beautiful, a mid-drive sighting of the moon is distracting enough to make her crash her Subaru. Here, baroque pop and melodic trance beautifully coalesce to bring her frolics to life.

### BOOF â€“ Night Blooming Cereus (BubbleTease Communications)
> Every five or so years, fans can expect a new album from Maurice Fulton's joyous, flower-themed alias, BOOF. His latest is an upbeat delight, moving through jazz, funk and house with the undeniable warmth of live instruments. But Night Blooming Cereus also weaves in darker, tunnelling techno moments that make you understand why this flower thrives at night.

### Darkside â€“ Nothing (Matador Records)
> DARKSIDE's long-awaited third album largely stems from a process that NicolÃ¡s Jaar, Dave Harrington and new member, drummer Tlacael Esparza, refer to as the "nothing jam." During these sessions, the trio practiced mindfulness and reflected on the contradictions of nothingness. The result? Warbling, guitar-fuelled songs that explore how nothing can mean everything in a crumbling world.

### Kelela â€“ In the Blue Light (Warp Records)
> In May 2024, one of Kelela's dreams came true. The alt-R&B artistâ€”who as a college student once drove from Washington D.C. to New York to visit Blue Noteâ€”finally made her debut at the historic jazz club. This live recording is a tender treat, offering acoustic reworks from Cut 4 Me, Take Me Apart and Raven.

### Various Artists â€“ Bay Area Renegade Trax Vol. 2 (NO BIAS)
> Bay Area-based label and event series NO BIAS thrives off cheeky, bombastic bangers. Featuring members Bored Lord, bastiengoat, Honey B and JEWELSSEA, the compilation effortlessly presents raucous breaks, electro, lo-fi house and pop edits. ### Ela Minus â€“ DÃA (Domino Recording)
> What will the apocalypse sound like? Colombian artist Ela Minus contemplates the answer on her new album DÃA, which fuses the raging energy of the club with shards of coruscating post-punk. It's a feeling best encapsulated by opener, "Broken," in which she purposefully croons: "I'll keep writing melodies / To sing away the gloom that we have succumbed to."

### Saffron Bloom â€“ Saffron Bloom (Delicate Records)
> Through his trip-hop alias, Saffron Bloom (AKA New York-based producer Sepehr) illustrates noirish, seductive scenes. Fans of Portishead and Tricky will revel in the looped murmurs of "Dirge Of The Lonely," while St. Germain lovers will enjoy the jazzy saxophone and dub techno spirit of "Times Up (It's Over)."

### Byron The Aquarius â€“ LOST VAULTS OF BYRON THE AQUARIUS VOL.1 (Self-Released)
> Byron The Aquarius is best known for jazzy house on Detroit labels like Theo Parrish's Sound Signature and Kyle Hall's Wild Oats. On LOST VAULTS, the Atlanta-based artist channels the soulful, gospel-influenced essence of '90s R&B. Guest appearances elevate the project to spectacularâ€”from TaMiyA's dreamy harmonies on "Music" to the mystical hopscotch of the FlyLo collaboration.

### Shygirl â€“ Club Shy Room 2 (Because Music)
> The second installment of the Club Shy series brilliantly highlights Shygirl's rap influencesâ€”just look at how comfortably she spits alongside Saweetie on the raunchy "Immaculate." This bawdy energy is only strengthened by her star cast of co-conspirators, including Isabella Lovestory, PinkPantheress and BAMBII. Inside Room 2, the club's never felt so hot.

### Baalti â€“ Mela (Steel City Dance Discs)
> Mela, a Hindi word for "festival," is any kind of banging party that brings together strangers, friends, neighbours, colleagues and distant relatives. On Steel City Dance Discs' latest EP, New York-based duo Jaiveer Singh and Mihir Chauhan create a mela of their own, fusing the rattling sounds of Indian sound system culture with an overseas style that's nearly as piercing: UK bass music.

### NadÄ«, Otus â€“ Freefall (all my thoughts)
> South London producers NadÄ« and Otus make music rooted in cultural exchange: weighty UK basslines and skittering breaks meet sinewy Bangladeshi vocals. On Freefall, this approach feels like second nature, seamlessly layering looped Bengali vocal samples over speed garage, dubstep, and on the gloriously chuggy title track, slippery ambient techno. Surefire DJ tools.

### Lucrecia Dalt â€“ cosa rara (World Music)
> Colombian experimental musician Lucrecia Dalt crafts nocturnal music indebted to the unsettling soundscapes of surrealist cinema. On her 2024 album, Â¡Ay!, she meditated on her heritage through sci-fi bolero. Her latest offering, "cosa rara," (which translates to weird thing) builds on this David Lynchian tension, with equally uncanny remixes from Mabe Fratti and Matias Aguayo.

### WOST â€“ Miniteca SelvÃ¡tica (TraTraTrax)
> TraTraTrax's first release of 2025 comes from rising Venezuelan producer WOST. His galvanising mix of low-end and vocal samplesâ€”invoking raptor house, baile funk and UK bassâ€”is primed for peak-time. On his debut EP, he strikes gold, inviting Ecuadorian artist EntraÃ±as and Hessle Audio's Pangea for a suite of rhythmic club trax. This is what the future of Latin electronic music sounds like.

### MUN SING â€“ Frolic (Illegal Data)
> MUN SING's music is typically built on a foundation of staticky synths and heaving low-end. Frolic takes these traits and fits them into a hyperpop mould, complete with all the rich songwriting the genre demandsâ€”from Katy Ketani's girlish voice soaring over Eurodance to ROOO's channeling of Mariah Carey, Hayley Williams and Grimes all at once. This is MUN SING's most devourable work yet.

### Prettybwoy â€“ Tokyo Ice Age (SVBKVLT)
> Prettybwoy makes club music that squirms and fidgets. Composed of bright melodies and shiny percussion, his music evokes the sound of cartoon characters tip-toeing into mischief. On his latest EP, he finds the sweet spot between the acoustic and the digital: wintry piano and strings melt into futuristic plinks and plonks, creating moments of perfect tension.

### Terror Danjah Tribute (Spooky)
> Grime lost a great innovator last month with the tragic passing of revered producer Rodney Pryce, AKA Terror Danjah. Spooky's latest dispatch compiles nearly two hours of classics and deep cuts by the late artistâ€”a heartfelt reminder of what made Pryce such a special and indispensable force in the London genre.

### Recorded at Houghton (2024) (Batu)
> Closing the Outburst stage at Houghton 2024, Batu delivered a masterclass in how to construct a set. The Timedance boss starts by moving through various shades of restraintâ€”think minimal and stripped-back tech house Ã¡ la Mark Henning's 2015 classic "Trojan"â€”before turning up the heat. Stay 'til the end for a final crescendo that the Bristol-based artist called "magical."

### Truancy Sessions (DJ Wiggles)
> Head of the label, mix and party series kinetic, DJ Wiggles is one of London's fastest-rising tastemakers. In her contribution to Truancy Sessionsâ€”Truants' new mix series for emerging artistsâ€”she flexes her muscles behind the decks. It's a spine-tingling affair, building up slowly from the skeletal rhythms of Azu Tiwaline and Beatrice Dillon to the ecstatic future-garage of Burial's "Truant." One for fans of Nono Gigsta or Shackleton.

### Cumulus 33 / Mixtape Discos Movimiento #28 (Cio D'or)
> Cio D'or honed her craft in the '90s at legendary Munich club Ultraschall before relocating to Cologne to fine-tune her deep, emotive take on minimal and dub techno. After temporary retirement due to ill health, she has reemerged in tandem with dub techno's renaissance via a 2024 Draaimolen slot and Kynant Records release. For Mexico City's Discos Movimiento, she moves fluidly through records old and new, from Basic Channel to RenÃ© LÃ¶we.

### FKA Twigs â€“ Eusexua (Young)
> FKA twigs shines with a quality we haven't really seen before on her third studio album, Eusexua. Anchoring her songwriting in the canon of '90s dance music, she draws from trip-hop, IDM, electro and living room techno, though the LP's best moments reference the darkness of the club. While the LP is a response to the liberating euphoria she has experienced on the dance floor, the music is no less cerebral than on revered full-lengths Magdalene and LP1. There's a gripping seriousness about her devotion to pleasure across the album, from the trip-hop poetry on "Girl Feels Good" to the operatic runs on "Striptease."

### Khadija Al Hanafi â€“ !OK! (Fada Records)
> It's undeniable that footwork, one of Chicago's proudest exports, has made its mark around the world, sweeping across the US, the UK, Japan and, more recently, Tunisia. Tunisian producer Khadija Al Hanafi's style is playful and light-footed, homing in on footwork's soulful elements with microbeats that have the glitchy nature of video game music.

### Voice Actor, Squu â€“ Lust (1) (Stroom)
> Off the back of Voice Actor's 2022 debut, Sent From My Telephone, word spread about the enigmatic duo in niche dance music circles. Now, they're back with a new offering featuring Welsh producer Squu. While previous albums centred abstract storytelling over satisfying loops, Lust (1) doubles down on repetition, reducing singer Noa Kurzweil's voice to rhythmic murmurs and ASMR-like sighs.

### Ethel Cain â€“ Perverts (Daughters of Cain)
> Reluctant popstar Ethel Cain has drawn comparisons to Lana Del Rey with her ruminations on shame and longing wrapped up in gloomy Americana. On Perverts, she excises her Southern charm, but shifts towards the power electronics of Puce Mary. Expect dark ambient, suffocating drone and guitars that sound like the Silent Hill alarm disintegrating.

### Africanoise â€“ CabaÃ§a (Self-Released)
> Africanoise, AKA Renato Junior, is a master of rhythm. His percussive instincts are informed by his study of candomblÃ© drumming, which gives his modular experiments a ritualistic tenor. Somewhere between jazz, candomblÃ© and techno, CABAÃ‡A combines these worlds so smoothly you're left wondering how they were separate in the first place.

### Blacksea NÃ£o Maya â€“ Despertar (Principe)
> PrÃ­ncipe affiliates Blacksea NÃ£o Maya have always favoured more sluggish, moodier sounds than their label peers. Low-down grooves for the body and mind.

### Radart â€“ Blips & Bleeps (Paper-Cuts)
> For nearly a decade, Naarm (Melbourne)-based label Paper-Cuts has specialised in low-slung house, downtempo and ambient techno, counting Kia, Roza Terenzi and CS + Kreme among its affiliates. ### Wata Igarashi â€“ Kaleidoscopic (Dekmantel UFO)

### naffcast003 (Priori, Cousin)
> Clocking in at over six hours, this marathon recording from Sustain-Release 2024 might take you a couple of sittings to get through in fullâ€”but it's massively worth it. ## [October's Best Music](https://ra.co/features/4397)
Date: 2024-11-08T12:30:52.000Z

### Fergus Jones - Ephemera (Numbers)
> NumbersFergus Jones - EphemeraFormerly known as Perko, Fergus Jones crafts some of the classiest '90s and early aughts downtempo and ambient you'll hear this fall.Listen:Bandcamp

### Moin - You Never End (AD 93)

### Midland - Fragments Of Us (Graded)

### Low End Activist - Municipal Dreams (Sneaker Social Club)
> Sneaker Social ClubLow End Activist - Municipal DreamsLow End Activist has dedicated much of his career to producing heads-down, semi-biographical bass music inspired by his childhood growing up in the Blackbird Leys estate in Oxford, UK. This time, his excellent patchwork of samples, contorted bass and dark ambient focus centres on a three-day Blackbird Leys riot in 1991.Listen:Bandcamp

### The Bug - Machine (Relapse Records)

### Dawn Richard & Spencer Zahn - Quiet in a World Full of Noise (Merge Records)

### Kelly Lee Owens - Dreamstate (Dh2)

### Dekmantel 10 (Steffi)

### Escenia 084 (Dj Popup)
> Dj PopupEscenia 084Since the mid-'10s, some of the best house music has consistently been coming out of Denmark, courtesy of the Regelbau crew in Aarhus.NES label head DJ Popup is continuing this legacy for the 2020s. ### A Far Blue (Sam Goku)
> Sam GokuA Far BlueSam Goku lays down an excellent 90 minutes for the latest mix in the Far Blue series. Balancing various textures without sacrificing depth and groove, it's one that's equally suited to home listening and the club."I recorded this mix right after I came back from my Asia tour," the Chinese-German artist wrote on SoundCloud. "Maybe it reflects the serenity I [felt] after returning from an inspiring trip-I felt very unrushed while recording it. What I also took home from this trip is a renewed fascination for textures of all kinds, which gave this mix its name. I hope you enjoy."

### Sparkling 02 (DJ Frog)
> DJ FrogSparkling 02Running parties and releasing music on Doo Records, DJ Frog is a local legend of the Montreal scene. It's not hard to see why: for the latest edition of Pascale Project's new mix series, Sparkling, she delivers a vinyl-only hour of crunchy minimal house and techno, closing out with the timeless "Planet Be (Hashman deejay remix)". One for any fan of Acting Press or PLO Man.

### SWOON | 18.10.2024 (Soria)
> SoriaSWOON | 18.10.2024An hour of sprawling, dubbed-out soundscapes on the latest Swoon podcast, courtesy of Dublin-via-Berlin DJ Soria.As noted in the description, the mix is inspired "by the main character from 'A Spy in the House of Love' by Anais Nin. Here the protagonist bathes at night in moonlight as one would in the sun, cultivating a power from its rays which pulls in and frightens the other characters around her. A reminder of the strength we have when we allow ourselves access to our own sensuality."

### Dub Delights XIII (Andy Martin & Sarcus Soundsystem)
> Andy Martin & Sarcus SoundsystemDub Delights XIIIGuadalajara-based favourite Andy Martin and the Parisian trio Sarcus Soundsystem take the reins of the dependably sick Dub Delights show on Rinse France. The result: two hours of dub-adjacent sounds, from Tikiman to Dubamine.

### The Bunker Podcast 233 (Mike Servito & Jeffrey Sifre)
> Mike Servito & Jeffrey SifreThe Bunker Podcast 233Of the many events across Movement weekend, Return to the Source makes for a consistent highlight. International Transmissions leads the event series encompassing parties like No Way Back and The Bunker, the latter of which hosted Mike Servito and Jeffrey Sfire earlier this year."Mike Servito always majestically closes out No Way Back, but what would this combination bring? Sfire brought the heat, and their styles melded in a slightly pitched-down form, music from all eras appeared," No Way Back cofounder BMG wrote of the duo's The Bunker mix on Instagram. "A magical closing set that naturally extended from two hours to five hours of pure heat from two DJs whose whole [lives are] this music and this cultureâ€”who could ask for more?"

## [August's Best Music](https://ra.co/features/4373)
Date: 2024-09-04T15:00:02.000Z

### Seefeel - Everything Squared (Warp)
> WarpSeefeel - Everything Squared The experimental band's first extended release in 13 years doesn't feel like a band trading on their reputationâ€”the initial impression is one of change. Everything Squared finds Mark Clifford zeroing in on his production process while Sarah Peacock's vocals continue to provide a crucial human quality to the band's reliably enigmatic sound. Listen: Bandcamp

### Tinashe - Quantum Baby (Nice Life records)
> Nice Life recordsTinashe - Quantum Baby Outside the brief flirtations on Quantum Baby's singlesâ€”including of course, the viral hit "Nasty"â€”Tinashe's seventh album is really about striving for authenticity. The 22-minute album leans toward the hazy, subdued end of her catalogue, while still delivering on the kind of smoky, sexy numbers that we'd expect from her. Listen: Apple

### Kampire - Kampire Presents: A Dancefloor in Ndola (Strut)
> StrutKampire - Kampire Presents: A Dancefloor in Ndola Kampire has helped champion envelope-pushing East and South African music from the '70s up to the present day. On her debut compilation, she steps into the role of curator proper. A Dancefloor in Ndola is a captivating exercise in crate-diggery, setting renowned heavyweights like Samba Mapangala and Tshala Muana next to unpolished gems with gritty production values, party-ready grooves and minimal Google footprints. Listen: Bandcamp

### Loidis - One Day (Incienso)
> InciensoLoidis - One Day Huerco S. brings back his Loidis alias on One Day, a stripped-back record that shows the producer falling back in love with the art of a simple loop. Across eight tracks, he writes deep, muted and wobbly rhythms filled with the sort of gorgeous dub techno melodicism you might hear on a Shinichi Atobe record. Listen: Bandcamp

### Chrystabell & David Lynch - Cellophane Memories (Sacred Bones)
> Sacred BonesChrystabell & David Lynch - Cellophane Memories Across Cellophane Memories's 37 minutes, the pair's longstanding creative chemistry takes a new and arresting shape. Stripped of burdensome song forms and almost entirely absent of beats or easy melodies, something genuinely mysterious emergesâ€”a mystery you'd be tempted to describe as "Lynchian" even without knowing who was behind it. Listen: Bandcamp

### Jon Hopkins - Ritual (Domino)
> DominoJon Hopkins - Ritual Jon Hopkins began his journey making "serious, emotional" music with 2021's hazy, beatless Music For Psychedelic Therapy. The follow-up to that album, Ritual, originated from music Hopkins wrote for an installation called Dreamachine, named after a 1959 invention heralded as "the first art object to be seen with eyes closed." The 41-minute composition expands into eight parts that unfurl like a guided meditation. Listen: Apple

### Laurie Anderson - Amelia (Nonesuch)
> Nonesuch Laurie Anderson - Amelia When Laurie Andersonâ€”who first conceived of Amelia as a stage performance 24 years agoâ€”was asked on BBC Radio 4 why Amelia Earhart's story appealed to her, the answer was simple: "She was a bad-girl pilotâ€”and I liked that." On the LP, Anderson follows the late pilot's final flight path. The album plays like an audio documentary, drawing directly from Earhart's writing and strapping us into the plane with Earhart with shaky, surround-sound instrumentation. Listen: Bandcamp

### Various - Time Passages 10 Years (Time Passages)
> Time PassagesVarious - Time Passages 10 Years A decade is a long time in dance music, but longevity looks good on the techno label Time Passages. On the anniversary compilation, Binh's label remains the high watermark for low-slung and sinister minimal electro and techno. Listen: SoundCloud

### Nectax - Body Talk (Play:Musik)
> Play:MusikNectax - Body Talk On the first release in 14 years on Play:Musik, Nectax brings the same shapeshifting energy of the label's early output. Across four slickly produced tracks, he connects elements of footwork, jungle, techno and hardcore on an impressively varied EP that vividly reimagines the sonic kinship between those genres. Listen: Bandcamp

### Danny Daze & Jonny From Space - Tumbadora EP (Craigie Knowles)
> Craigie KnowlesDanny Daze & Jonny From Space - Tumbadora EP On Tumbadora, Danny Daze and Jonny From Space reunite for an EP that swaps the introspection of their respective debut albums for three original cuts of sludgy, polyrhythmic electro and techno. It even includes a cameo from Miami's other wunderkind, Nick LeÃ³n. Listen: Bandcamp

### Ciel & CCL - Tilda's Goat Stare (NAFF)
> NAFFCiel & CCL - Tilda's Goat Stare On Tilda's Goat Stare, Ciel & CCL's debut collaboration's chaotic feminist streak found a fitting anchor in the 2002 sci-fi feminist film Teknolust. Much of the EP lands with a thwack, top-loaded with precisely the kind of dusty peak-time tracks you'd find in the duo's festival sets. Listen: Bandcamp

### Dubbel Dutch - Cosmic Tone Poems (Rare Earth Tones)
> Rare Earth TonesDubbel Dutch - Cosmic Tone Poems Over a decade since Dubbel Dutch's last solo release, one of the breakthrough stars of the post-dubstep bubble returns after literally going off the grid. Cosmic Tone Poems is built around the contrast between synth lines that float like champagne bubbles and basslines that plunge the tracks down to earth, updating the sort of genre promiscuity he championed in the '10s. Listen: Bandcamp

### gyrofield - These Heavens (XL Recordings)
> XL Recordingsgyrofield - These Heavens The producer makes their debut on XL with a dynamic EP inspired by a night out in Bristol. Over four tracks, they swerve from angular acidlines to delectable, sputtering drum & bass breaks. Listen: Bandcamp

### All Arthur Russell DJ set, live at The Barbican (JD Twitch)
> JD TwitchAll Arthur Russell DJ set, live at The Barbican Optimo's JD Twitch dives into Arthur Russell's vast catalogue for this live recording at London's Barbican Centre back in May, celebrating the late composer's extraordinary life.

### GROOVE Podcast 428 (Mattias El Mansouri)
> Mattias El MansouriGROOVE Podcast 428 For the 428th GROOVE Podcast, Stockholm-based DJ and producer Mattias El Mansouri delivers a stellar two-hour mix, traversing eclectic boogies from the likes of The Durutti Column and Barrington Levy to the deep minimal rhythms of Arkajo and Dorisburg.

### XLR8R Podcast 863 (Assyouti)
> AssyoutiXLR8R Podcast 863 The Berlin-based producer and DJ goes tear-out, spinning hard-as-nails choppage from the likes of Breakage, B-Key and Champa B. If you like your drum & bass dark and weighty, this one's for you.

### Rinse FM (Ploy)
> PloyRinse FM While he may have initially made his name releasing wonky bassbin tracks on the likes of Hessle Audio, Timedance and Hemlock, Ploy isn't one to be pinned down. On the July edition of his Rinse FM show, the Bristol-based DJ and producer demonstrates that he's equally comfortable (and excellent) at playing house.

### Freerotation 2024 : The House Of Crocodiles Part 2 (Live Recording) (Nono Gigsta)

### Kiosk Radio 11.08.2024 (DJ Maria)
> DJ MariaKiosk Radio 11.08.2024 With regular appearances at Berghain, Bassiani and VENT, DJ MARIA. is one of the best DJs to emerge out of Japan in recent years.Guesting on Kiosk Radio, the Tokyo-based artist delivers a masterclass in building atmosphere, perfectly balancing muscle with texture (including one particularly mind-bending transition in which it sounds like she mixes a field recording from a working kitchen into Ben Klock's "Wolf"). It's the kind of eye-opening session that makes you want to listen to all her other mixes right after.

### Live at Nowadays 7 April 2024 (Objekt)
> ObjektLive at Nowadays 7 April 2024 Objekt is one of the most dynamic artists in underground techno today, and this recordingâ€”from the equally influential New York club Nowadaysâ€”captures him on typically excellent form."I played on Sunday morning from 9 AM to 3 PM, between JASSS and Bearcat," he said, calling it "one of the most creatively fulfilling sets I can remember playingâ€“one of those sets where the audience, environment, atmosphere, tech setup, phase of the moon, whatever, all somehow lined up for a full six hours."

### Down The Rabbit Hole 2024 (Sarkawt Hamad)
> Sarkawt HamadDown The Rabbit Hole 2024 The versatile Amsterdam-based DJ covers a lot of ground in this two-hour live recording from Down The Rabbit Hole. You can hear her adventurous approach in full bloom, moving through starry-eyed house, hypnotic techno, squelchy acid and more from the likes of Peach, Polygonia and Zephyr.

> One of Copenhagen's rising stars delivers slamming rhythms and zapping synths made for peak-time sets. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Overlook Public Image UVB-76 
> A whip-smart fusion of techno and drum & bass that sits defiantly between both worlds. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Cromby Retribution Feel My Bicep 
> A track that further refines the Irish producer's raw but lush house sound, bolstered by remixes from Shanti Celeste and DeFeKT. Listen: Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Gerry Read Preventing Violence Against Ears Accidental Jar 
> Abstract, funky and touchingâ€”it's no surprise Matthew Herbert signed these tunes to his label. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Mor Elian Move Like Atoms Fever AM 
> Deceptively innovative techno from Mor Elian, who sneaks little surprises into even her most functional tracks. Listen: Bandcamp / Soundcloud

### Justin Cudmore Twisted Love / About To Burst Phonica White 
> Acid house firing on all cylinders from New York's purveyor of squelch. Listen: Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### VTSS Self Will Intrepid Skin 
> The BrutaÅ¼ affiliate's debut record mines the middle ground between EBM and acid. Listen: Soundcloud

### Bone Head Soft Power Arcola 
> Experimental club music with a pop sensibility, from a new project by one half of DVA Damas.

### Bonaventure Mentor Planet Mu 
> Bonaventure delivers tightly woven club tracks on her Planet Mu debut. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Joey Anderson & DJ Qu Neutrino Inimeg Recordings 
> Two masters of modern US house return with a cosmic EP to dazzle dance floors. Listen: Soundcloud

### Shelley Parker Red Cotton Hessle Audio 
> A new face appears on Hessle Audio with restless dance music that feels outrÃ© even for this label. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

## [The Best Releases of 2025](https://ra.co/features/4350)
