## [The Best Mixes of 2024](https://ra.co/features/4405)
Date: 2024-12-04T16:30:00.000Z

### **NONO GIGSTA** - The House of Crocodiles (Live at Freerotation)
> Halfway through Nono Gigsta's sequel to her 2018 Freerotation set, also named The House of Crocodiles, we get an indication of the strange title's origins. "The males' rippling flesh sends soundwaves through the waterâ€¦ humans can barely hear them, but the crocodiles can. Welcome to the House of Crocodiles," a sample narrates. And then, oh so naturally, it moves into a roaring electric guitar solo (Led Zeppelin's "Whole Lotta Love"). It's a bonkers move that can prompt you to completely rethink what DJing can be. It's also completely natural in the hands of the Belgian DJ.Jaw-dropping transitions dominate this two-hour recording, aptly described as "Big Blend Academy" by one commenter. Low-end frequencies anchor the mix as it darts through wild variations in mood and tempo. Dubwise experiments (LUXE's "Diamond Dub") morph into frenetic jazz techno (Gigi FM's "Gabriella"), sounding like DJ Sprinkles if she dabbled in UK bass. You can feel Gigsta's sense of freedom as she aqueously glides across loose and liquid rhythms.Freewheeling mixes of this sort often risk being overly headsy, but this is a very fun listen that spans BjÃ¶rk, Foster Sylvers and Victoria Monet. The inclusion of more "popular music" only adds to the overwhelming sense of feverish delight. There's only one reasonable response to a mix this audacious: "WTF." - Bella Aquilina

### **Chucheewa** - Sound Metaphors (Refuge Worldwide)
> Chucheewa, one-half of Bangkok duo Acid Sister, thrives in slow tempos where she can flex her storytelling skills. In this mix, she's the sonic embodiment of an off-duty femme fatale. Balearic downtempo, acid house, dubby disco and woozy krautrock criss-cross one another like whispery marble veins, transporting listeners to a sleek, '70s-style disco where our protagonist is getting her lounge on. There's a nonchalant swagger underlining every track, as if mirroring her breezy movements. The mood is loose-limbed but there's a high degree of intellect and intention behind each rhythm, just like a Bond girl's alluringly sharp demeanour. - Nyshka Chandran

### **JADALAREIGN** - Episode 65 (There Is No Planet Earth)
> For Black History Month, New York's JADALAREIGN explored the myriad shades of deep house through a futurist lens. Selections emphasise the radical spirit behind Black music-making, whether via icy, austere melodies or the psychedelic squelches of 303s. Cruising through under-the-radar classics (Felix Da Housecat's "Free Love") and curveballs (Sweater on Polo's "Computer Controlled Madness"), the Nowadays booker zones in on tunes with a spacey touch that often borders on kooky (just look at Marcus Mixx's twisted jack track "Salut The Noize With A Laugh"). This is a concise but essential glimpse into the innovative imaginations of Chicago and Detroit artists, past and present. - Nyshka Chandran

### **Mia Koden** - One Hour of IICON (FMB Mixtape 243)
> If you caught our Glastonbury recap from earlier this year, you'll already know that Mia Koden's opening set at the IICON stage was something special. A "blend of celestial, 2562-esque dubstep backdropped by a beautiful sunset," as one RA staffer put it. For FMB, the London-based artist condensed that two-and-a-half-hour set into this lean power-hour of soulful sub-pressure. Just listen to the way she moves from the soothing resplendence of Ella Fitzgerald to the dank 140 of Slimy, Delta and Obskure within the opening ten minutes. Anything's possible in Mia Koden's capable hands. - Tom Gledhill

### **Priori** - Dekmantel Podcast 459 
> 2024 was a career-defining year for Canadian DJ and producer Priori, whose entry into the vaunted Dekmantel series blooms with spiralling, psychedelia-dipped sound design. This 90-minute session bears more resemblance to a longform song than a tapestry of different ones, applying incredible attention to detail by collaging deep and squelchy textures that sit as much in the future as they do in the past. If a snapshot could be taken of the styles that reigned 2024's dance floors, it's this: an incredibly cohesive and soft-hued marriage of nimble breakbeats, techno and trance from an artist going from strength to strength. - Chloe Lula

### **Reptant** - Floresta (Live at Waking Life)
> The appeal of a festival lies in its promise of escape from the mundane, and there's perhaps no better soundtrack to this promise than Reptant. A key figure in the electro revival, the Melbourne producer is known for a sleek, omnivorous sound that blends elements of tech house, trance and techno. His powers shine in this live recording from Portugal's Waking Life festival, which brims with otherworldly ambience. One standout at the 22-minute mark sounds as if Mike Skinner and Plastikman made an electro record together. Reptant later called it his "most special" gig ever. Check the SoundCloud comments and you'll see the dancers agree. - Bella Aquilina

### **DJ Swisha** - The Lot Ã— Kiosk (Live at Horst)
> DJ SWISHA is currently operating at the peak of his powers. With a doctorate-level grasp of Black American dance music and UK breakbeat, he's a true mixologist with a PhD in tearing up the club. This recording proves it. Effortlessly weaving through East Coast club, ghetto house, jungle and footwork, there's an enviable ease to every blend. The feral crowd noise is the perfect cherry on topâ€”each transition is met with unrestrained whoops and cheers. Aspiring club DJs, take notes: this is a masterclass in how it's done. - Fahad Akinsanya

### **Toumba** - FACT mix 938 
> Full disclosure: this one actually landed in December 2023. But because it slipped through the cracks of year-end coverage, and the legendary mix series shut down weeks later, we decided to bend the rules. Plus, it's totally mesmerising, the kind of mix that triggers 1,000 wormholes andâ€”should you listen in a particularly fragile stateâ€”possibly floods of tears. This is bold, cinematic, heart-on-sleeve DJing. A long ambient first half features tracks from Ulla, Burial and Slikback before morphing into headbanging mode with shards of Verraco, Eartheater and Lil Wayne. Stick this on when you really want to feel something. - Carlos Hawthorn

### **DJ Travella** - Live at Draaimolen Festival 
> DJ Travella is the face of singeli's future. The Dar Es Salaam artist infuses techno and taarab into the famously hi-NRG genre, adding a touch of experimentalism and contemporary rave to its frenzied tempos. For many in attendance, this was a clear highlight of Draaimolen Festival and it's easy to understand why. His vibrant selections possess a sense of urgency, commanding movement through jolting synths and madcap effects. The crowd vibed so hard that Travella ended up dancing on top of the decksâ€”a perfect picture of singeli's joyful nature. - Nyshka Chandran

### **YAJAIRA LA BEYACA & GENOSIDRA** - Misantropical (Rinse France)
> Three things are guaranteed when these two subversive powerhouses link up: an onslaught of Latin-infused bass trax, coquettish flexes about diva behaviour and an involuntary desire to throw ass. Venezuelan rave doll Yajaira La Beyaca has been on a tear since 2021, but this hybrid live setâ€”one of her first in Europeâ€”alongside frequent collaborator Genosidra, demonstrates an artist fully stepping into her powers. Darting through apocalyptic perreo, guaracha and what some call Latincore, this session is a soundtrack for all your freaky pre-club rituals. When Genosidra slips into a speed dembow refix of JME's "If You Don't Know"? Proof that perfection does exist. - Rachel Grace Almeida

## [The Best Tracks of 2024](https://ra.co/features/4401)
Date: 2024-12-04T12:45:45.000Z

### **DJ Love** - Bomb Tech 49 (Eastern Margins)
> Like gqom and raptor house, budots is finally joining the modest list of regional dance music genres gaining global recognition. Originating in the Philippines in the early '00s, the street-pioneered sound combines trancey techno and house with fat bass, high-pitched synths and lots of air horns.Now, pioneer DJ Love is showing off a new mutation of the classic sound with "Bomb Tech 49." Fittingly called bomb-tek, this offshoot is more techno-driven and undeniably harder, darker and leaner. Whereas the traditional stylings tend to be chirpier and whimsical, blippy effects, this strain, full of springy basslines and looped drums, takes budots off the streets and into the club. - Nyshka Chandran

### **Nuovo Testamento** - In My Dreams (Powerhouse Mix) (Eskimo/N.E.W.S.)
> "In My Dreams (Powerhouse Mix)" is the early '90s Italo house classic that never was. Pairing sugary, Latin freestyle-inspired vocals with huge piano stabs Ã  la 4 For Money's "It's a Moment in Time," it's the kind of turn-of-the-decade anthem you'd expect to hear soundtracking grainy archival footage from CocoricÃ² or Quadrant Park.Except "In My Dreams" isn't from the '90sâ€”it's a new release from contemporary synth pop outfit Nuovo Testamento. Dismiss it as frivolous if you like, but doing so won't diminish the truth: this track is custom-made for massive, life-affirming rave moments. - Michael Lawson

### **Sam Goku** - Temple Arp (Dekmantel)
> Like many great techno tracks, "Temple Arp" is a marathon, not a sprint. Stretching out over seven minutes, this beatific roller hooks you in with a cosmic intro that builds tension like a thriller. Sam Goku's previous releases, such as 2021's Tanggu and 2021's East Dimensional Riddims, have demonstrated the Munich-based producer's eye for the finer details."Temple Arp" is the stunning zenith of this meticulous approach: softly padded kicks and constellations of otherworldly synths work seamlessly to lull you into a trance, plotting a dubby voyage of epic proportions that favours nuance over heft. - April Clare Welsh

### **Leonce** - Not Here For It (Morph Tracks)
> It's one thing to produce a dance track. It's quite another to permeate it with the sheer essence of the club, transporting listeners to the dankest dance floor they've ever been on. Atlanta-based producer Leonce's incandescent banger "Not Here For It" uses effervescent keyboard arpeggios and infectious diva vocal samples ("here, here for you") to convey bodily liberation on a visceral level.When the beat drops, you can almost feel the sweat bead on your brow, as Leonce flexes not only his production chops, but his keen understanding of what makes the most seasoned ravers go off. - Cameron Cook

### **TAAHLIAH & Elouiza** - Boys (untitled (recs))
> Nothing hits like a sexy a cappella lineâ€”and TAAHLIAH and singer Elouiza delivered on "Boys." Fans of TAAHLIAH's bolshy, playful DJ sets may have been surprised by the introspection of her debut LP, Gramarye, but TAAHLIAH still made room for "Boys," the glossy, seductive club cut she's been teasing since 2022.Elouiza's smouldering vocalâ€”"These boys, they all want me / They all want to get in me"â€”is adorned with a growling bassline, crashing kick drums and plasticky neon synths, resulting in a perfect balance of cheeky yet tough. If 2024 served us up a track for stomping around the city feeling hot, this is it. - Katie Thomas

### **1OO1O** - Del SalsÃ³dromo al Rave (self-released)
> What happens when you throw "Talento de TelevisiÃ³n" by salsa legend Willie ColÃ³n into a blender with Nightcrawlers' '90s house anthem "Push the Feeling On"? Possibly the most fun you can have on a dance floor.Mexican producer 1OO1O has been steadily ascending with his tropi-fusions of salsa and breaks, expertly folding the Caribbean genre's rhythmic principles into techno and bass musicâ€”all with a puckish wink. But "Del SalsÃ³dromo al Rave" takes this formula and intensifies the flavour. A base layer of Nightcrawlers' immediately recognisable synth line, a dash of ColÃ³n's warming trumpet ensemble, all bound by pummelling, hip-vitalising kicks at 150 BPM. Delicioso. - Rachel Grace Almeida

### **INVT & Introspekt** - Seismic Activity (ec2a)
> The global club music cross-pollination was in full flow long before Miami duo INVT and neo-garage innovator Introspekt decided to make music together, but the resulting EP, TectÃ³nica, is nevertheless one of the explosive statements in recent memory.It's a quality three-tracker, but opening cut "Seismic Activity" is the one that truly stands out as the jewel in the crown. The trio find a rousing middle ground between their respective styles of Latin-fortified tech house and buoyant UKG, enhanced by a slowed-down sample from Salt-N-Pepa's "Push It." This is dark and lusty 2-step capable of, well, shattering dance floors the world over. - Michael Lawson

### **HiTech** - SPANK! (Loma Vista)
> HiTech know how to keep cool under pressure. This is key to the trio's marriage of heart-palpitating ghettotech with laid-back rapping: their ability to float atop 150 BPM sizzlers with pure control. "SPANK!" pushes that contrast to the max, overlaying a dizzying central bongo loop with programmed keys, synth flares and laser FX.But it runs on GDMRW and King Milo's verses, traded off drill-style in attempts at getting their hands on a triple threat: "She got beauty / She got brains / She got booty all in that thang." Sure, "bend it over, let me spank," isn't the subtlest come-on, but HiTech's flow makes it seem almost elegant. The end result is as sexy and tactile as the palm-to-ass communion. - Hattie Lindert

### **Claire Rousay & Lala Lala** - please 5 more minutes (Thrill Jockey)
> There is an inherent melancholy in having to ask for more time; an underlying sense of defeat in prolonging the inevitable. And though experimental composer Claire Rousay is not above having to â€œbegâ€ for it, as she candidly croons on electronic ballad â€œplease 5 more minutesâ€â€”a standout from this year's sentimentâ€”she wrings clear-eyed dignity out of an act of vulnerability.Combining purposeful guitar with heavily Auto-Tuned vocals, Rousay modifies the self-described "emo ambient" textures of her early work into a cyber-folk vignette that pierces your heart and subverts your ear. Its emotional clarity is overwhelming; the track abandons words for a climax of hymnal chords which slowly fade into a denouement of silence. Time, as it must, has run out. - Jake Indiana

### **Joker** - Juggernaut (Kapsize)
> 2024 was filled to the brim with throwbacks to that foggy period in the late '00s when dubstep was being transformed. This British bass revival also meant that when Joker dropped a 140 BPM monster, he'd arguably never sounded more contemporary. "Juggernaut" is classic Joker: ethereal strings and anthemic horns twist over sparse drum programming and distorted bass so nasty it could make Howard Stern blush.What keeps "Juggernaut" from being a nostalgic victory lap is how he turns everything up to 11. He's had big drops before, but nothing as gargantuan as the lift-off a minute into "Juggernaut." This is "Tron" for a whole new generation. - Henry Ivry

### **Moktar & Saad El Soghayar** - Haraka Ø­Ø±ÙƒØ© (Astral People)
> "Haraka Ø­Ø±ÙƒØ©" is a monumental convergence between Moktar and Egyptian Mahraganat luminary Saad El Soghayar. Translating to "movement" in Arabic, the track is a unique and powerful meeting point of two street-born genres that embody celebration, cultural resistance and community. Moktar has weaved El Soghayar's wedding anthem into a tapestry of traditional darbuka rhythms and drum & bass, creating a rhythmically rich dialogue of tension and release.Moktar has managed to span meridians, creating a knockout that echoes the venn diagram of heritage and contemporary dance music. From Cairo's DIY block parties to London's pirate radio, "Haraka Ø­Ø±ÙƒØ©" is a testament to how the underground has always spoken the same language, no matter where it calls home. - Ramsey Tawil

### **Tinashe** - Nasty (Tinashe Music/Nice Life)
> Janet Jackson owns the word "Nasty." But you know what? The economy's rough. You can forgive herâ€”even thank herâ€”for leasing it out to Tinashe, who didn't take on stewardship of the word lightly.Tinashe's "Nasty" is both an impeccable Janet tributeâ€”minimal, casual and freaky in all the right placesâ€”and a marker of what you can achieve if you tell the major label pop ecosystem to do one and chart your own path instead. It's the kind of song that seems forgettable at first listen and totally indispensable by your third, in part because it's so confident. Unlike so much pop this year, "Nasty" is so unbothered about proving itself to you that it's easy to dismiss at first glance, even as its rubbery bassline and off-kilter vocal samples build and build. Dismiss it at your peril. - Shaad D'Souza

### **CarrÃ©** - Fawn (SPE:C)
> Los Angeles bass enthusiast CarrÃ© elevated her skills in the studio this year. Following stellar releases on Beatrice M.'s Bait and Fast at Work, Air Sign EP was the standout. Sandwiched between a pair of heavier bangers, its comparatively low-key B-side, "Fawn," is a masterful distillation of her signature technoid dubstep. Moving at a subtly brisker clip than traditional 140, the track's bass pulses, spiralling vocals and dubbed-out drums shift and cycle, evoking the earth-rattling march of a giant.After 80 seconds of moody table-setting, a playful series of plucks erupts seemingly from nowhere, skipping up and down in pitch. Then, as quickly as it arrived, this cute riff is gone, displaying CarrÃ©'s deft control over arrangement. For anyone curious about dark and minimal dubstep's evolution over the past decade, this is the place to start. - Tom Gledhill

### **Kim Gordon** - BYE BYE (Matador)
> Kim Gordon landed the coldest industrial trap record of 2024, you say? Why not. Where earlier instances of the downtown icon fringing electronic music were speckled in hissâ€”see Ciccone Youth's insouciant Madonna flip "Into The Groovey" or far-out noise excursions with illbient pioneer DJ Oliveâ€”"BYE BYE" is incredibly forthright.It's loud, both in the offhand banality of Kim Gordon rapping a pre-trip checklist (turtleneck, milk thistle, vibrator), as well as the collision of synth stabs, abrasive guitars and a beat that knocks like a cinder block to the head. Gordon can evidently sell anything. And if you figure the former frontwoman of Sonic Youth has no business being on an RA end-of-year list, well, I can think of two words she might use to bid that sentiment adieu too. - Gabriel Szatan

### **Mk.gee** - Breakthespell (R&R)
> If we're being honest, part of Mk.gee's appeal is that you can't understand a word he's saying. Throughout his dazzling debut album, Two Star & the Dream Police, the New Jersey-born artist's warbled vocals are at points barely decipherableâ€”prioritising atmosphere over precision, which cloaks his music in a quixotic, almost Jai Paul-ish mist.On "Breakthespell," his voice melts into the heavily delayed guitars and billowing synths he's become known for. Once you finally manage to decode lyrics, they only heighten the hazy ambience, as he anguishedly calls out: "I can't win / And I won't end." The agent of his heartbreak is unclear; although if the song title offers any hints, it might even be Mk.gee himself. "Breakthespell" may not provide clarity, but it doesn't matterâ€”this is the sound of catharsis. - Bella Aquilina

### **Charisse C & DJ Kwamzy** - Morning Sun (Abantu)
> It was almost inevitable that Charisse C, one of the UK's leading ambassadors for amapiano, would eventually step out from behind the decks and into the vocal booth. "Morning Sun" is her bright take on the beloved genre, buoyed by airy vocals that create a sense of spiritual peace. But those sparkling notes soon transform into a moody dance floor heater, channelling the irresistible drama of amapiano and 3-step's percussive patterns.With Kwamzy on the assist, the pair created a hybrid anthem that represents the vibrant sounds of contemporary South African dance music. As well as being an excellent entry into the canon, "Morning Sun" represents Charisse C's natural progression from DJ to fully rounded artistâ€”and she makes it look effortless. - Jesse Bernard

### **Mica Levi** - slob air (Hyperdub)
> You never know what to expect from South London composer Mica Levi. Their last solo record, 2021's Blue Alibi, was a spiky, lo-fi grunge affair, while their score for Jonathan Glazerâ€™s 2023 chilling film The Zone of Interest unleashed nightmares through experimental found sound.This summer, Levi once again opted for unpredictability with their Hyperdub debut, the 12-minute dream pop epic hypnotically circles around a loop of undulating synths, a rumbling bass hum and an assertive, locked-in beat. Occasionally, the transcendental melody is interrupted by a slight key change or the growing swell of indecipherable voices, but it's never enough to unseat the song's steady, meditative pace. "slob air" is like watching the sun rise on the top deck of the bus after a bleary night outâ€”life-affirming. - Steph Philips

### **Thoughtforms** - Tubes (Thoughtforms)
> Uruguayan artist Fernando Zapico, AKA Z@P, has been steadily drip-feeding low-slung, acid tech house into the catalogues of niche labels for years. Now, his endeavours have culminated on Red, a statement of intent on own imprint. The EP's sharpest cut, "Tubes," features a classic proggy synth line that syphons off inspiration from techno, electro and wave, intertwining pulsing synths with metallic rhythms that pitter-patter across the four-four grid.While the rest of the EP nods towards some of the nostalgic signifiers defining today's zeitgeistâ€”consider the mesmeric bounce of Kalahari Oyster Cult's outputâ€”"Tubes"' insatiable groove is the real winner. It's easy to imagine it ripping at the height of a raucous party, the crowd swaying to its heaving beat. - Chloe Lula

### **FKA twigs** - Eusexua (Young)
> In 2024, pop stars shaped culture not only through their art, but by outright defining social mores and public behaviour. Tinashe's "Nasty" allowed an anxiety-ridden generation having less casual sex to try on a slutty persona and Charli xcx's carefree BRAT paved a green road from the club to the Vice President's office.As the sun began to set on late summer, avant-pop visionary FKA twigs also chimed in with the sultry mystique of "Eusexua," the title track from her forthcoming album. While muted techno kicks thump in the distance, the song immediately introduces us not only to a feeling (which twigs describes as "the pinnacle of human experience"), but also an entire cinematic universe full of alien tattoos, silver statement jewellery, seven-inch Pleasers and sheer lingerie. twigs has always sung around the dance floor's periphery, but on "Eusexua," she's never sounded so sure of her place in the heart of the club. - Kiana Mickles

### **RHR & Logan_OLM** - Diagonal (Dub Mix) (Nice & Deadly)
> It's almost too easy to make a club incinerator with Logan_olm on the mic. The London MC has proven time and again that his fierce flows can dominate any beat. In 2024, he met his match in SÃ£o Paulo funk export RHR, who spent years observing the UK scene from almost 6,000 miles away, fusing his learnings with Brazil's diasporic rhythms. So when he finally got in the ring with Logan, what was the result?The pair's rowdy team-up, "Diagonal (Dub Mix)," vaults straight out the blocks with disorientating sample chops and a chest-caving rumble, laying the perfect foundation for the MC's righteous assertions of his own ability to storm onto any track and make himself heard. Stomping bass that slips off its axis; flecks of flanged synth; percussion that reaches for tamborzÃ£oâ€”it's a whirlwind of energy. "Diagonal (Dub Mix)" is the sound of SÃ£o Paulo and London colliding spectacularly. - Nathan Evans

### **Joy Orbison** - flight fm (Hinge Finger)
> There's always one: doggedly ubiquitous, memed halfway to oblivion, the international overplayers' anthem. Our answer came in record time this year, after "flight fm" landed on January 17th and confirmed that Overmono's Dobermanns would be treated to 12 months of much needed R&R. Dance floors haven't exactly been light on wallopers cribbing their sub action from darkside jungle and speed garage lately, so to understand why "flight fm" went supernova, it's worth paying attention to what the song doesn't do."flight fm" is no-nonsense enough to make the track it might be modelled on, Si Begg's "Revolution No 1," sound positively cluttered. A dainty pre-tremor, some skippy drums and that enormous, grungy basslineâ€”done. Incredibly effective. Vast pockets of negative space compelled others to fill in the blanks, which is why everyone from ropey TikTok remixers to Future and even The Chainsmokers (yes, seriously) mobbed in. What Joy O understands more than most is that a killer hook only represents half the battle. You still need the nous to clear everything else out the way and let it roll. - Gabriel Szatan

### **Snakeskin** - Waiting (Mais Um)
> Snakeskin's second album, They Kept Out Photographs, reflects on a tumultuous year in Lebanon, fuelled by a sense of anger, melancholy and defiance. Its piÃ¨ce de rÃ©sistance is the ominous and introspective "Waiting," which features one half of the duo, Julia Sabra, reciting an excerpt from Lebanese poet Etel Adnan's To Be in a Time of War. The words, profoundly poignant on their own, transform simple ongoings of daily life into acts of resistance during wartime.Paired with strong drums, the track opens with an eerie beat reminiscent of a church bell or a loud clock tolling the arrival of doomsday. The combination of Sabra's gradually distorting voice, the increasingly aggressive rhythm and almost mundane lyrics is deeply hypnotic, immersing us in Snakeskin's alternate reality. Yet, like a silver lining amid the heaviness, chimes add a subtle brightness, hinting at the resilience that quietly endures beneath the agony of living through destruction. - Tamara Saade

### **Objekt** - Ganzfeld (Djrum Remix) (Kapsela)
> Djrum vs. Objekt? The nerds were salivating. Djrum vs. Objekt on "Ganzfeld"? Tongues were practically on the floor. The ten-minute odyssey gets the gong for the year's glitchiest anthem, shapeshifting its way through tender piano, Syro-style turbulence and half-time freakouts with an exhilarating level of detail and unpredictability."Giving something a completely new context is, in some ways, the name of the game," Djrum recently told RA. He was talking about DJing, but you can tell he applied the same philosophy to this remix, transforming Objekt's much loved electro classic into a swarm of breakbeats and squiggly left turns. Few could have nailed it so hard. - Carlos Hawthorn

### **James K** - Blinkmoth (July Mix) (AD 93)
> This year, no artist has made downtempo more appealing than New York producer James K, whose breathy, lilting vocals have floated across some of 2024's best music. It makes sense that amid sustained geo-political violence and economic turbulence, we'd again find solace in shoegazeâ€”music that slows the anxious heart while holding a mirror to deep-rooted angst we prefer to leave unspoken."Blinkmoth (July Mix)" commanded repeat listens this year for an instantaneous pull that sucks you into the muted vortex of James K's romantic solitude. As she sings about the endless transference of love, a trip-hop beat glides and gallops, tactfully situating us in the '90s. But really, it's the heavenly vocals that we're here for. Her delivery glistens with the Elizabeth Fraser effect: carried foremost by feeling, the curvature of her indecipherable lyrics capture the fleeting moment in which euphoria sinks into quiet melancholy. Additions like this to the electronic shoegaze revival should give any non-believer proof of its enduring relevance. - Kiana Mickles

### **Nick LeÃ³n & Erika de Casier** - Bikini (TraTraTrax)
> A great pop song is like a charm: compact and entrancing, a daydream corked and uncorked at will. If it can't guarantee good fortune, it can at least transport a listener somewhere they feel lucky to be. And no song in 2024 made as great an escape as Nick LeÃ³n and Erika de Casier's "Bikini.""It leaks into the music somehow," LeÃ³n said earlier this month of growing up by the ocean. The Miami native describes his compositions as spaces to inhabit rather than stories; a personal stamp strong enough to transform any output he lends his hand to, be that ambient (Gloria) or perreo heaters (Rompediskoteka). De Casier wields similar scene-setting skills: she wrote one of 2023's stickiest earworms, New Jeans' "Super Shy," without ever sacrificing her signature delicate style presented to perfection on 2019 breakout album, Essentials.An anthem like "Bikini" was always on the cards for the pair: their last collaboration, the Dionysian "Ex-Girlfriend" with SHYGIRL, nailed the body-first composition of Nelly Furtado and Timbaland's best work. Harp-like keyboard notes pierce the clip of a bassline, plunging into deep dembow as elegantly as four-on-the-floor. Embracing de Casier's crystalline mezzo-soprano, "Bikini" pushes sound into pure sensation: sand between toes and lips on goose-pimpled skin. When she was a teenager, "going to the swimming pool was the worst thing I could imagine," she told Mixmag in 2021. A decade-plus later, "Bikini" comes alive in the shedding of those inhibitions: why hedge around the pool, when you could head straight for the sea?Despite "Bikini"'s deft movement between shifting rhythmic patterns, the track still manages to capture a profound sense of pause. Trying to make sense of the changing tidesâ€”"Lookin' out there / Tryin' to find a meaning"â€”de Casier only finds herself recentered "with the wind in my hair, just breathing in the air." It's these atmospheric tendencies that take "Bikini" from the track of September to the track of the year. Before LeÃ³n and de Casier, artists from Otis Redding to Kelela have gazed "out there," hoping to find some sort of solace in the meeting of water and sky. And in a year so rife with misery, there are plenty of reasons to be fearful for the future. But "Bikini" charts a different courseâ€”it's a three-minute appeal to just be. - Hattie Lindert

## [The Best Records of 2024](https://ra.co/features/4404)
Date: 2024-12-03T11:05:14.000Z

### **British Murder Boys** - Active Agents and House Boys (downwards)
> Surgeon and Regis have been creating industrial anthems as British Murder Boys for more than two decades. Individually, they're synonymous with taut, stripped back dance floor grooves that close a circle between musique concrÃ¨te and steel-toed techno. But when they come together, their output is raw and unbridled, channelling the punk lineage of Coil, Suicide and Throbbing Gristle.Indeed, their debut LP, Active Agents and House Boys, is fundamentally live-sounding, its distorted kicks and walls of resonant feedback grinding like unoiled gears. Yet the music's embrace of funk and even melody â€” a new string to their bowâ€”underlines the duo's conviction that serious music doesn't have to take itself so seriously. - Chloe Lula

### **Regal86** - Unearthed Vol.II*100 Trax* (self-released)
> 100 tunes. Let that sink in for a second. One hundred. The craziest thing? Unearthed Vol. II *100 Trax* isn't even a slog. In fact, these bitesize jams slide down like a fresh cocktailâ€”all zinger, no filler.Regal86's exquisite drum work, crafty sampling and smoky sound palette coat the vast Bandcamp dump in a marked soulfulness. Even more impressive, he's no one-trick pony: the Monterrey producer is just as adept slinging out dubby ambient techno ("Deep Forest") and slamming hip-hop ("Quiero que sepan") as euphoric hardcore ("Fades") and the hardgroove ("Baby Phat Jacket") he built his name on. Honestly, it's all so good. All of it. - Carlos Hawthorn

### **Jlin** - Akoma (Planet Mu)
> The first thing Jlin fans will notice on her third album, Akoma, is that the producer and composer's idol, Philip Glass, has added his famous arpeggios. Avant-garde queen BjÃ¶rk and contemporary ensemble Kronos Quartet also impressively made the roster.These features hint at the direction Jlin, who has gone from inventive footwork producer to unruly experimental composer, has taken over the years. "Eye Am"'s jubilant hand drums find more common ground with traditional African drumming, whereas "Summon" creates tension with a torrent of piercing strings. Rest assured, though, one listen to the plinky keys and juddering rhythms on "Grannie's Cherry Pie" confirms that this is still music that will spring dancers and footworkers into action. - Kiana Mickles

### **Nourished By Time** - Catching Chickens EP (Nourished By Time)
> Nourished by Time makes double-take music. When you first hear Marcus Brown's hypnagogic R&B anthems, you almost can't believe someone is going that hard. His songs, which gesture towards the spiritual truths underpinning quotidian tasks, are imbued with a life-or-death urgency by his stentorian baritone alone.Following 2023's breakout Erotic Probiotic 2, Catching Chickens sees Brown stretching out stylistically, exploring shoegaze guitars ("Poison-Soaked"), funhouse synth solos ("Had Ya Called") and classic nightclub crooning ("Romance in Me"). But it's the massive opener, "Hell of a Ride," that keeps us coming back. With its airy chorus, galloping beat and infectious "goodbye baby, goodbye" refrain, you can envisage Brown speeding off into yet uncharted territory. - Matt McDermott

### **Nala Sinephro** - Endlessness (Warp)
> It can be tough for a rising artist to follow up a spectacular album. Nala Sinephro's sublime debut, Space 1.8, mesmerised listeners in 2021 for its soul-stirring marriage of ambient and spiritual jazz. Three years later, the London-based harpist and modular synthesist returned with a second LP that dives deeper into restorative sounds.As its title implies, Endlessness feels like an infinite moment in time, suspended by languorous synth arpeggios and hushed sax runs. While some jazz fans prefer the dynamism of its predecessor, the beauty of Endlessness lies in its quietude. Sit back and soak up its ambrosial chords. - Nyshka Chandran

### **Midland** - Fragments of Us (Graded)
> Midland's long-awaited debut album, Fragments of Us, is a moving document of queer heritage, from the peak of the AIDS crisis and institution of the UK's discriminatory Section 28 legislation to the utopian dreaming of artists like Stereogamus' Jonny Seymour and clubs like NYC Downlow.The record is a collection of moody and overcast downtempo songs, in which Midland's poignant yet glittering arpeggios and skittering drums commune with queer voices, past and present. But as much as it's an interrogation of the violence that has engulfed queer public life, Fragments of Us is also a celebrationâ€”just wait for those life-affirming strings on "Chapter 10." - Henry Ivry

### **Total Blue** - Total Blue (Music From Memory)
> What do you picture when you think of the Los Angeles skyline? Maybe it's a haze of hot air, twinkling lights at night or how the city seems to stretch as far as the eye can see. It's that topography and atmosphere that Angeleno trio Total Blue wanted to replicate on their debut LP.They succeeded with gusto: the record is a gentle, meandering excursion through expansive ambient textures, New Age jazz experimentations and lush vintage melodies that recall noirish film scenes where the protagonist drives through Beverly Hills, totally unburdened by the downward pressures of life. A stunning escape. - Katie Thomas

### **gum.mp3** - Black Life, Red Planet (Gum Studio)
> gum.mp3 is that all-too-rare artist making smart music you can still go stupid to. The Baltimore-based producer and eldiaNYC crew member's latest offering, Black Life, Red Planet, is a studied yet unfussy expedition through house and jungle, woven with threads of blues, funk and trap."Knowingness" shakes the dust from a swampy blues riff; on "Deimos," a red herring flamenco loop gives way to dembow that could be played via a didgeridoo. "Believe," co-produced with Detroit juke master swoozydolphin, might be the first ambient soundbath with a breakbeat. gum.mp3 creates a common home for radical creative traditions too often siloedâ€”it's one of the most innovative projects of the year. - Hattie Lindert

### **Tim Reaper & Kloke** - In Full Effect (Hyperdub)
> It's hard to believe it took this long for Tim Reaper to release a full-length album. Same goes for agenda-setting label Hyperdub, which, before In Full Effect, had never released a jungle LP. Luckily, Reaper and Naarm (Melbourne) producer Kloke linked up to do the honours, whisking different flavours of early '90s breakbeat into something that transcends the all-too-comfortable pastiche of revivalism.They masterfully reimagine what jungle's trajectory would've looked like had it gone on uninterrupted from its ragga era, with propulsive drum programming and emotional atmospherics serving as the project's anchor. Evocative and trance-inducing, In Full Effect has only solidified jungle's enduring versatility. - Emeka Okonkwo

### **Tyla** - Tyla (FAX/Epic)
> It all started with "Water." In 2023, South African pop powerhouse Tyla's refreshing R&B single launched her into global stardomâ€”and even kicked off a millions-strong TikTok dance craze. This year's self-titled debut album builds on that momentum with a carefully balanced work that's as exciting as it is soulful, as assured as it is vulnerable.Infused with pop, Afrobeats and polished amapiano log drums, the LP is a potent reflection of the various global musical cultures that raised Tyla. Her thoughts on her own identity may have sparked social media discourse, but she stood firm in her truth, dog-walking doubters all the way to the GRAMMYs. - Shiba Melissa Mazaza

### **Various Artists** - Sky Is The Limit (Love on the Rocks)
> Love On The Rocks' catalogue oozes fun and whimsy. On this ten-year compilation, PARAMIDA gathered label regulars (Massimiliano Pagliara, Fantastic Man) and newbies (Sweely, E-Talking) to curate a record capturing the label's exuberant palette of colour and feelingâ€”think trancey synths, progressive grooves, wriggling 303s, dreamy melodies and pumping house rhythms.The frivolity is loudest in the bounce of Alex Kassian & Running Hot's closer "The Love Theme," which gleefully samples Haddaway's 1993 chart-topper "What Is Love." Toasting to a decade via a gleaming eight tracks is a confident missive. Some may say the compilation leans towards "guilty pleasure." To that, we say: there's no such thingâ€”it's just pleasure. - Katie Thomas

### **Skee Mask** - ISS010 (Ilian Tape)
> ISS010 strikes a chord with both factions of Skee Mask's fan base: the production nerds and the DJ set devotees. For the heads, it delivers his signature package of intricately layered sound design, dense percussion, and a wash of echo and reverb. But this time, the DJ devotees get their due as well. ISS010 marks a shift from Skee Maskâ€™s breakbeat explorations to a more dance floor-focused sound, reflecting the heavily house and techno-infused energy of his current DJ sets. The seven-tracker blends syncopated rhythms with gorgeous melodies, weaving flashes of dubstep and ambient textures into rave-ready form. Grime-indebted beats on tracks like â€œThe Billsâ€ could as readily host an MC as send a Detroit loft party into overdrive, while â€œDouble Standardâ€ combines shimmering synths with propulsive drums, making it well suited for introspective home listening or peak-time club play. In a major year for Skee Mask, ISS010 was a record that engaged both body and soul. - Fahad Akinsanya

### **CCL & Ciel** - Tilda's Goat Stare (NAFF)
> CCL and Ciel are a natural fit. Not only because of the DJ-producer pair's enduring friendship, but their shared affinity for journeying through the psychedelic end of the rave spectrum, from proggy doof bangers to swampy downtempo.The unruly title track on their powerful joint EP lights the path to a portal filled with bass pressure and dialogue sampled from Tilda Swinton's 2002 film Teknolust (with an acid-spiked Priori remix to boot). "Goblin Mode" burrows into a subterranean network of synth gurgles and menacing hoover, while "Spiral Drive" sounds like a cyborg reaching for a higher state of consciousness. Who else could melt a feminist sci-fi film into chemistry-altering club trax? - April Clare Welsh

### **Various Artists** - Letters to a Future Palestine (Umay)
> The first compilation on Nene H's UMAY label is a proud display of musical and political unity. Featuring an array of artists and allies from across the Palestinian and SWANA diasporaâ€”ranging from Muskila and KETTALYNNE to Estoc and rRoxymoreâ€”Letters to a Future Palestine's 19 tracks are a collective call for solidarity.Traditional drum loops reworked for the rave ("Arish") and powerful Arabic vocal passages ("TARWIDA") build on the sense of ritual and communion, while disjointed breaks accompany eerie grime verses ("Ghrab Ilbain"), all bound by a palpable spirit of defiance. With proceeds going to Gaza's community kitchens, this moving collection of tracks transmits hope for Palestinian freedom. - Nyshka Chandran

### **Verraco** - Breathe, Godspeed (Timedance)
> On Breathe, Godspeed, Verraco is in full-throttle mode. The Colombian producer's subversive attitude takes flight via a bricolage of techno, dembow, IDM and glitch, bodying listeners with its sheer weight. Intensity levels escalate to a peak with a clever emphasis on rave fundamentals rather than shock value: there are nasty basslines, tribal influences, elements of rowdy post-dubstep and distorted vocal samples.Tracks are thunderous and jaw-dropping but strategically calibrated, transforming the cadence of Latin rhythms into a throbbing mass of futuristic sound design. Breathe, Godspeed is a radical snapshot of Verraco's music-making philosophyâ€”it disorients, stimulates and, best of all, knows exactly what it wants to say. - Nyshka Chandran

### **Mabe Fratti** - Sentir Que No Sabes (Unheard of Hope)
> "At the moment, I'm pro-confusion. Or maybe not," wrote Guatemalan composer Mabe Fratti in the liner notes of her fourth LP, Sentir Que No Sabes, which means "to feel that I don't know" in Spanish. The first clue that demonstrates the strength of her latest work is opener, "Kravitz," with its funky cello bassline, dark atmospherics and strolling-pace rhythm. It's a fitting introduction to the musician's most accessible album yet, which largely forgoes the murky timbres and synth abstraction of her earlier works.Instead, tracks such as "OÃ­dos," where Fratti's sweet soprano springs above whining trumpet, have spawned comparisons to the jazzy angst of singer-songwriters like Fiona Apple. Or take "Descubrimos un suspiro," where her voice is raw and up close as strings rustle against warm horns. On Sentir Que No Sabes, Fratti takes the threads of her denser projects and weaves it into a richly textured, utterly enthralling tapestry. - Kiana Mickles

### **NÃ­dia & Valentina** - Estradas (Latency)
> NÃ­dia and Valentina Magaletti may be from different musical backgrounds, but one thing they have in common is a shared disregard for convention. NÃ­dia is something of an outlier within the PrÃ­ncipe universe, her singular brand of kuduro and batida positioned slightly outside of the label's core sound. As for Magaletti, the experimental percussionist appears to be driven by a burning desire to constantly break new rhythmic ground, with each of her collaborative projects more ambitious than the last.It's no surprise, then, that their debut joint project, Estradas, sounded like little else this year. The nine-track LP begins as a tense to and fro between two artists feeling each other out, but the moments in which they find a shared musical language are dizzying. It's both a testament to the transcendental powers of rhythm and the thrilling possibilities of improvised collaboration. - Michael Lawson

### **Syclops** - Black Eye (Bubble Tease Comms)
> "Fried Ice Cream Is a Reality." Maurice Fulton's Twitter bio offers a glimpse into a typically press-shy artist's delight for oddball concepts. The Baltimore DJ and producer's vast discography connects the dots between disco, jazz, house and experimental electronics, from BOOF and Eddie & The Eggs to unexpected collaborations with Crystal Waters and RoÃ­sin Murphy.His singular sense for fusing the weird and the funky has perhaps never been more apparent than on Syclops' fourth album, Black Eye. The trioâ€”Fulton, percussionist Mim Suleiman and guitarist Hanna Sarkariâ€”delivers yet another kaleidoscopic album bursting at the seams with ideas: tracks like "Pink Sarah NYC Is Back" invoke future jazz and bleep techno, while "Karo Is Going Swimming" sounds like dub techno chucked through a cosmic blender. It's frankly bananas, and our dance floors are all the better for it. - Bella Aquilina

### **gyrofield** - These Heavens (XL Recordings)
> When getting arms around this riot of hyper-technical programming, overlapping rivulets of sound and intricate fidelity, it's worth stating things plainly: These Heavens is one of the most satisfying EPs in quite some time.Drum & bass virtuoso gyrofield (AKA Kiana Li) has been quietly prolific in recent years, popping up everywhere from Critical to Eastern Margins. Yet it was her XL debut where she truly shot for the moon with a record informed by stargazing and Stephen Hawking as much as Hideo Kojima and Noisia. Li practically undergoes a full villain arc in 23 minutes, staging a shift from tones so crystalline you'd be forgiven for thinking they were beamed direct from the Pillars of Creation, to mottled drumfunk hissing and heaving under the weight of menace. These Heavens is explosive, but more than that, it's pure cosmology in motion. - Gabriel Szatan

### **DJ Anderson do ParaÃ­so** - QueridÃ£o (Nyege Nyege Tapes)
> DJ Anderson do ParaÃ­so knows how to twist baile funk's frenetic energy into haunted minimalism. The Belo Horizonte native's productions merge sparse electronic elements inspired by drill and trap with sluggish violins, pianos, flutes and timpaniâ€”all of which fill the air with a mysterious sensuality and ominous aura. QueridÃ£o, which translates to "beloved" from Portuguese, is a collection of tracks that has taken the producer from SoundCloud cult favourite to living legend in the rising funk mineiro scene of Belo Horizonte.The mountainous, landlocked city is widely celebrated for its slower and more melodic take on funk, but what sets Anderson apart is his commitment to downright eerie experimentalism, stripping down the sound's full-bodied elements to forge epic and radical restraint. It's really no wonder that QueridÃ£o stands out as some of the most enticingly abstract dance music of the year. - GG Albuquerque

### **Polygonia** - Da Nao Tian Gong (Midgar)
> Da Nao Tian Gong is Polygonia's most watched childhood film. Translating to "Havoc in Heaven," the narrative links heaven to natureâ€”from the peaches of immortality in the Heavenly Garden to Fruit Mountain. The Chinese-German artist has consistently sought out lessons from our environment, recently telling Resident Advisor: "People should collaborate together in peace to save our planet."In 2024, Earth is increasingly heating up. Citiesâ€”and peopleâ€”have been set alight. On Da Nao Tian Gong, Polygonia makes sense of this destruction through an effervescent mix of ambient, techno and downtempo, using the synthetic to recreate the organic, from a synth pad dawn chorus to the rhythmic hissing of water. Nestled at the heart of this sublime EP lies the simple yet powerful message of protecting our world. The peaches, the seeds, the roots. In a year of mass displacement, what could be more pertinent than that? - Vivian Yeung

### **Astrid Sonne** - Great Doubt (Escho)
> Great Doubt is Astrid Sonne's first album as a singer-songwriter, but she's been using her voice for much longer. The Danish artist has spoken about her time spent in church choirs, acknowledging its role in shaping her vocals: "I definitely wouldn't be singing as loud as I do." On Great Doubt, Sonne is definitely loud, producing immense emotional volume out of sparse arrangements."Do you wanna" arrives with a straight but heavy drum beat as Sonne confesses, "Do you wanna have a baby? / I really don't know." This unnervingly direct existentialism runs through the entire album, whether in the slow, booming 808s on "Everything is unreal" or the simple pizzicato viola on "Almost." Sonne doesn't shy away from bold, unembellished statements, only augmenting the sense of intimacy (as on the plaintive, Ben Vince-assisted "Say you love me"). In daring to confront her deepest fears head-on, Sonne has made the year's most striking pop album. - Bella Aquilina

### **Charli xcx** - BRAT (Atlantic)
> For a decade, Charli xcx thrashed between two seemingly contradictory stations: pop sweetheart and cult icon. She lacquered finely tuned singles in industry-standard polish, then loaded brilliant, labyrinthine albums with dense lines about her deepest fears. With BRAT, she swung to please her nicheâ€”and ended up painting the summer radioactive green. Her most momentous album to date is a rare animal: a galvanising pop record all wound up for the club on one hand, a glistening smorgasbord of spilled guts on the other.By turning her insecurities inside out on songs like "Sympathy is a knife" and "Girl, so confusing," then counterweighting those cerebations with the whole-body release of "Von dutch" and "Club classics," Charli alchemised a new vision of her own success. She's long picked over the question of what it means to make it. BRAT homes in on something of an answer: there's no "it" to make. Sell all the records you want, or don'tâ€”you have to come home to yourself either way. Might as well crank the bass and dance through it. - Sasha Geffen

### **De Schuurman** - Bubbling Forever (Nyege Nyege Tapes)
> Slamming body music from a true master who transmits the vivacity and nerve of Caribbean club culture: that's Bubbling Forever. On his second official collection of bubblingâ€”a sped-up mutation of dancehallâ€”Dutch-Surinamese producer De Schuurman builds on the genre's Afro-diasporic legacy with a clutch of tracks designed to whip up hysteria in the rave."Benniale Dakar" starts with the ominous drama of an early Pop Smoke trap tune then launches into a rattling speed dembow. As smoky pads permeate the air, the beat decelerates into half-timeâ€”only a quick moment to gather your waist before the wine-inducing rhythms of "Bubbling Meets Kaseko," which fuse bubbling's restless kicks with traditional Surinamese skratji percussion. On "Stylez two," mischievous samples of Lil Jon's infamous "OK!" and KRS-One's "Sound of da Police" can jolt even the stiffest hips into work. When "Scratchin"'s pointillist synths plink around vocal samples of "I'm just scratchin' the surface," you get the sense it's both a call to action and warning shot: Schuurman is here to stay. - Rachel Grace Almeida

### **Loidis** - One Day (Incienso)
> Not waving, or drowning, but drifting. That's how 2024 felt for many of us: a serotonin crash made all the more raw by an increasingly cruel world. After years of clubland electrifying the masses with the shock of the new, we chose to lean the other way, prioritising cosy records that made you thankful for what you already have (a craving that, in alternative circles, drew people to the spectral-jukebox transmissions of Cindy Lee like moth to flame). Into this climate landed a masterclass in softer vibrations from Brian Leeds, who, as Huerco S. and Pendant, has already proved himself a master of suspended animation several times over. One Day both encapsulated the mood and cut through it like a beacon.Does it augur poorly for a culture built on progression to take a step back and recalibrate? Well, the past was priced in; Loidis is the ancient name for Leeds, after all. And though One Day was built around slippery micro rhythms and delayed dub stabs, Leeds hardly soapboxed for a return to subtlety. The strongest promo was essentially happenstance, after he termed the project "dub mnml emo tech" to wriggle out of anything too formal, but wound up perfectly articulating its playful vibe.Just as For Those Of Youâ€¦'s truncated loops were a creative sleight-of-hand, One Day pulls off a sly trick throughout. Leeds mimics the lossy compression and audio degradation favoured by the clicks 'n cuts set, only this time using stem separation software and creative resampling that falls closer, he told us, to hypermodern genres. In doing so, he created a shapeshifting palette: all muzzled kicks, panned basslines bobbing through hyaline textures and indulgent codas tacked onto nine- or ten-minute tunes ("Why Do," "Love's Linneaments," "Sugar Snot") that you could have sworn flashed by in four. It scans as wrong at first blush, so you're compelled to run it back a dozen timesâ€”by which point, naturally, it sounds exceptional.One Day doesn't just revitalise styles that faded from favour; it glows with the patience of Shinchi Atobe and DJ Sprinkles, the frolic of IsolÃ©e and Dinky, the 3 AM soul-searching of Claro Intelecto and Paul St. Hilaire. Most obviously, the spirit of Alcachofa and Vocalcity feel hardcoded into its DNA. These are records that have meant a lot to people over the years, made by artists who have stood the test of time. I'd be lying if I didn't think Leeds is in that conversation now.When it arrived, One Day might have seemed too discrete to break out, but months of compulsive listening have upended that. If we're resting at a waystation en route to a destination as-yet-unclear, there was no more generous or agreeable companion. So while there aren't many conclusions to be drawn from the discomforting haze of 2024, this much is true: the album that felt primed to take a slow stroll to classic status has raced way ahead of schedule. It's already there. - Gabriel Szatan

## [The Best Tracks of 2023](https://ra.co/features/4289)
Date: 2023-12-19T17:20:26.000Z

### DJ SWISHA - CLUB MEGAMIXXX
