## [The Best Albums of 2023](https://ra.co/features/4293)
Date: 2023-12-14T14:00:39.000Z

### Kelela - Raven (Warp Records)
> Warp RecordsKelela - Raven At the shows for her new album, Kelela stood alone onstage. This was a deliberate choice, she explained, to have everything stripped back so audiences could see herâ€”and hear herâ€”for all she was. But up there, the blue lights around her dimmed, it was clear that her solitary figure also reflected her more bitter-than-sweet struggles against what she described as "male stoicism." This remark came from the revelations she had while reading The Will to Change, an investigation of men, masculinity and love by the radical Black feminist scholar bell hooks. Her epiphany was painstakingly reflected in the dancehall derivation "On The Run": "You get around enough / Too busy actin' tough / Give me a softer side / I won't wait all night." Patriarchal culture doesn't only hurt women, Kelela discoveredâ€”it also restricts the way men are able to explore intimacy and achieve wholeness for themselves. I saw Kelela perform in Berlin. 13 of Raven's 15 tracks were produced there, and it shows. There's a sorrow and solemnity woven into the city's monochromatic corners that echo through Raven, like a pebble rattling in an empty aluminium can. Even the title track is underpinned by a spacious yearning, as if on the brink of a breaking pointâ€”"Took all my labour / Don't tell me that I'm strong," she sings, before gradually trotting into a heaving 4/4 beat, a subtle nod to clubbing as escapism. By the album's conclusion, "Far Away," Kelela finds her deliverance in the form of honeyed ad-libs undulating over sounds of crashing waves, as if signalling that with enough time and perspective, all pain can be alchemised into pure spirit. -Whitney Wei

### Caroline Polachek - Desire I Want To Turn Into You (Perpetual Novice)
> Perpetual NoviceCaroline Polachek - Desire I Want To Turn Into You Diving headfirst into the delusion and madness that accompanies the all-consuming feeling of romantic and sexual passion, this unapologetically raw album leaves no stone unturned in its portrayal of emotional intensity. Through visceral lyrics that underline the idea of desire as a truly physical sensation, the ex-Chairlift vocalist sings of self-indulgent surrender to a lover without the slightest care of appearing desperate or needy. But it's the productionâ€”from Polachek and Danny L. Harleâ€”that truly makes this a multifaceted pop record: feathery drum & bass, flamenco, dreamy rock and bassy R&B bops add to the physicality of Polachek's feelings, pushing her theatrical vocals outside of the shielded realm of inner thoughts and into the material world. -Nyshka Chandran Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### James Holden - Imagine This Is A High Dimensional Space Of All Possibilities (Border Community)
> Border CommunityJames Holden - Imagine This Is A High Dimensional Space Of All Possibilities James Holden's music has always been otherworldly. Raised on pirate radio, folktronica, free jazz and everything in between, he conjures up mythical fairy tales where flickers of dance music past meander into pastoral soundscapes. This all culminated with Imagine This Is A High Dimensional Space Of All Possibilities, which marks a welcome return to the club for Holdenâ€”or his version of it, anyway. Recognisable dance music tropes (hints of dub techno, echoes of house, microdoses of rave) nestle into the rich and complex instrumentation that gives all of Holden's music its distinctive flair. If Jon Hassell had been born four decades later and became hooked on acid house, this is the album he would've wanted to write. -Henry Ivry Listen: Bandcamp

### Tirzah - trip9love...? (Domino)
> DominoTirzah - trip9love...? Over the past decade, childhood friends Tirzah Maston and Mica Levi have become a quietly formidable power duo (in leftfield music circles, at least). On their latest LP of heart-tugging R&B, Levi's tough 808s and trilling piano sketches hold a steady, unrelenting pace while Tirzah pours her heart into 11 rough-and-ready love songs. All the familiar hallmarks of Tirzah are thereâ€”understated vocals and a sound rooted in "disarming simplicity"â€”but here everything is notched up to a new, more physical intensity. Each track packs a smouldering punch and Levi's distorted piano melodies on tracks like "F22" and "Promises" have Grand Cru earworm qualities. The album turns Tirzah and Levi's often ramshackle songs into a steamrolling train that tugs at the heartstrings all the harder, while still holding onto the lightweight feel that makes all of the project's music so enchanting. -Conor McTernan Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Regal86 - La Onda (Self-released)
> Self-releasedRegal86 - La Onda If there was one trend in techno to note this yearâ€”aside from "fast"â€”it was hardgroove, a taut and loopy style originally pioneered in the '90s and making one hell of a comeback on dance floors across the Americas and Europe in 2023. Regal86, a buzzy producer from Monterrey makes all kinds of music, but he's particularly good at hardgroove. His album La Onda landed at the perfect time to take the revival to the next level. With breathless sequencing and expert programming, this is hard, fast dance music that doesn't bludgeon you over the head, but instead invites you to dance and get lost in its intricacies. And with trip-hop breaks and clever interludes, La Onda works as an album through and through, recalling some '90s techno greats with real finesse. -Andrew Ryce Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Overmono - Good Lies (XL Recordings)
> XL RecordingsOvermono - Good Lies Going from throwing makeshift parties deep in the woods to sold-out global tours, Overmono's ascent is long overdue. After a decade of passionate grinding in the underground, their debut album, Good Lies, makes a well-earned victory lap. Boundless euphoria is the goal and '90s rave and Burial-adjacent techno are the meansâ€”including radio-ready vocal chops from the likes of Tirzah, Slowthai and CASISDEAD. Having penned a vibrant love letter to both the past and present of UK dance music, the two brothers from rural Wales establish themselves as authors of its future. -Emeka Okonkwo Listen: Bandcamp

### James Blake - Playing Robots Into Heaven (Columbia)
> ColumbiaJames Blake - Playing Robots Into Heaven Don't call it a comebackâ€¦ but James Blake's latest album kind of feels like a comeback. He's spent years perfecting an electronic singer-songwriter style that has seen him working with everyone from Kendrick Lamar to Frank Ocean. On Playing Robots Into Heaven, he dives head first into club music and delivers some of his canniest fusions yet. The melodrama and introspection is still there, but on tracks like the thrilling "Loading" or the surging house of "Fall Back," his wordsâ€”and dextrous vocal choppingâ€”gains a whole new power, especially when sandwiched between woozy ballads like "Fire The Editor." In other words, it's the best of both worlds. -Andrew Ryce Apple Music / Spotify

### Mr. G - Pearls Don't Lay On The Shore (Childhood)
> ChildhoodMr. G - Pearls Don't Lay On The Shore According to Mr. G, Pearls Don't Lay On The Shore is what happens when he makes music from the soul. Over 14 tracks, the funky tech house he built his name on makes room for plaintive New Age delights and darkly tinted downtempo. It's a turbulent, subaquatic voyage that reaches even murkier depths than 2021's The Forced Force Is Not The True Force. Where the sonar-guided ominousness and broad sawtooth basslines on tracks like "No Safe Zones" evoke the ocean floor, the searching keys and trance-inducing hand drums on tracks like "For Those Who Have Lost" still reach for the cosmos. A riveting ode to his mother Sylvia, Pearls Don't Lay On The Shore is Mr G. at his most soul searching and experimental. -Emeka Okonkwo Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### DJ Gigola - Fluid Meditations (Live From Earth)
> Live From EarthDJ Gigola - Fluid Meditations Aside from being a phenomenal debut album, Fluid Meditations is compelling because it embodies the enduring influence of wellness culture on dance music. The album is a tropical, at times ghostly take on modern New Age electronic music, with vocal techniques that recall Voice Actor's sibilant whispers and the guided meditation of DJ Python's memorable 2020 cut "ADMSDP." The album picks up in its second half, the meditation laid underneath hoover synths and spritely trance, making it a record that travels well from day into night. -Kiana Mickles Listen: Bandcamp

### Maara - The Ancient Truth (Step Ball Chain)
> Step Ball ChainMaara - The Ancient Truth Maara has a preternatural sense for interstellar atmospheres that are also suited to intimate home listening. Her debut album yawns to life with loose breakbeats over a lattice of whispery vocals, and eventually spins out into another realm of glimmering downtempo music. A special kind of self-assured ease in drifting into the unknown exists here. The Ancient Truth feels like a period of focused introspection, full of lush pads and pensive basslines, that reveals an inner world even more vast and mystical than how it first seems (just after the beat drops on the title track, a "wake up, wake up" chirps in the distance). All it takes is a wide-eyed sense of wonder to appreciate Dunbar's gentle yet far-flung exploration. -Whitney Wei Listen: Bandcamp

### Surgeon - Crash Recoil (Tresor)
> TresorSurgeon - Crash Recoil On Crash Recoil, Surgeon's first album in five years, he said he tried to bring his live improvisational sets to the studio for the first time, "in the same way that bands tour songs before going into the studio to record an album." The Detroit-indebted swing of earlier albums is subdued to a simmering pulse, and Surgeon's longtime influencesâ€”experimental rock bands Coil and Faustâ€”take centre stage. Spectral pads elongate over crunchy drums. Abrasive melodies appear and fade into the ether. Songs travel with the meandering, liberated structure of music built through feeling instead of dance floor mania, unlocking a new level of depth and nuance in one of the most legendary catalogues in techno. -Kiana Mickles Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Wata Igarashi - Agartha (Kompakt)
> KompaktWata Igarashi - Agartha Techno trends come and go, but Wata Igarashi will never go out of style. Cerebral, psychedelic, Rome schoolâ€”whatever adjective you choose to describe the Japanese producer's music, so long as clubs are willing to stay open for more than 12 hours at a time, there'll always be DJs digging for Igarashi's style of lean, introverted techno. This makes his debut album, Agartha, such a curveball. The LP fuses Berlin school Krautrock and fourth world ambient with the odd bit of Detroit electro and techno, both unexpected and unbelievably impressive. Igarashi has always been more than "just" a techno producer, but Agartha solidifies his reputation as a true electronic music visionary. -Henry Ivry Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Yves Tumor - Praise a Lord Who Chews But Does Not Consume (Warp Records)
> Warp RecordsYves Tumor - Praise a Lord Who Chews But Does Not Consume It's hard to believe Yves Tumor's Praise A Lord Who Chews But Which Does Not Consume; (Or Simply, Hot Between Worlds) came out in Marchâ€”it already feels like one of those timeless cult albums fans know inside-out. In recent years, the US artist has swirled around the smokey, delay-drenched periphery of '90s alt rock. Here, they jump right in, heels first, to riff on alt-rock greats like Jimi Hendrix ("Heaven Surround Usâ€¦"), The Strokes ("Operator") and even prime-era Bloc Party ("In Spite of War"), with epic guitar leads and explosive drum patterns as the rushing, technicolour backdrop to Tumor's angsty lyricism. -Sophie McNulty Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Nondi_ - Flood City Trax (Planet Mu)
> Planet MuNondi_ - Flood City Trax Johnstown, Pennsylvania, suffered devastating floods in 1889, 1936 and 1977. What was once a city with a thriving steel mill and coal industry was left in tatters alongside a draining population. According to local producer Nondi_, those who were left behindâ€”like herselfâ€”now live in limbo, floating between boredom and a constant fear of when the next flood will strike. On her ambient juke LP Flood City Trax, cutesy, cotton-cloud FX meet frenetic footwork percussion to convey a conflicting and distant depiction of a place that's been left for dead by the rest of the world, yet stubbornly lives on. -Joseph Francis Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Paul St. Hilaire - Tikiman Vol.1 (Kynant Records)
> Kynant RecordsPaul St. Hilaire - Tikiman Vol.1 It's been 17 years since his last album, but Paul St. Hilaire remains dub techno incarnate. The OG producer and Basic Channel collaborator resurfaced this March with nine exquisite tracks that show off his mastery of subtle, politically charged grooves. Touching on downtempo, minimal techno, roots reggae and dancehall, Tikiman Vol.1 runs the gamut genre-wise while delivering concise commentary on displacement, education and memory. Fuzzy dub tones on "Keep Safe" and "The Weather Man" give way to chuggier cuts like "In Door," with St. Hilaire's mesmeric vocals and streamlined basslines acting as key transition tools throughout. Still instantly recognisable, the dub techno MC has a way of making dreamy, '90s-style atmospheres feel fresh with carefully leftfield touches. -Nyshka Chandran Listen: Bandcamp

### Laurel Halo - Atlas (Awe)
> AweLaurel Halo - Atlas Laurel Halo never loved playing the piano, but she returned to it just before the pandemic. And then she was kind of stuck with it, until it became her defining instrument of the decade so far. On Atlas, her first so-called ambient album, she takes her piano and the sounds of collaborators on strings and explodes it into sonic dust. Those particles are rearranged into gentle compositions that inhale and exhale like a living respiratory system, with melodies that appear like clouds on the horizon before rolling away and letting the music clear up again. Atlas takes the fearless compositional framework of past albums and her ear for slight-but-dazzling melodies and presents them in a new, almost neoclassical way. It's another excellent entry in one of dance music's most wonderfully unpredictable discographies. -Andrew Ryce Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### DJ Danifox - Ansiedade (PrÃ­ncipe)
> PrÃ­ncipeDJ Danifox - Ansiedade Traditionally, batida is a sound characterised by a lively interplay of emotions and energies: roiling drums, racing tempos and rousing vocals. Lisbon label PrÃ­ncipe has long documented the genre's many faces, from electro bangers to housey grooves, and this stunning offering from one of its core members reveals a foggier take. The slow-burning LP unravels like a gentle love letter, pairing intuitive, staccato drums with conversational vocals and lush instrumentation (guitar and woodwinds). There are hints of jazz, trap and dub technoâ€”perhaps a reference to batida's own cross-pollination from various Angolan and Portuguese stylesâ€”and a thread of tenderness and toughness. Danifox's lilting melodies wrap batida's bounce into a dulcet, romantic daze. -Nyshka Chandran Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### a.s.o. - a.s.o. (Low Lying Records)
> Low Lying Recordsa.s.o. - a.s.o. Lewie Day and Alia Seror-O'Neill's debut self-titled LP as a.s.o is one of those albums that anyone with a longing for nostalgia could fall in love withâ€”fans of Mazzy Star, Warp Records devotees, trip-hop lovers. Part of the reason why is because the album's palette sounds eerily familiar, like every phenomenal downtempo album released before the turn of the millennium blended into one. But it's not pastiche: the lyrics feel bitingly modern and the production is taken to outer space in ways their predecessors didn't yet have the language for. And to top it off, Seror-O'Neill's frigid, sultry voice reverberates through it all gracefully. -Kiana Mickles Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Sofia Kourtesis - Madres (Ninja Tune)
> Ninja TuneSofia Kourtesis - Madres There's a track on Madres, the debut album from Berlin-based artist Sofia Kourtesis, named after the neurosurgeon who saved her mother's life. Kourtesis's music has always been connected to familial relationshipsâ€”2021's Fresia Magalena EP was named after Fresia (her mother) and Magdalena (the district in Lima where she's from) while reflecting on the death of her fatherâ€”but with each new record her music becomes an even more personal, ecstatic and richly layered collage. Madres deftly combines house music with field recordings from indigenous communities, the Peruvian cajÃ³n drum, clips from a protest against homophobia and pan-Latin American rhythms. Kourtesis makes restorative, kaleidoscopic house music that blooms from her heart and tugs at the strings of others, highlighting the power of dance floor healing. -Katie Thomas Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music

### Various - Chants Of The Holy Oyster (Kalahari Oyster Cult)
> Kalahari Oyster CultVarious - Chants Of The Holy Oyster Chants Of The Holy Oyster celebrates six years of Rey Colino's Kalahari Oyster Cult, documenting the Amsterdam label's increasingly singular footprint on contemporary club music. Connecting the dots between various corners of '90s dance musicâ€”from dreamy IDM to spacious electro, squelchy trance to wiggly tech houseâ€”Colino's vision updates these sounds, rather than basking in nostalgia. With contributions from best-in-school producers such as Roza Terenzi, Sansibar, Maara, Priori and more, the compilation serves as a great reminder that the fruits of the '90s are still ripe for renovation (and innovation). -Bella Aquilina Listen: Bandcamp

### Brutalismus 3000 - ULTRAKUNST (Live From Earth Klub)
> Live From Earth KlubBrutalismus 3000 - ULTRAKUNST Over the last two years, Brutalismus 3000 have become one of the biggest techno acts in Europe through sheer force of will and attitude. Their music, which they call "anti-techno" or "nu-gabber-post-techno-punk"â€”and they won't say it, but it's also kind of bloghouseâ€”is confrontational but also funny. They channel the outlandish vibe of early electroclash acts and dress it up in an outfit thrifted from Humana that you might see walking down Warschauer Strasse on a Friday night. Tales of murder, excess and scene-baiting ("Safe Space") are soundtracked by short-circuiting electronics, making for a gleeful LP as giddy as it is confrontational, leaving a path of destruction and laughter in its wake. -Andrew Ryce Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Mun Sing - Inflatable Gravestone (Planet Mu)
> Planet MuMun Sing - Inflatable Gravestone Inflatable Gravestone, the title of Mun Sing's debut album on Planet Mu, neatly summarises the fantastical world the Giant Swan cofounder operates in: a cold, hard symbol of death is turned into something squashy and playful. The music on Inflatable Gravestone folds listeners into that strange and wonderful land, like jumping on a bouncy castle that deflates and re-inflates without warning. The textures are intense ("Squabble"), the rhythms jolting, swerving and sometimes falling off into oblivion ("Gliding"). And it all ties together with an underlying absurdity ("Spider"). It's a place only a truly brilliant and off-kilter mind could conjure up. -Sophie McNulty Listen: Bandcamp

### Natural Wonder Beauty Concept - Natural Wonder Beauty Concept (Mexican Summer)
> Mexican SummerNatural Wonder Beauty Concept - Natural Wonder Beauty Concept On their self-titled debut album, Ana Roxanne and DJ Python aim to massage out the beauty in loneliness and alienation. Floating on tides of ambient synths, the duo employ emo rap, synth pop, lucid breakbeat and more to explore the substrates of deep connection and unspoken tenderness. Avant-garde instrumental flourishes seamlessly blend into metropolis-at-night atmospherics. Roxanne's ethereal singing plucks at every fibre of your being, while Python's intricate percussion arrangements are modulated until they begin to trickle like water. These two masters of contemplative, shoegazey electronica come together for a debut that lives up to its name and more. -Emeka Okonkwo Listen: Bandcamp

### Ciel - Homesick (Parallel Minds)
> Parallel MindsCiel - Homesick The miracle of globalised contemporary electronic music is how artists have imprinted their own unique cultural identity into their productions. The stylistically and geographically roving debut album from Ciel is one such example, melding downtempo, ambient and electro. Ciel, who was born in Xi'an, China, and came of age in Toronto, based Homesick on eight types of traditional Chinese instruments, each of which correspond to the individual track titles. The most striking among them is the anxious tremble of "Metal," interpolated between syncopated drums, and "Silk," all sly chimes and rotund basslines. Conceptually rich, Homesick embroiders the disparate textures of Ciel's Eastern home and her Western world into one elegant tapestry. -Whitney Wei Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Pangaea - Changing Channels (Hessle Audio)
> Hessle AudioPangaea - Changing Channels Festival FOMO moment of 2023? It's gotta be Ben UFO unleashing Pangaea's "Bad Lines" at Dekmantel. The happy hardcore-inspired anthem was the coda to the UK artist's short but magnificently sweet album, Changing Channels, which nailed the hard-to-wrangle cocktail of silly yet classy. In one fell swoop, Pangaea wrote the tune of the summer, doffed his cap to the hardcore continuum and poked fun at dance music's current obsession with speed and neon soundsâ€”all with a massive smile on his face. -Carlos Hawthorn Listen: Bandcamp

### K-Lone - Swells (Wisdom Teeth)
> Wisdom TeethK-Lone - Swells Swells dropped on July 7th, a few days before I made my annual pilgrimage to Love International festival. In Tisno, the sea sparkles, the air is hot and the buzz of the cicadas in the trees is omnipresent. I listened to the glossy ripples of K-Lone's second album as I lay by the water, felt the sun on my skin and closed my eyes to allow my body to recover from the night beforeâ€”the setting was just right. There are a couple dance floor-leaning tracks on the LP ("Love Me A Little," "Gel"), but Swells is largely made up of elastic tunes that slip, slide and undulate like the lapping of waves on a shoreline. Eliza Rose's vocal appears in hazy manipulations throughout (most notably on woozy R&B cut "With U"), accompanying colourful tones, melodies that glimmer and chords that melt into each other. -Katie Thomas Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Deena Abdelwahed - Jbal Rrsas (Infine Music)
> Infine MusicDeena Abdelwahed - Jbal Rrsas Tunisian artist Deena Abdelwahed has a predilection for pulling sonic touchpoints from the MENA region and dissolving them into dense, at times confrontational, productions. Case in point is opener "The Key To The Exit," her interpretation of the EDM-adjacent working class Egyptian genre mahraganat. It's a stunner of jagged synth lines that, in spite of its influences, feels like an electronic cousin to doom metal riffs. "Six As Oil" is just as intrepid. Abdelwahed slings around a fugue of subterranean drones, sustained sirens and tight snares to make for a deliciously anti-authoritarian rallying cry. -Whitney Wei Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Oceanic - Choral Feeling (Nous'klaer Audio)
> Nous'klaer AudioOceanic - Choral Feeling Why do we sing? It remains one of the great mysteries of human evolution. But to open your mouth, vibrate your vocal chords and produce musical tones through exalting air is at the core of being human. To do so in unison with others is a tradition that can be traced back time immemorial. On his debut album, Oceanic reimagines choral music for the 21st century, chopping, warping and distorting the voices of 30 friends to create Choral Feeling. Equal parts odd and profound, the vocals are often distorted beyond recognition, whether drawn out into haunting melodies or woven into drum patterns through syncopated rhythms. Oberman stays true to choral music's antiquated roots, producing a capacious vision of human connection, one that is mysterious, kaleidoscopic and fundamentally beautiful. -Bella Aquilina Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Fever Ray - Radical Romantics (Rabid Records)
> Rabid RecordsFever Ray - Radical Romantics Fever Ray's third album is probably the closest that Karin Dreijer's solo project has come to sounding like The Knife, and that's no bad thing. Across ten outrÃ© pop tracks that range from the political to the almost hilariously personal (like when they threaten their child's bully on "Even It Out"), Dreijer belts out some of their catchiest hooks over neon-hued production from Trent Reznor, NÃ­dia, Peder Mannerfelt and more. Where Dreijer's past work has revelled in alien unintelligibility, Radical Romantics puts its journey of self-discovery, emotion and passion out there for everyone to see, in all its pseudo-tropical, plastic-palm-tree and artificial beach glory. -Andrew Ryce Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Purelink - Signs (Peak Oil)
> Peak OilPurelink - Signs Signs, the stunning debut album from Chicago trio Purelink, occupies a nook all of its own in the broad realm of chill-out musicâ€”too feathery to be IDM, yet too alert to be ambient. This dubby netherworld, all gentle donks and silky earworms, evokes masters like Jan Jelinek and Lowtec. There's tension and dialogue. In short, don't be fooled into thinking this is background musicâ€”you'll be sitting bolt upright within minutes, marvelling at the wisps, wafts and occasional distant chime. It's all too beautiful to ignore. -Carlos Hawthorn Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

## [The Best Mixes of 2022](https://ra.co/features/4064)
Date: 2022-12-21T13:00:47.000Z

### Fact Mix 878 (Juba)
> JubaFact Mix 878 Zipline through a pastiche of Afro-electronic sounds, both domestic and diasporic. Juba, a British-Nigerian DJ who was recently featured in our newest episode of Soundtracking, cherrypicks from gqom, global club, techno and amapiano (the scene's consistent genre du jour) with an energetic panache more often reserved for dancers in front of the decks. The hour-and-a-half, which "ends on a rhythmic high," in the artistâ€™s own words, boasts cameo tracks from the veritable who's-who of the Black underground: DJ Lag, Anz, DJ Swisha, Griffit Vigo and Juba's close friend and promising talent Gafacci. At a most unexpected apotheosis, she tucks in a tasteful Avicii bootleg by Dee Traits as well as the Pearson Sound remix of Nick LeÃ³n's "Xtasis (feat. Dj Babatr)", AKA RA's track of the year. Both inclusions mirror two ubiquitous trends of 2022: the Latin-infused techno and pop edit predilections of the undergroundâ€”signifying the savviness of a selector in the know. All in all, the mix delivers an uppercut of infectious optimism in a new chapter defined by post-pandemic growing pains. â€”Whitney Wei

### fabric presents (Leon Vynehall)
> Leon Vynehallfabric presents Creative pressure is a very real thing for artists. How does one constantly evolve and meetâ€”even surpassâ€”their best work? Leon Vynehall seems to know the answer. Since 2018's powerful conceptual album Nothing Is Still, the UK musician has matured from a talented club producer into a storyteller par excellence, weaving original and compelling narratives through sound. 2019's RA-recommended DJ-Kicks was one of the best mixes that year. Now, in 2022, he's charted again. Like DJ-Kicks, fabric presents Leon Vynehall is all about dynamics, except this time the focus is on the club. You'd think that might be restrictive, but Vynehall is a master at finding common threads and energies in disparate musical worlds. Here, work by Mala, A2, Or:la, Ehua, Lady Blacktronika, Commodo, Hagan, Skee Mask and textures from so many other producers hang together in a smoky, soulful soup. The stitching is sublime, the music consistently excellent. At points, it's enough to take your breath away. â€”Carlos Hawthorn

### Live At Dimensions 2021 (Joe Delon)
> Joe DelonLive At Dimensions 2021 Hot take: Joe Delon likes dance music more than just about anyone. He tours all the time, but still finds time to write a regular newsletter about everything going on around him. As a DJ he exudes enthusiasm, playing groovy records that run the gamut from sleek contemporary tech house to old school Italo classics. This live recording from Dimensions captures his range perfectly: he starts low and slow, but just as things get a bit heady, he makes a U-turn with the outrageous vocal track "Adventure" by Eleanor and Shep Pettibone. From there, things dart between the cerebral and the cheesy. Vintage hip house gives way to G-funk-laced electro and acid before dissipating into celestial techno and old school rave. It's hard to imagine that even the security team wasn't losing it during this masterclass in Tisno. â€”Henry Ivy

### Accidental Meetings Podcast #72 (Yumi)
> YumiAccidental Meetings Podcast #72 New York DJ Yumi was probably a new name to a lot of people when they first heard this mix for UK platform Accidental Meetings, but anyone who did listen was probably left hungry for more. This 66-minute journey is the kind of unassuming but carefully built mix that lays eggs in your brain and hatches weeks later. Eventually, before you know it, you'll memorize every transition. Speaking of transitions, they're all remarkably seamless as Yumi blends together odd tracks at various tempos, gradually pulling off a 30 BPM change so impeccably that you barely notice it. Maybe RA staffer livwutang put it best in one of the SoundCloud comments: "dude [this] is fucking wildâ€¦ im glad im alive to hear this sound." â€”Andrew Ryce

### HÃ–R, January 13 2022 (D Dan)
> D DanHÃ–R, January 13 2022 Berlin-based DJ and Mala Junta resident D.Dan had a big year. Seemingly unknown during the recesses of the pandemic, he catapulted to international acclaim in the last 18 months, not only because of his unanticipated glut of speed-demon dance floor releasesâ€”all of which skirt the 150 BPM markâ€”but also because of his position at the helm of a refreshing new trend towards nimble, groovy techno. His HÃ–R Berlin mix from January this year perfectly encapsulates this style. Minimal yet replete with understated hooks, it layers psychedelic flurries of toms with tribal drums, house vocals and trancey melodic fills. Strategically moving from rhythmic tracks to deep peak-time riffs and back, he showcases here why he's become such a lauded underground tastemakerâ€”and a name to watch. â€”Chloe Lula

### Juanita's 063 (Quest?onmarq)
> Quest?onmarqJuanita's 063 "Spiraling" is a concept central to quest?onmarq's work. The New York-based DJ hosts a Lot Radio show of the same name, which sees them exploring a vast range of genres, from breaks to gqom, experimental and the harder regions of techno. They are not only technically skilled, but they have also been gifted with an insatiable curiosity about music, which allows them to play pretty much anything. For the 420-themed mix series, Juanita'sâ€”a platform on which DJs typically showcase the slower, sweet-tempered end of their collectionsâ€”quest?onmarq turned to hazy breaks. The windswept mix breezes past early works like Equinox's rattling "Taking Over" to contemporary jungle like "For The Headstrong" by Tim Reaper & Response. It's a tutorial in considered pacing, showcasing how to play fast while maintaining a subdued energy. â€”Kiana Mickles

### Untitled 909 117 (Toumba)
> ToumbaUntitled 909 117 Dubby, dark and loaded with gnarly bassweight, Toumba's Untitled 909 Podcast is a beastly mix that infuses halftime mutations with a sense of industrial-tinged dread. It's a perfect introduction to the Amman-based artist, whose style nods to Nervous Horizon, Hessle Audio (home to his latest EP) and Nyege Nyege Tapes. The up-and-coming producer shows off his love for tectonic basslines, footwork, hiphop, Middle East folk rhythms and hybrid club music from the developing world during this 80-minute session, which features South Korea's NET GALA gqom ensemble Phelimuncasi reworked into a glitchy bricolage, as well as Dua Saleh's delicate trap. Toumba plays for the dance floor, but he's not afraid to indulge in experimental atmospherics and distorted textures either. This sense of adventure makes this mix powerfulâ€”and a whole lot of fun. â€”Nyshka Chandran

### Honcho Podcast Series 108 (Kilopatrah Jones)
> Kilopatrah JonesHoncho Podcast Series 108 On September 15th, Haitian-born, Queens-based DJ Kilopatrah Jones wrote on Instagram: "When you think of house music, what do you think of? For me, it's house dancing, getting free on the beat with a friend [you] made on the dance floor." The 108th edition of the Honcho Podcast Series, delivered by Jones as a special Pride mix, encapsulates this feelingâ€”the joy of dancing, moving your body in sync with the kindred spirit on the dance floor you met just moments ago. Full of piano riffs, sensual vocals and a whole lot of groove, Kilopatrah Jones's Honcho offering is an hour of brilliant, ecstatic house that will make you dance until you sweat. â€”Katie Thomas

### BSU 066 (Truly Madly)
> Truly MadlyBSU 066 It's possible that Michael Joyce, AKA Truly Madly, is jumping between two or three different tracks in the first six minutes of his Butter Side Up Mix. It's also entirely possible that Joyce owns a 12-inch that somehow overlays sweeping chords with gurning rave stabs, rolling hand drums and short-circuiting electrical currents. The fact that we'll likely never know the answer is part of the fun (plus, it's not like we'd be able to find any of the records he plays anyways). This two-hour treasure trove of all things '90s sees Joyce in particularly bouncy and jubilant form. There are Latin-flavored rhythms, vintage NY vocals, and little bits of proper late night garage. The mixing is seamless without being showy, and Joyce keeps us on the edge of our seats the whole time, wondering what Shazam-breaking gem he'll reach for next. â€”H.I.

### Live From Sugar Hill (Jon K)
> Jon KLive From Sugar Hill Striking twists and turns are what make Live From Sugar Hill such a sharp and dynamic mix worthy of the physical media it was released on. Taken from Jon Kraus's set for Club Night Club at Brooklynâ€™s Sugar Hill Disco in September 2021, the cassette (released this year) niftily winds through bouts of grime, baile funk, gqom, ballroom and Jersey club like an alpine skier through a mogul field. Moments of more atmospheric, experimental tunes tease respite here and there, but Kraus knows the attention span of a dance floor all too well. On Live From Sugar Hill, a volley of breaks or a wall of kick drums is always only just around the corner. â€”Joseph Francis

## [The Best Tracks of 2022](https://ra.co/features/4098)
Date: 2022-12-20T15:45:42.000Z

### Nick LeÃ³n feat. DJ Babatr - Xtasis (TraTraTrax)
> TraTraTraxNick LeÃ³n feat. DJ Babatr - Xtasis If 2022 belongs to anyone, it's Nick LeÃ³n. The Miami producer is at the forefront of a new wave of 305-area artists who fuse together the city's unique tapestry of Hispanic culturesâ€”and its deep connections to Latin Americaâ€”with its robust dance music history. LeÃ³n specifically mixes influences from reggaeton and perreo into what is sometimes termed "Latin tribal techno," but whatever you want to call it, there's no denying the appeal of "Xtasis," the track most of us heard out on dance floors more than any other, by a country mile. "Xtasis," a collaboration with Venezuelan raptor house pioneer DJ Babatr, is a good example of the intercontinental cross-pollination happening within this scene. The percussion plays a trick, both four-on-the-floor and broken at the same time, at a chemically-enhanced pace with distant vocal wails that add a lysergic flair. But "Xtasis"â€”and its accompanying Pearson Sound and Doctor Jeep remixesâ€”really clicks with the old-school organ bassline that drops in at about the two-minute mark. It's something so simple, so familiar and, frankly, genius, that by the time the kick drum drops back in, the room should be in a frenzy. If it isn't, then you're probably in the wrong place. â€”Andrew Ryce Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Kelela - Washed Away (Warp Records)
> Warp RecordsKelela - Washed Away It's a special, and rare, moment when music drops and completely disrupts the flow of the internet. This was the case with Kelela's "Washed Away," her first single since she put out her acclaimed debut album Take Me Apart five years ago. During the hiatus, she looked inward and studied literature on misogynoir, Black labour and racial capitalism. Suffused in hazy pads and reverbed vocals that sound more like mantras than vocal refrains, "Washed Away" could be perceived as the release of all this collective pain. In a recent interview with Dazed, Kelela described the single as a "heart check-in," a song recorded to "send out a clear message to Black people, who are my core audience and who I intend this music for, that you n***as are worthy." Message received. â€” Kiana Mickles Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Rhyw - Honey Badger (Voam)
> VoamRhyw - Honey Badger On paper, "Honey Badger" shouldn't work. Its main drum line moves in and out of time with the impatience of a toddler hammering at a sequencer. The sole synthâ€”the closest the track has to a melodyâ€”is aggressively abrasive, as if it were made from a substance somewhere between quicksand and sandpaper. But I'll be damned if it isn't one of the catchiest tracks I've heard all year. Undeniably weird, but equally infectious, if you heard the track out (and odds are you did if you went to a festival this summer), it sent every crowd into full blown meltdown. Walking away from any set where it was deployed meant that there were punters with their heads still spinning trying to shriek along to those metallic snares. â€”Henry Ivry Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### A+A - Eternal September (AD 93)
> AD 93A+A - Eternal September Both times I heard "Eternal September" this summer I didn't know what it was. On each occasion, it was sunrise at a festival, those blissful hours when time seems to stand still as the sky changes from milky to glowing. It's an ideal track for those hazy moments, with swathes of lush organ chords and fluttering high notes that swoop around like birds with silk wings. When Avalon Emerson and Anunaku (AKA TSVI) shared the upcoming release online, Midland commented on the former's Instagram saying: "I have played these songs and had a nice time while doing so!" To which I thought: I have danced to these songs and had a nice time while doing so! â€”Katie Thomas Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### DJ Plead - Come Quick (Livity Sound)
> Livity SoundDJ Plead - Come Quick DJ Plead usually plays and produces slick, percussive zingers that meld traditional rhythms from the Middle East with high-tempo dance music. But on his second offering for Livity Sound, the Nervous Horizon core member switches out his frenzied pace for a more pared-down tone. Drums remain his core ingredient but the mood is more whimsical, making the record feel more like a score to a picnic in the park rather than a party. Despite its light-hearted nature, "Come Quick" is still loaded with sharp corners and jolting melodiesâ€”a true day to dusk record. â€”Nyshka Chandran Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Ahadadream - Spaceship (More Time)
> More TimeAhadadream - Spaceship Imagine Lunice, DJ Lag, Roska and Benga linking up for a recording session, and you start to get a sense of what "Spaceship" sounds like. On an EP filled with massive, celebratory tracks, Ahadadream's "Spaceship" was colossal. Every few bars it felt like he was shifting his reference points. What starts as a UK-funky-meets-gqom hybrid morphs into a dubstep throwback with its airy, descending melody. But then the xylophone chimes and upbeat snares capture the maximalism of TNGHT records. As the inadequacy of comparison should make clear, though, "Spaceship" is sui generis, announcing the arrival of a new torchbearer for all things big and bassy. â€”H.I. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Pariah - Caterpillar (Voam)
> VoamPariah - Caterpillar It's been a few years since Pariah put out any solo material (he's primarily active as one half of Karenn alongside Blawan). It's been even longer since he released dance music in his own right. Caterpillar, thenâ€”which came out in June on Voam, the label he runs with Blawanâ€”is an exciting interruption to this interlude. The hypnotic title track is capital-T techno, but it's heavily textured and nuanced, layering dense modular noodlings with a repeating guttural squelch that sounds more like an off-the-cuff live rip than the polished veneer of most of today's peak-time output. Flanged-out percussion, sizzling analog stabs and a spacey, Pole Group-like synth lead make it the ultimate selection for breaking open a late night set. â€”Chloe Lula Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### DJ Python - Angel (Incienso)

Within its sumptuous depths, there's an earnest, refreshingly unironic appeal to softening, unfolding and tenderness. â€”Whitney Wei Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Sally C - Downtown (Big Saldo's Chunkers)
> Big Saldo's ChunkersSally C - Downtown When Sally C released the second EP on her label Big Saldo's Chunkers back in April, the tracks had already been doing the rounds for almost a year. Most notable was "Downtown," a big, brash, in-your-face hip house roller that encapsulates what Sally C and her pals mean when they refer to a "chunker." This is functional, no-nonsense dance music that does exactly what it needs to: make your body want to move and groove. The vocal samples are textbookâ€”"Put the needle on the record" and "Do you want to dance?"â€”but they're a consummate companion for a tune designed to keep the party pumping, proof that less isn't always more. â€”K.T. ### Nikki Nair - Step 2 (n goes to infinity)
> n goes to infinityNikki Nair - Step 2 It's hard to imagine following dance music in 2022 and not hearing at least a handful of Nikki Nair tracks. The genre-hopping polyglot was everywhere with everyone, establishing a tight but all-over-the-place sound that blends electro, drum & bass, jungle and footwork. Case in point, "Step 2," which kicked off Nair's own label n goes to infinity. It starts out as hectic uptempo acid jungle track, before crescendoing into a halftime breakdown full of metallic skronks and other aural detritus. It's like walking from a FABRICLIVE night into a Daedalus set circa 2011, and then finishes off with a sprightly techno-jungle jig that feels completely of the momentâ€”an era that Nair is helping define with each new release. â€”A.R. ### GiGi FM - Manas (PST) (Bambe)
> BambeGiGi FM - Manas (PST) GiGi FM's first signed EP, Magnetite, supposedly holds "spiritually-charged techno mantras." While that may conjure a suite of vaguely spiritual motifs, we get none of that on this kinetic four-tracker. "Manas (PST)" embodies her aesthetic most distinctly, nodding subtly to the artist's sometimes collaborator, Donato Dozzy, with its deeply tribal percussive intro. The rest of the song is beguilingly simple; the propulsive kick-and-tom pattern continues uninterrupted under a single-note cowbell, never changing except for a brief drop about two-thirds in. GiGi FM, an alumnus of both the New York City Ballet and the Alvin Ailey Theatre, has said that the release is a testament to the ritualistic relationship between movement and music. This synergistic dynamic is elegantly elicited on the EP's A2, which is trance-inducingly danceable. â€”C.L. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Heavee - Sonic Warfare (Hyperdub)
> HyperdubHeavee - Sonic Warfare Heavee's Audio Assault was probably our favourite record on Hyperdub this year, with six tracks of inventive hybrid footwork that capture the label's ethos to a T. The best example was probably "Sonic Warfare"â€”which shares its name with Kode9's bookâ€”a blend of jabby footwork drums, eerie synths and a melodic motif that stutters and fades like electrical interference. â€”A.R. ### Physical Therapy - Emotional Rescue (Allergy Season)
> Allergy SeasonPhysical Therapy - Emotional Rescue Physical Therapy spent the last four years working diligently behind the scenes on his label, Allergy Season, as well as releasing records via a slew of his other aliases (Car Culture, DJ Overnite and Fatherhood, his project with Michael Magnan, to name a few). His last release under his original moniker, the 2015 EP Million Years Crushed, was deep, busy and granular. His latest album, Teardrops On My Garage, sounds like a subdued version of Physical Therapy. The garage-inspired chopped vocals are pitched-up and sweet, the melodies resonant and rich. My personal favourite, "Emotional Rescue," is an edit of Tru Faith's "Let The Beat Hit 'Em," that brightens the source material's original vocals with a sparkling melody and rollicking breaks. â€”K.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Isabella Lovestory - Exibisionista (Self-released)
> Self-releasedIsabella Lovestory - Exibisionista Reggaeton has been undergoing a renaissance in the electronic music world in recent years as artists like Rosa Pistola and the trio Sangra Nueva dissect dembow loops with a toolbox of global club rhythms, producing a kaleidoscope of sub-genres. Among those fringe styles is perreopop, and Isabella Lovestory is one of its leading faces. Here, her sultry lyrics and cam girl aesthetic take on an almost spooky air thanks to producers Nick LeÃ³n and Kamixlo who inject elements of dub and industrial into classic dancehall patterns. Transforming what would have been a regular pop song into a deadly dance floor weapon, the trio are a bright example of reggaeton's futuristic sector. â€”N.C. ### Eliza Rose & Interplanetary Criminal - B.O.T.A. (Rosebud Recordings)
> Rosebud RecordingsEliza Rose & Interplanetary Criminal - B.O.T.A. If, when one of SASS played "B.O.T.A." at around 8 AM on the Sunday morning of Love International, someone had said to me: "This tune's going to be #1 in the UK," I probably would have laughed and suggested it was time for bed. "B.O.T.A." was the summer's most ubiquitous tune, yes, but in my universe of clubs and festivals. Or so I thought. Skip to Friday, September 2nd, 2022, and Eliza Rose & Interplanetary Criminal had scored the UK's 1,400th #1, the first-ever for a woman British DJ. The percussion is simple and buoyant, the chords are warm and the vocal is catchy as fuck; "B.O.T.A." is a flawless summer bop. â€”K.T. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Nia Archives - Forbidden Feelingz (HIJINXX)
> HIJINXXNia Archives - Forbidden Feelingz British jungle revivalist Nia Archives began her astronomical year releasing a slew of hits du jour and ended it by winning a MOBO award in the ceremony's very first electronic/dance music category. ### Maara - Lezzies In A Jacuzzi (Radiant Love)
> Radiant LoveMaara - Lezzies In A Jacuzzi MontrÃ©al-based Maara has cultivated a fun and femme queer aesthetic that found an appropriate home on the Berlin label Radiant Love. ### Margaret Dygas - Butterfly Effect (Half Baked Records)
> Half Baked RecordsMargaret Dygas - Butterfly Effect The best minimal tracks are all about attention to detail, so it should come as no surprise that Margaret Dygas' "Butterfly Effect" clocks in at 9:09. The track is immersed in the micro world of details as she dilates and contracts looped conga drums, 909s, a creeping synthline and stormy pressure from her subs. Simple but effective, Dygas approaches these elements with a surgeon's precision as she moves them up and down in the mix. This was Dygas's first 12-inch in over half a decade, a welcome return of one of minimal's weirdos-in-chief. "Butterfly Effect" is a reminder of the strange sense of wonder that only the best minimal can create, where it feels like a loop could go on forever. â€”H.I. Listen: Soundcloud

### Utada Hikaru - Somewhere Near Marseilles (Epic Records)
> Epic RecordsUtada Hikaru - Somewhere Near Marseilles The year's greatest grown-and-sexy jam came out of an unlikely collaboration between the biggest J-pop star of all time and UK house producer Floating Points. Starting with the flicker of an acid line, "Somewhere Near Marseilles" unfolds over 11 minutes of exquisitely produced house, bobbing and glimmering in all the right places. Hikaru sings what feels like three different choruses in a mixture of English and Japanese, glamourously exhorting their lover to meet them in Marseilles as an in-between point between London and Paris. "Let's go fast, then go slow," they repeat over the constantly morphing instrumental track. It's a snippet of luxury and contentment that feels as lush as the song sounds, only improved by Hikaru's impeccable vocal performanceâ€”the way she sings, "I'm in London / You're in Paris" is both commanding and effortlessly cool. It's rare that the pleasures of pop and house music come together this well, a cosmopolitan adult contemporary jam made for the most amourous hours of the night. â€”A.R. Listen: Apple Music / Spotify

### Kush Jones - BX Bounce (Self-released)
> Self-releasedKush Jones - BX Bounce Growing up in New York, it's nearly impossible not to be inundated by different strains of music. The summer streets come alive with reggae and hip-hop; house music wafts in through FM radio or from the cracked window of your longtime neighbour. The vital life force and diversity of the city's sounds has coloured Kush Jones's discography over the years. He typically releases musicâ€”drawing from house, jungle, footwork and hip-hopâ€”independently at a fast clip. One of his many works from this year was 6 Days, an EP that was written in, you guessed it, six days. Within a record that shifts rapidly between house and juke, the highlight comes from the pensive pads, idle, honey-sweet melody and subtle percussion on opener "BX Bounce," embodying the very best of New York's intangible cultural heritage. â€”K.M. ### BeyoncÃ© - BREAK MY SOUL (Columbia Records)
> Columbia RecordsBeyoncÃ© - BREAK MY SOUL When BeyoncÃ© released the first single from her album Renaissance, souls weren't the only thing she broke. ### Peggy Gou - I Go (Soulwax Remix) (Gudu Records)
> Gudu RecordsPeggy Gou - I Go (Soulwax Remix) In the remix circuit, Soulwax hold a god-tier status. ### Shanti Celeste - Cutie (Hessle Audio)

### Skin On Skin - Burn Dem Bridges (FFRR)
> FFRRSkin On Skin - Burn Dem Bridges It seems unbelievable that it took someone this long to combine UK drill and techno as perfectly as this. It only took an Australian to do it. The whole thing sounds ready to blow at any minute.
