### Two Shell - home (Mainframe Audio)
> Mainframe AudioTwo Shell - home Impersonators showed up to their Boiler Room to play a pre-recorded set. Their first interview was taken off the internet in mere hours. Two Shell blew down the doors of 2022. And while some of their gimmicks may split opinions, "home" was a unifying track beloved by the dance music community. The single marked a new direction for the London duo, setting them apart from their peers by creating a completely singular sound where bubblegum pop meets UK bass. A frothing breakbeat at 160 BPM drives the track under its SOPHIE-reminiscent vocal, meanwhile its neon melodies burst like fireworks across the stereo spectrum. "home" will be remembered the way "Hyph Mango" was, marking the entrance into some unknown, but exciting era of UK club music. â€”H.I. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### KH - Looking At Your Pager (Self-released)
> Self-releasedKH - Looking At Your Pager In many ways, 2022 was a massive year for pop music. Underground club producers have long played out cheeky edits of '90s chart-toppers in their DJ sets, but it felt more prominent this year. Under his KH alias, Four Tet brilliantly reworks 3LW's "No More (Baby I'ma Do Right)," autotuning the original lispy vocals against a mean bass synth and a cooing, sparkling melody that feels straight out of a nursery rhyme. It's teen pop in holy matrimony with garage-like beats, plus a faint hint of dubstepâ€”a combination that only someone like Four Tet could pull off. â€”N.C. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### SHE Spells Doom - Bossano (All-centre)
> All-centreSHE Spells Doom - Bossano "Trying to see how African rhythms combine with techno for me is an experiment," said Wamya Tembo AKA SHE Spells Doom in an interview with the Zambian press. "[I like] seeing how far you can push it while still making people want to dance." His latest Afrobeat techno tune, "Bossano," toys with tension with the poise of a tightrope walker. Bursts of percussion ruffle the songâ€™s militant batida march, punctuating every bar of sci-fi synths while also teasing the ruckus of a street party throughout. Like an ellipsis, it brings you to the edge of your seatâ€”or rather, the tips of your toes. â€”Joseph Francis Listen: Bandcamp

### Paurro - GalavisiÃ³n (CÃ³meme)
> CÃ³memePaurro - GalavisiÃ³n This lean breakbeat house number serves as a definitive introduction to Paurro's dynamic sound. Combining UK garage and dub influences with psychedelic effects, "GalavisiÃ³n" is the kind of immersive groove that lends itself to escapist fantasies. Whether hearing it at home or at the club, it's easy to be transported into a lush dream state, one where pleasure and instinct hold more currency than logic. Paurro understands the power of skippy rhythms and low-end frequencies, letting them shine without indulging in too many choppy breaks. With its clear '90s influences and rollicking drums, "GalavisiÃ³n" is perfect for both peak time and after hours. â€”N.C. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Jennifer Loveless - Around The World (Butter Sessions)
> Butter SessionsJennifer Loveless - Around The World Galloping, loopy house abounds on this Melbourne producer's EP for home-turf label Butter Sessions. "Around The World" encapsulates the experiences of being a contemporary jetset flÃ¢neur, whose lackadaisical saunters are replaced with fast-paced globetrotting. This all seems immediately interpreted through glitchy, disembodied vocalsâ€”like filtered announcements over an intercomâ€”and roving, rotund basslines that seem to spend the entire seven-plus minutes attempting to catch up with themselves. Loveless's perspectives bounceâ€”quite literallyâ€”in palpable optimism. There's an dazzling array of life out there to see, and simply not enough time to see it all. â€”W.W. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Joy Orbison - Pinky Ring (Hinge Finger)
> Hinge FingerJoy Orbison - Pinky Ring No year-end list is complete without a Joy Orbison banger. If the South Londoner's talent is distilling pockets of the hardcore continuum into original bitesize chunks, "Pinky Ring" is a particularly golden nugget. Breaks, drum & bass, post-dubstep, possibly even electro? It's all in there, and yet the track feels anything but retro. Making the past sound fresh and futuristic could well be Joy Orbison's greatest skill. â€”Carlos Hawthorn Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

## [The Best Albums of 2022](https://ra.co/features/4077)
Date: 2022-12-15T09:30:58.000Z

### D. Tiffany & Roza Terenzi - Edge Of Innocence (Delicate Records)
> Delicate RecordsD. Tiffany & Roza Terenzi - Edge Of Innocence Electronic music is something of an ouroboros: sounds hark back to the past as trends recycle in a never-ending loop. The revival of genres like jungle and trance, among others, is proof positive, and the subject of many articles from cultural critics like Simon Reynolds and Mark Fisher. But there's a distinction to be made here. Some artists' chase of rose-tinted nostalgia is nothing more than empty clichÃ©, while others treat their return to a bygone era like a hero's journeyâ€”familiar, yet eclipsed by a new, fortified sensibility. D. Tiffany and Roza Terenzi achieve the ideal balance on their debut album, Edge Of Innocence. It offers a mÃ©lange of influences that run the hi-BPM gamut from electro to drum & bass without losing grip of the rippling, psychedelic groove at the core of everything this duo do. "Grains Of Sand" is a case in point, replete with synths that stab through a thicket of lumbering percussion, as is the fittingly named breakbeat bop "Redemption Arc," kitted out with all the sleek dynamism that emerges after a period of dark contemplation. By the end of Edge Of Innocence, you get the feeling that, though the duo are working with well-worn sounds, they've made them all their own. -Whitney Wei Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Hudson Mohawke - Cry Sugar (Warp Records)
> Warp RecordsHudson Mohawke - Cry Sugar Ross Birchard told us he only works up the nerve to make a solo album about every seven years, and this time it was worth the wait. Like a summary of his history of making weirdo IDM hip-hop and mainstream rap, Cry Sugar is the Glaswegian producer's most epic and wide-ranging LP, chock full of earwormy melodies, left-turn smackdowns and the symphonic pomp-and-circumstance that makes his work one of a kind. You can hear the last ten years of rap music refracted through Birchard's many-sided prism, which is often as funny as it is heavy as it is genius. Like the title implies, Cry Sugar careens from the depressed to the euphoric, each feeling pumped up to the scale of a Marvel movie. -Andrew Ryce Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Black Rave Culture - Black Rave Culture Vol. 2 (Black Rave Culture Records)
> Black Rave Culture RecordsBlack Rave Culture - Black Rave Culture Vol. 2 One of the most potent club weapons this year, the second offering from Washington DC supergroup Black Rave Culture is a motley crew of historical dance music styles from across the Black diaspora. Representing East Coast club, junglist rhythms and sunny house music with a truly holistic, cross-genre vision, the album teems with grit, unbridled energy and most importantly, power. From the baile funk underpinning "Never Left" to the '90s rave ethos of "Peace Plan," these tracks jump across styles effortlessly, and the fine-tuned production of members Amal, DJ Nativesun and James Bangura holds it all together. -Nyshka Chandran Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Kerri Chandler - Spaces And Places (Kaoz Theory)
> Kaoz TheoryKerri Chandler - Spaces And Places When it comes to making music, too many house and techno legends struggle to hold a candle to their younger selves. Not Kerri Chandler. The US house giant's latest album, Spaces And Places, is a three-hour epic stacked with the kind of tasty grooves and lush instrumentation we've all been gobbling up for 30 years. That its 24 tracks were mostly recorded inside the clubs and venues they pay homage to is both a remarkable feat and a quirky novelty. But it also speaks to something more profound: Chandler's global, enduring popularity. -Carlos Hawthorn Listen: Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Shygirl - Nymph (Because Music)
> Because MusicShygirl - Nymph As someone who's been listening to Shygirl since her breakthrough single, "Want More," it might have come as a surprise that the UK artist only released her debut album this year. But as the saying goes, good things take time. This record, aptly titled Nymphâ€”a play on words nodding to the album's whimsical nature and bawdy undertonesâ€”is Shygirl in full effect. The vocalist's hooks are tighter than ever, and the ever-expansive production spans pastoral pop, raunchy hip-hop, nostalgic Eurodance and the kind of saccharine hyperpop that trends on TikTok. More than just an excellent first LP, Nymph is a masterclass on collaboration, boasting production credits like Sega Bodega, Arca, Mura Masa and more, whose work melts effortlessly into Shygirl's one-of-a-kind style. -Kiana Mickles Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Carmen Villain - Only Love From Now On (Smalltown Supersound)
> Smalltown SupersoundCarmen Villain - Only Love From Now On Norwegian musician Carmen Villain has a preternatural ability to evoke a sense of cold, uneasy beauty. Her fourth album, Only Love From Now On, features ambient compositions that are often startling in their psychological intrigue. On "Future Memory," Villain expertly braids the sounds of cooing birds, humming flutes and irregular heartbeats to build suspense. "Liminal Space" conjures something similar, except with the inclusion of what seems like faint, irregular footsteps that stumble closer and further away. With its disarming atmospherics, Villain's fourth full-length has nothing to declareâ€”only quiet intensities to whisper. -W.W. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Waajeed - Memoirs Of Hi-Tech Jazz (Tresor)
> TresorWaajeed - Memoirs Of Hi-Tech Jazz Waajeed's debut on the prestigious Tresor label is a tribute to his hometown of Detroit, as a rousing tribute to both Black leisure and resistance against oppression. Conceptualised with a mini road trip around the Motor Cityâ€”specifically, from the his own Underground Music Academy to Belle Isleâ€”Memoirs Of Hi-Tech Jazz connects the dots between Detroit's rich musical traditions, encompassing jazz, deep house, minimal techno and marching band music. Even the title, a reference to the Underground Resistance subgroup Galaxy 2 Galaxy, reflects Detroit's storied sonic lineage. Proud, joyous and unapologetically local, Waajeed's love letter to his hometown is packed with velvety tones and lustrous chords that acknowledge the past and pave the way for the future. -N.C. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Marina Herlop - Pripyat (PAN)
> PANMarina Herlop - Pripyat Do you ever wonder how the world looks through a baby's eyes? Everything's new, and nothing makes sense. It's just one brilliant, ever-shifting mirage of colour and sound. Marina Herlop's third album, Pripyat, dazzles in a similar way. Where the Catalan artist's first two records showed off her expert piano playing and freeform, wordless vocals, Pripyat goes a step further into the unknown, patching together her classical training with dissonant electronics, and even weaving in an ancient Indian singing style called konnakol. The album might share its name with a ghost town, but Herlop's Pripyat is alive and bright with boundless imagination. -Joseph Francis Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Whatever The Weather - Whatever The Weather (Ghostly International)
> Ghostly InternationalWhatever The Weather - Whatever The Weather While Loraine James was working on her acclaimed 2021 LP Reflections, Loraine James filed away several songs that would ultimately make up her self-titled album, Whatever The Weather. On this meteorology-themed album, James did away with her club sound completely to write a series of ambient tracks distinguished by a worn, melancholy beauty. Here, intermittent rain is depicted as a flurry of lustrous synths, "14Â°C" is transformed into pensive arpeggiosâ€”the playfully jagged IDM she's revered forâ€”and sounds hiccup and stop-start across placid pads all over the LP. As an artist whose main project emphasises tricky beats over strikingly subdued terrain, her pivot to producing a downtempo recordâ€”and doing it so wellâ€”makes perfect sense. -K.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Soichi Terada - Asakusa Light (Rush Hour Music)
> Rush Hour MusicSoichi Terada - Asakusa Light Before this album, Japan's deep house don hadn't released a full-length in over 25 years. But it's abundantly clear that he hasn't lost his touch. There's a light, almost weightless, feel to this 11-track LP as the Tokyo composer and producer shows off his mastery of twinkling chords, spacey disco grooves, vintage synth patterns and video game sounds. Asakusa Light is relatively sparseâ€”even its big-room tracks like "Bamboo Fighter" feature relatively minimal arrangementsâ€”which allows his signature melodies to really shine. Graceful and flowing, this is an album that celebrates Terada's craft without feeling like a pastiche of his '90s discography. -N.C. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Marcel Dettmann - Fear Of Programming (Dekmantel)
> DekmantelMarcel Dettmann - Fear Of Programming Marcel Dettmann has always earned more attention for his DJing than his productions, but real fans know that his discography is a treasure trove of dark, detailed techno. Fear Of Programming, which lands on the all-purpose Dekmantel label, is something different: bright, vibrant, even a little funny (thanks to a vocal guest spot from fellow Berghain resident Ryan Elliott). Fear Of Programming is loaded with bold, bassy techno and arresting ambient passages. The real gold is in the hooks, which the spartan but still powerful production emphasizes like a gold frame around a masterpiece painting. It's the work of someone who knows techno inside-out, and knows how to make it compelling without going too far outside the box. -A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Hagan - Textures (Python Syndicate)
> Python SyndicateHagan - Textures With his debut album Textures, the South London DJ and producer Hagan celebrates the intersecting cultures close to his heart with rich, percussion-driven music. Organic flourishes (Ghanaian group chants, windswept koras and sunny guitar lines, to name a few) broaden the horizons of his historically urban sound palette, and he truly comes into his own as an all-around songwriter. With expertly curated vocal collaborations that reflect on family and faith, elements of gqom, amapiano and highlife, Textures is a transportive ode to the drumming continent, and the meaning of growing up both within and away from it. One moment you're in a lush, jungly landscape, the next you're hustling in the streets of Accra. Textures is more than just African dance music; it's a vibrant amalgamation of all the ingredients and influences that make Brendan Ware Hagan. -Emeka.Okonkwo. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Deepchord - Functional Designs (Soma Records)
> Soma RecordsDeepchord - Functional Designs All of Deepchord's records are goodâ€”all of themâ€”but a few are extra special. Functional Designs falls into this category. On first glance, it's not all that different from his countless other LPs. You've got gaseous dub techno beats echoing out into a painstakingly woven web of field recordings, sure. But the melodies are bigger, the drums are heavier and, most importantly, the tracks are separate, each with its own hook, its own uniquely staggered rhythm. Creating another noir-ish world of rainy-night ambiance, Functional Designs is one of Deepchord's most approachable and immersive LPs, gently refurbishing the rock solid formula of dub techno that the Detroit artist has relied on for decades. -A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### BjÃ¶rk - Fossora (One Little Independent)
> One Little IndependentBjÃ¶rk - Fossora BjÃ¶rk spent a lot of time dancing and thinking about mushrooms during lockdown. From thisâ€”a time she described to Pitchfork as her "fungus period"â€”came Fossora, the Icelandic vanguard's tenth album. BjÃ¶rk has been making music for over three decades now, and with each record she steps into mystical, uncharted territory, creating work which is ever more beguiling, more avant-garde and always, somehow, even more BjÃ¶rk. On Fossora, BjÃ¶rk sings with a sweeping gravitas over rich woodwinds and distorted gabber beats, the additional instrumentation dancing around her vocal as she muses on the circle of life, nature and her own late mother. Digging her fingers into the earth, BjÃ¶rk unknots tributaries of tangled roots, the crashing drum patterns and complex textures representing the stark, breathtaking topography of her homeland. -Katie Thomas Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Huerco S. - Plonk (Incensio)
> IncensioHuerco S. - Plonk From the first three seconds of Plonk, you know Huerco S. isn't doing the misty ambient thing again. Plucked strings ping in various directions, like popcorn exploding in a pan. Or, to be more accurate, like parts of a car yawning into gear. The automotive-inspired album, his first in six years, takes the American artist's sound to strange and innovative placesâ€”new sounds, unexpected textures, a first-ever vocal cameo. Isn't this what great artists do? Evolve, take left turns and, crucially, always deliver. -C.H. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Kode9 - Escapology (Hyperdub)
> HyperdubKode9 - Escapology Britain has never felt so close to collapse as it did in 2022. Between prime minister jockeying, mini-budgets and a volatile currency, Steven Goodman returned as Kode9 with a record that made the perfect accompaniment for the instability of the modern UK landscape. Written to accompany an experimental video game about Scotland leaving the union, Escapology operates along a dual axis, at once anxiousâ€”filled with eerie bits of sci-fi chatter and dense layers of swelling feedbackâ€”but also hopeful, at least when he turns to club tracks. "Uncoil," for example, is a pearl half-covered in sand somewhere between drum & bass and footwork, while "Cross The Gap" uses the negative space of dub to create something glimmering in the weight of the darkness around it. -Henry Ivy Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### DJ Lag - Meeting With The King (Ice Drop)
> Ice DropDJ Lag - Meeting With The King After years pushing the Durban scene and helping to make the sound a global sensation, anticipation for DJ Lag's debut album, Meeting With The King, was sky-high. He used the opportunity to champion his community instead of his own glory, creating a record that is collaborative from start to finish, with a majority focus on artists hailing from his home country of South Africa. Meeting With The King takes the moody sonics of the gqomâ€”born from township house partiesâ€”and makes it polished, opulent, even melodic, honouring the origins of the sound while adding catchy elements of amapiano, house, Afrotech and more. The title is boastful, but it's not wrongâ€”on Meeting With The King, DJ Lag stakes his claim and continues his ascent, taking his musical family along for the ride. -K.T. Listen: Apple Music / Spotify

### Schacke - Apocalyptic Decadence (Instruments Of Discipline)
> Instruments Of DisciplineSchacke - Apocalyptic Decadence Martin Schackeâ€”of "Kisloty People" fameâ€”has a knack for writing a hook. And almost every track of his debut album is decadent and addictive, loaded with catchy melodies. While the first half of the release gestures towards new beat and EBMâ€”"Miasma Of Filth" and "Tasteless Passion" both pull from a lineage of tinny 808s and mid-tempo industrialâ€”the second half offers grade-A techno-pop made for the the dance floor. Songs like "Body Type" and "Dungeon Crawler" are deceptively simple production-wise, but their repetitive choruses are the stuff that makes crossover hits. It's easy to imagine waiting for the train in the early morning hours after the rave, deliriously looping these brash three-note motifs again and again through your head. -Chloe Lula Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Ron Trent presents WARM - What Do The Stars Say To You (Night Time Stories)
> Night Time StoriesRon Trent presents WARM - What Do The Stars Say To You Ron Trent's WARM project captures it all in the name. As the Chicago house genius has advanced in his career, he's slowly luxuriated into a silky fusion sound that plucks from jazz, Balearic and soft rock in the spirit of carefully considered collaborators, like Texan psych-rock trio Khruangbin or Italian ambient composer Gigi Masin. "Admira," for instance, unfurls alongside loose bongo drums like a satisfying slow yawn after a midday slumber. Dappled sunlight patchworks "Flos Potentia," bound together by strumming bass guitar, and "On My Way Home," an earnest, jazzy sonic panacea for the oft-jaded ennui of modern music. After a long 11 years away from the format, Trent's latest album is a gorgeous evolution to behold. -W.W. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Jamal Moss - Thanks 4 The Tracks U Lost (Modern Love)
> Modern LoveJamal Moss - Thanks 4 The Tracks U Lost Jamal Moss, under his own name and as Hieroglyphic Being, is one of the defining forces in Chicago dance music. Whether he's making jacking house, experimental noise or blown-out techno, his work is defined by its sense of pure energy as he whips his machines into a frenzy. You'll find plenty of that rawness on his first LP for Modern Love, but where Thanks 4 The Tracks U Lost stands apart is in its surprising tenderness. Don't get me wrongâ€”the drums have plenty of edge, and Moss still pushes his synthesizers to their breaking pointsâ€”but the record is strikingly wistful, making for one of the most beautiful and tenderhearted of the many albums he's released. -H.I. Listen: Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Beast Nest - Sicko (Ratskin Records)
> Ratskin RecordsBeast Nest - Sicko In their work as an organiser and mediator, Beast Nest, AKA Sharmi Basu, believes that healing should be a communal effort. The process for making Sicko could be described as a collective effort. The LP was recorded in the years following 2016's tragic Ghost Ship fire, which ended up killing 36 people in an unlicensed warehouse. Sicko was an integral part of their healing journey as a survivor. There's palpable catharsis written into the energetic pulse of the album, which bleeds several genres into a satisfyingly cohesive mix that makes it difficult to discern where one song ends and another begins. Ambient sequences with knotty sections that twinkle and flutter turn into spaced out dub and then, somewhere along the way, listeners are transported to post-punk-leaning IDM. The songs sprawl out slowly, but capped at six tracks, the LP is actually quite short, emblematic of the slowness of grief and the unpredictable, dynamic moments that accompany it. -K.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Sudan Archives - Natural Brown Prom Queen (Stones Throw)
> Stones ThrowSudan Archives - Natural Brown Prom Queen Sudan Archives has always been a jewel of eccentricity. On her boundless second album, Natural Brown Prom Queen, rewind-worthy lyrics, maximalist experimentation (and what might be the most beat switches per song this year) coalesce into one remarkable document of self-empowerment and discovery. She embodies both her inner child and the person she's becoming ("I just wanna build LEGOs / I just wanna build, let's go"), all while keeping her signature sultriness dialed up to the max. Even putting her signature violin to the sidelines doesn't distract from her unique songwriting style. By the time she brings it home on the closer, "#513," she's delivered a defiant manifesto of hedonism, joy and femininity that raises the bar when it comes to post-genre pop music. -E.O. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Tanya Tagaq - Tongues (Six Shooter)
> Six ShooterTanya Tagaq - Tongues Amid an ongoing reckoning with Canada's own history of indigenous genocide, Inuk artist Tanya Tagaq's sixth album approaches this legacy with righteous fury and surprising tenderness. An extension of a book of verse of the same name, Tongues takes stock of decades of violence and its effects on the bodies and minds of a people, but also recognizes the power one can possess in even the most hopeless of circumstances. Combining her traditional throat singing with English words wielded like daggers, it's a disarming and personal listen that makes the historical personal, underlining the scale of a tragedy but also the resilience and power of those who have survived it. -A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Steffi - The Red Hunter (Candy Mountain)
> Candy MountainSteffi - The Red Hunter For the past five years, Steffi has been refining a style of electro that sits somewhere between bruising club weaponry and crystalline IDM sound design. The Red Hunter broadens this palette to include touches of hip-hop and contemporary club music, while keeping the nuts and bolts of classic Detroit in place. The result is the best full-length of her career. On The Red Hunter she creates a singular cosmology where strange, stuttering drum patterns emerge underneath windswept melodies and contracting basslines. But even as she moves into far-flung realms, she never loses sight of the club, and almost every single one of these tracks would make a head-turning standout in a DJ setâ€”which is what we've always come to Steffi for in the first place. -H.I. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Mall Grab - What I Breathe (Looking For Trouble)
> Looking For TroubleMall Grab - What I Breathe In just a few years, Mall Grab went from master of a niche to king of everything. His debut album is a Chemical Brothers-sized crossover behemoth, attacking every form of radio-friendly dance music, from big room house to pounding jungle. It's inspired by the sounds of his adopted home of London, and to his credit, it captures what makes the city so enduring in dance music history. A restless blend of sound system culture, American and European imports and the kind of vocal hooks you hear on BBC Radio 1â€”with a few vocal turns from the man himselfâ€”it transforms Mall Grab from bedroom producer into something closer to a pop star. -A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Dopplereffekt - Neurotelepathy (Leisure System)
> Leisure SystemDopplereffekt - Neurotelepathy Gerald Donald and To-Nhan Le Thi of Dopplerekkeft's second LP, like many 2022 albums, emerged from the toils of pandemic-induced isolation. The album's accompanying press text loftily asserts that its ten tracks are "considerations of the machine-human interface" and "transformative mental, psychological and transgenerational states." While some of these (perhaps overwrought) academic themes come through in the album's titles, it mostly sounds like the duo's mood piece-like electro fareâ€”in the best possible way. The tracks throughout Neurotelepathy aren't predictable arrangements made for club play. They're spare and considered, making exquisite use of spatial sound design, spectral percussion and arpeggiated melodies. Some songs, like "EEG," take more than a minute to settle into a more legible song structure, but their expertly rendered craftsmanship make them worth the wait. -C.L. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### 700 Bliss - Nothing To Declare (Hyperdub)
> Hyperdub700 Bliss - Nothing To Declare Spoken word and darbuka drums join in holy matrimony on this joint album from 700 Blissâ€”Philadelphia-based Moor Mother and DJ Haram. As the first full-length work from the duo after a series of collaborative EPs, Nothing To Declare sees the two artists claiming their matriarchal stake in electronic music. Haram's frenetic electronics speak in dialogue with Moor Mother's throaty vocals, delivered with a potent urgency. "Things ain't been the same since they put the lynch on us / water thicker than blood they convinced us," Ayewa opines. She's always been fearless in her delivery, but it's Muzeyyen's jagged productions that drive the point home. -W.W. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### ABADIR - Mutate (SVBKVLT)
> SVBKVLTABADIR - Mutate SVBKVLT became one of the most important club music labels by showcasing the vital Shanghai club scene, though the label's purview has expanded and only become more vibrant in the process. Case in point: this LP from Cairo producer ABADIR, which combines a freewheeling style of jungle with Arabic rhythms. This is music that sounds permanently out of breath, feeding off its own excitable energy. Inspired by maqsoum music and the humid bustle of the Egyptian capital, Mutate features impossibly funky beats shrouded in thick field recordings and melodies that hang in the air like smog. It's a vision of the kind of global club music that SVBKVLT has always championed, and one of the best records in a catalogue that constantly ups the ante for where club music can go next. -A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Batu - Opal (Timedance)
> TimedanceBatu - Opal According to the International Gem Society, an opal is "distinctly individual"â€”more so than any other gemstone. The 3D-rendered opal on the cover of Batu's debut album is just that: a unique kaleidoscope of colours. Icy blue, vibrant green and a hot, lava red contrast with the grey underside of the opal and the moody background. Examining Opal's cover gives a strong sense of the sounds within. 11 tracks of sharp (though sometimes soft), complex and unpredictable electronic sculptures, a world of intricate sound design that Batu said he intended to feel vivid and transportive. Like so many LPs released this year, Opal is a lockdown record, made when Batu was in an introspective and contemplative state of mind, experimenting with moving away from club 12-inches and into a space more vulnerable and experimental. -K.T. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### FKA twigs - Caprisongs (Young)
> YoungFKA twigs - Caprisongs Caprisongs was one of the first RA Recommends of the year, and it was no surprise to many of us that it lingered long enough in our minds to make this end of year list. The album is brighter than anything we'd heard from twigs before. Gone is the operatic austerity of MAGDALENE. Instead, Caprisongs is a pop album with a capital P. The album mines from Afrobeats, grime, baile funk and R&B. It also sources from her personal life via snippets of conversations she recorded with loved ones. The immersive world she creates here deals with insecurity, "stupid boys" and friendship, but it's also celebratory. The world had opened up, after all. Twigs might have had a cry now and then, but at least she was doing it on the dance floor in the album's first single, "Tears In The Club.". As phenomenal as Caprisongs is, it's somehow even more impressive because it was pulled off with a welcome sense of humour. The album title, for example, is inspired by astrologyâ€”her "stubborn Caprisun ass telling her to work through the pain." Listeners can even eavesdrop on an astrological reading by the album's close. Sometimes, a little stubbornness is worth it. -K.M. Listen: Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

## [The Best Mixes of 2021](https://ra.co/features/3952)
Date: 2021-12-22T13:00:01.000Z

### Presents: Eargoggles (Theo Parrish)
> Theo ParrishPresents: Eargoggles "There are no genres. Nope, there's none. It's all tune for tune," Theo Parrish said outside the familiar NTS stall in Dalston's Gillett Square. And he doesn't just talk to talk. Many DJs claim to play across genres, but there are "many DJs" and then there is Theo Parrish. Over the past few years, the historically private artist has given fans a near-unprecedented view into his creative mind, first with the lengthy and unclassifiable sonic essay-meets-radio drama We Are All Georgeous Monsterss, and then this year with a six-and-a-half hour mix for NTS called "Eargoggles." (Parrish also dropped another six-hour mix close to press time.) Eargoggles is a marathon celebration of the infinite diversity of Black music, spanning from hard bop to hip-hop, searing psych rock to roots reggae. No random grab bag, this is a grand narrative and the revelation of a modern canon of soul with appearances by James Brown, The Congos and D'Angelo. The mix is an education unto itselfâ€”around hour five Parrish drops "Jazz Cats Part 1," a cut consisting of Madlib breathlessly laying out his key jazz influencesâ€”yet it's also a generous statement of purpose bursting with joy and urgency. 25 years into his career, Parrish gives us an exhaustive guide to the music that makes him tick, that has informed his own enduring classics. But why now? He explains the gravity of his convictions in the final moment of the magisterial "Eargoggles" mix: I'm hoping that at some point during this... After you've had a ride, a musical ride with me, that you take a moment to consider the troubles that you have, and consider that you're lucky to have them. Even if it doesn't affect you demographically, you should seriously consider the fact that there's an urgency that should be lived, in respect for those that get taken from us early under the guise of 'serve and protect.' So let's survive together. But let's remember them together as well. Let's not forget how we treat each other when the music's playing and how things change when the lights go on and we all go back to the rest of our lives. Let's go back with a little more urgency and care for the fellow man. Let's give a damn a little bit. And if we can do that, we got a better place.â€”Matt McDermott

### BIS Radio Show #1085 (Tim Sweeney)
> Tim SweeneyBIS Radio Show #1085 Over the past 21 years, Tim Sweeney never missed a week on the WNYU airwaves, hosting generations of DJs in the college station's basement studios. Beats In Space became iconic over this decades-long stretch, with Sweeney joining a grand tradition of New York radio DJs that also includes Shep Pettibone, Tony Humphries, Stretch and Bobbito, who held sway and influence far beyond the five boroughs. Though Sweeney has since brought Beats In Space back via Apple Music, last March he unexpectedly wrapped up his term on WNYU with episode #1085. Listeners flooded the comment section on a YouTube livestream after the news broke, thanking him for his illustrious tenure. For the finale, Sweeney played Beats In Space classics that highlighted the show's connection to the history of New York City dance music, dropping in an eclectic selection from Alicia Myers, Chaz Jankel and Arnold Jarvis. Full of hope, the two-and-a-half hours imparts a heartfelt message of gratitude to dedicated listeners and guests alike.â€”M.M.

### borshch mix 26 (Crystallmess)
> Crystallmessborshch mix 26 We're in the age of the polymath musician, and Crystallmess is the epitome. The French-born Ivorian and Guadeloupean DJ, producer and mixed media artist (who has shown her work at the Centre Pompidou and the Geneva Biennale, as well as playing at hallowed institutions like Berghain), has steadily made her way into the art and electronic music vanguards simultaneously. For her entry in the Borshch Magazine series, Crystallmess uses the mix format to express the social whiplash of lockdowns and reopenings, all the while showing off her agile genre-agnosticism. She includes edits of beloved Lil Wayne and Aaliyah tracks, blown-out jungle sampling "Ready or Not" by The Fugees, swirled with a heavy-handed dose of otherworldly ambient to evoke the expansive solitude of pandemic isolation.â€”Whitney Wei

### Lost In Dreams (Irini)
> IriniLost In Dreams Lost In Dreams was another entry in the growing SoundCloud archive of Traumprinz's resplendent multiverse. Irini, one of the elusive artist's many pseudonyms, trots out over three hours worth of new material, charting a comprehensive course in sensitive dance music from someone who creates at a relentless pace. Unlike some of his other aliases, irini doesn't have a unique sound in the way that DJ Healer or the Prince Of Denmark do, but that's also what makes this mix so rewarding. The dub techno, UK garage, even minimal house productions spring forth from an enigmatic source, keeping the intrigue of listening alive. Now it's just a matter of waiting for the inevitable vinyl releases.â€”Henry Ivry

### ETCHED 003 (Live Set) (Wata Igarashi)
> Wata IgarashiETCHED 003 (Live Set) A live set from techno's undisputed master of arpeggios, Wata Igarashi, is a special thing no matter where it takes place: dark basements orâ€”why notâ€”the Nobeyama Radio Observatory. Located in Yatsugatake, Japan, the observatory has been a hub for radio astronomy research since 1982. Its imposing rows of satellites and telescopes, set against a beautiful landscape, provide an almost too-good-to-be-true backdrop for Igarashi's cosmic, otherworldly sound. Beautifully shot on video by ETCHED (an audiovisual project showcasing domestic artists), the set plunges into the outer reaches of Igarashi's unmistakable productions, reworking previous records and some unreleased material into an hour-long trip that remains one of 2021's most memorable techno sets.â€”Richard Akingbehin

### 100% UNRELEASED OSSX MIX (OSSX)
> OSSX100% UNRELEASED OSSX MIX For many of us, New Jersey group OSSX's "Split Wig" on Allergy Season was one of the year's indisputable anthems. And the only thing better than just one track is a whole hour of exclusive material. 100% UNRELEASED OSSX is a goldmine for anyone into big drums and even bigger melodies (with a "Split Wig" appearance early on). There's a light-footed touch to breakbeats, plus some nimble choppage and a parade of brazen, uplifting edits that sample a tongue-in-cheek gamut: Modjo to Janet Jackson to September's Eurodance hit "Cry For You." It's that "Are they really doing this? Sampling that?" swagger that cinches this mix as one of our endlessly replayable favorites this past year.â€”Andrew Ryce

### TTT Mixtape (Josey Rebelle)
> Josey RebelleTTT Mixtape Josey Rebelle couldâ€”and probably will, honestlyâ€”make this list every year for the foreseeable future, and it would be nothing short of deserved. The UK DJ is one of the best selectors on the planet, with a record digger's taste but a party-rocker's ear. She'll play obscure records, sure, but they'll never feel obscure. Her mix, first released as a very limited tape on The Trilogy Tapes in April, is a perfect example of this, stitching together slow jams, weirdo techno and even snippets of radio play, with a darker edge than what we're used to from some of Rebelle's recent mixes. The eventual streaming upload of the mix was greeted with the fervor of an album drop, and for good reason: this TTT Mix strums the eclectic but intuitive thread thatâ€™s tied through all of her sets. The only flaw is that it isn't twice as long.â€”A.R.

### GHOSTCAST 014 (DESYN)
> DESYNGHOSTCAST 014 In certain circles, the name Desyn Masielo commands a kind of reverence, and the London lifer has been blending the finest never-on-YouTube Discogs gems for the past two decades. Here, Masiello flaunts those deep-digging DJ tendencies with wild abandon. Ghostcast14, recorded live at Hoppetosse, is a good intro to what he can achieve when he goes for the jugular from the very beginning. We start in medias res with UK garage basslines, but his masterful pacing and mixing means that before we know it, we're zipping through starry rave, acidic electro, '90s house and just about everything else under the sun. For us mortal trainspotters, the only thing worse than having missed this party is that we'll likely never know what any of these records are.â€”H.I.

### Daisychain 154 (DJ Fart In The Club)
> DJ Fart In The ClubDaisychain 154 DJ Fart In The Club (AKA Soyoon Choi) certainly has an offbeat sense of humor, but when it comes to their DJ sets, they're entirely straight-faced. Even though this set came in at the tail end of last year, it still banged all the way through into 2021. The Berlin artist unleashes a sticky hour-and-a-half of acid-tinged wobblers, prog house and freaky trance for the Chicago-based, women and non-binary focused podcast series Daisychain. In the knottier sections, Choi takes listeners on a jaunt full of vertiginous peaks and deep valleys by roving into spiraling wormholes of techno, garage and preternatural club music.â€”Kiana Mickles

### sit on my interface (1/2) (CCL)
> CCLsit on my interface (1/2) In the weeds of the first 20 minutes of CCL's sit on my interface mix, it's easy to presume that this is a fully ambient offering. But that would be a hasty judgement, as once it approaches the one-hour mark, the energy intensifies with such careful, gradual restraint that even the active listener might wonder how they even got to this point. Sure enough, the mix ultimately reaches a dark, slinky plateau with a bubbling, percussive roller and then rockets off from there. "sit on my interface (2/2)" can't arrive soon enough.â€”K.M.

## [The Best Tracks of 2021](https://ra.co/features/3951)
Date: 2021-12-21T00:47:34.000Z

### Overmono - So U Kno (Poly Kicks)
> Poly KicksOvermono - So U Kno 2021 felt like Overmono's breakthrough year. Each new release of theirs seemed to outdo the last, from the euphoric rave of "Pieces Of 8" to their pitch-perfect fabric mix to the peppy garage of "Diamond Cut" (one of the major highlights from what was arguably the year's best Essential Mix). But it was "So U Kno," released not on the duo's usual home of XL Recordings but on their own, smaller Poly Kicks imprint, that made it into what felt like every DJ set of the post-reopening world. Like so much of Overmono's recent work, there's a whiff of a bygone, post-dubstep era to "So U Know." Built around an unforgettable vocal chop, "So U Kno" is the kind of track that elicits cheers from a dance floor the minute the DJ starts to mix it in. It has one of those in-between beatsâ€”kind of house, kind of 2-step, kind of technoâ€”and a thrill-ride of a breakdown. Encapsulating the frenzied, overjoyed vibe of the summer's post-reopening clubbing with a hint of wistful nostalgia, "So U Kno" perfectly sums up this year's excitement and radical ups and downs.â€”Andrew Ryce Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Billie Eilish - Oxytocin (Interscope Records)
> Interscope RecordsBillie Eilish - Oxytocin Hidden in the middle of Billie Eilish's intimate, often confessional singer-songwriter album is one of the year's biggest, loudest club tracks: the pop megastar's equivalent of Nine Inch Nails' "Closer." "Cause I like to do things God wouldn't approve of / If she saw us," Eilish whispers over a clanging, outsized beat. "Oxytocin" takes the tactile, goosebump-inducing approach of Eilish's other records and blows it up to a macro scale. It's the sound of being cornered in the club, pushed towards the speaker until all you can hear are the kick drums.â€”A.R. Listen: Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Elvin T - Get Close (Regraded)
> RegradedElvin T - Get Close Throw a jacking house rhythm underneath the right vocal and soaring strings, and you've found yourself a tried and true way to excite a dance floor. There is nothing radical or even innovative about Elvin T's "Get Close," which hews closely to this time-honored formula, but there doesn't need to be. The Philadelphia producer laced together the perfect combination of driving percussion, vocals, a glossy string loop and a couple of breakdowns. Released as the final record on Midland's Regraded label at the start of summer, the track's timing was also fortuitous as dance floors got busier over the summer. â€”Henry Ivry Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### PinkPantheress - Just for me (Parlophone)
> ParlophonePinkPantheress - Just for me TikTok made PinkPantheress one of the year's defining pop stars. She became a musical sensation just for releasing snippets of songs on the video app before the full versions appeared on streaming services. Anyone who hadn't heard of PinkPantheress probably did when she finally released the music video for "Just for me," an early '00s-inspired visual depicting her on a studio stage with a sulky crew of emo kids. The Mura Masa co-produced track nodded to garage and early '00s pop-rock, perfectly encapsulating "new nostalgic," a term PinkPantheress uses to describe her own sound. If the lyricsâ€”which follow a stalker's infatuation with a crushâ€”are unsettling, it's intentional. The song was inspired by the obsessive themes that run through Eminem's "Stan," and is more a practice in dramatic storytelling than a portrayal of real-life events. Much like the rest of her catalog, which is tailor-made for bright-eyed Gen Z TikTokers with short attention spans and a love for danceable, snappy hooks, "Just for me" hovers around two minutes in lengthâ€”just long enough to make you want to press rewind and hear it all over again.â€”Kiana Mickles Listen: Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Planetary Assault Systems - Say It Loud (Token)
> TokenPlanetary Assault Systems - Say It Loud As Planetary Assault Systems, Luke Slater makes huge, no-bullshit techno. There's plenty of technical wizardry going on, sure, but you know what to expect: thunderdome kick drums and synths that sound like sonar pings. Enter "Say It Loud," the highlight from Belgian label Token's 100th release, which subverts Slater's historical output with a goofy sound that matches its goofy title (right down to the deadpan vocal repeating "say it loud"). Refreshing and zippy, it sounds a bit like Slater poking fun at the current crop of big-time techno producers, then beating them at their own game with a track that's over-the-top, funky and absolutely monstrous.â€”A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Soundcloud / Spotify / Soundcloud

### tondiue - Painted Creature (secondnature)
> secondnaturetondiue - Painted Creature tondiue's debut packed an album's worth of ideas into an EP of techno that explores the outer reaches of the genre, specifically slowed-down breakbeats and tunneling, Wata Igarashi-style arpeggio workouts. "Painted Creature" falls somewhere between these styles. What starts out as a loose hand percussion workout laced with clipped, unnerving vocal samples before the breakdown turns it into a tripped-out big room techno cut that could stand up with the best of 'em. It's just one of many highlights on a techno EP that sticks with us like few others have this year.â€”A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Nia Archives - Headz Gone West (HIJINXX)
> HIJINXXNia Archives - Headz Gone West Drum & bass was all over pop and R&B this year, though it rarely sounded as heavy and convincing as it did on Nia Archives' Headz Gone West, where the London singer peppers expert breakbeat chop-ups with jazzy vocal runs. The title track is an easy highlight, packing a whole lot into just over two minutes as Nia Archives sings about her anxiety, her wandering mind and getting "high just to pass the time" over beats that crest and wane like lashing ocean waves.â€”A.R. Listen: Apple Music / Spotify / SoundCloud

### Stef Mendesidis - Stalker (Klockworks)
> KlockworksStef Mendesidis - Stalker Like his first EP for Ben Klock's label in 2019, Greek born, Kyiv-based producer Stef Mendesidis' Klockworks 33 delivered four irresistibly catchy, full-pelt techno tracks when it came out in October. "Stalker" is by far the most elegant cut of the batch, threading delicate hats and a single, sonorous pad in and out of an arpeggiated bassline that opens and closes over the course of five-and-a-half minutes. Like Klock, Mendesidis has mastered the art of functional peak-time techno that feels anthemic despite its simplicity.â€”Chloe Lula Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Logic1000 - I Won't Forget (Therapy)
> TherapyLogic1000 - I Won't Forget Logic1000's "I Won't Forget" had unfortunate timing, landing at the very beginning of the year when most of the world was still shut down. It has all the makings of a festival hit with its deliciously heavy slo-mo breakbeat and moody synths that come in halfway through the track, like tears blurring your peripheral version. Just when you think you have the track pegged down, everything falls away to reveal a truly evil-sounding Reese bassline that pushes it to another level. In all, it's a wonderful, canny fusion of UK dance music styles from a talented Australian producer.â€”A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### John Glacier - If Anything (PLZ Make It Ruins)
> PLZ Make It RuinsJohn Glacier - If Anything "If Anything" producer and Frank Ocean collaborator Vegyn originally found John Glacier's music on SoundCloud, but the London-based artists quickly realized they'd met before, gravitating towards each other to chat at the back of parties. It's appropriate, then, that "If Anything," the opening salvo from Glacier's debut album, brims with the swooning disorientation of a big night out. Over a triumphant, boom bap-influenced beat, Glacier raps in impressionistic turns of phrase: "Starlight, dancin' in the moon / I'm ravin' rabbit, I'm on shroom." "If Anything" introduces a visionary and arty MC with an instantly recognizable banger.â€”Matt McDermott Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### KG - Koko feat. Mista Silva (Black Acre)
> Black AcreKG - Koko feat. Mista Silva Karen Nyame KG earned the nickname "The Goddess of Rhythm" for her intricate UK funky productions, but the British-Ghanaian artist's biggest track to date came when she stepped up to the mic. "Koko" was an immediate summer hit that benefited from a magpie's approach to recent African dance music innovations. In just under three minutes, Nyame mixes airy highlife guitar, Afrobeats and amapiano. Her vocal, meanwhile, is unapologetically carnal: "Don't waste my time / I wanna bust down, bust down / Go rounds, go rounds / lights out, lights out." Modern dance music often feels like it's designed for some airless dungeon. By comparison, "Koko" feels like sex on the beach.â€”M.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Koreless - Joy Squad (Young)
> YoungKoreless - Joy Squad It's safe to say the Welsh producer Koreless got a little in his head while working on his debut album, which was almost a decade in the making. The time enabled him to do endless revisions and embark on creative soul-searching that eventually paid off. The LP's ten tracks display extraordinary sonic detail and inventiveness. "Joy Squad" sticks out as a granular reimagining of a big room anthem. Chopped-up shards of melody and vocals combine with cinematic strings in a kaleidoscopic funhouse of a track that would be overwhelming if it wasn't so concise.â€”M.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Maxwell Sterling - Decay Time (AD 93)
> AD 93Maxwell Sterling - Decay Time Turn Of Phrase reveals Maxwell Sterling as a rare talent, remarkably adept in both electronic sound design and orchestral arrangement. While the title track flabbergasts with a mix of furious classical runs and Autechre-level sound processing, the brief "Decay Time" is the record's centrepiece. While the drums clearly hearken back to IDM's '90s heyday, the track's plinking synth bass and strings converge to evoke a sense of deep lament. This difficult balance of head-spinning programming and lilting emotionality recalls classics within the genre like Aphex Twin's "Flim."â€”M.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / SoundCloud

### DJ Black Low & Kapzela feat. Licy Jay & MLG - Emonate Oe Bethela D Vosho (Awesome Tapes From Africa)
> Awesome Tapes From AfricaDJ Black Low & Kapzela feat. Licy Jay & MLG - Emonate Oe Bethela D Vosho Considering house and techno are inventions of the African diaspora, it feels like poetic justice that some of the most innovative changes happening in modern electronic music are emerging from the continent. In recent years, amapiano's log drum grooves have sprung from Gauteng townships to clubs around the world. DJ Black Low, the 20-year-old amapiano producer signed to Awesome Tapes From Africa, brought an experimental edge to the young genre on his 2021 album, Uwami. On "Emonate Oe Bethela D Vosho," Black Low works with Kapzela and the MCs Licy Jay & MLG to forge a groove that's as urgent as it is inviting.â€”M.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Currency Audio - Modus Choperandi (Exit Records)
> Exit RecordsCurrency Audio - Modus Choperandi Photek's 1997 hit "Modus Operandi" brought together the best parts of trip-hop, jazz, jungle and hip-hop. Consisting mostly of drums and atmospheric effects, it redefined drum & bass and celebrated the art of percussion itself. On his entirely improvised tribute to the track, Rajeev Maddela pulled from Photek's beat science, fusing recreated '90s breakbeats with live drumming and his own signature sound. Maddela's razor-sharp instrumentationâ€”accentuated by ghostly padsâ€”brought new depths to jazzy drum & bass this year.â€”Nyshka Chandran Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Max Watts - Hipnautic (Self-released)
> Self-releasedMax Watts - Hipnautic Only recently exiting his teenage years, rising techno prodigy Max Watts has released some of the freshest renditions of Detroit techno this year. His self-described "post-Detroit" style is unique for its raw, improvisational flow, channeling the freewheeling energy of Midwestern techno greats like Underground Resistance, Claude Young and DJ Rush. Watts's sincere investment in the emotion and groove behind his music makes way for some of the purest and most exuberant modern techno around. One of the hits off April's MW002 EP, "Hipnautic," was a favorite for its lurching percussion, drunken, loopy melody and dissipating hi-hats. Watts knows how to build and retract momentum in all the right places.â€”K.M. Listen: Bandcamp

### Bapari - Daybreak (Self-released)
> Self-releasedBapari - Daybreak The "Ha" stab, a rousing "crash" sample that typically falls on the 4, is to ballroom music as vocal chops are to Jersey club. They're classic hallmarks of the genresâ€”once you hear them, it's difficult to mistake what you're listening to. The key elements of ballroom music, a style intrinsically tied to its dance culture, have understandably caught the eye of numerous club producers in recent years. And Bapari, a Brooklyn-based artist whose music draws from all manner of East Coast club styles, is one of the latest to be inspired. On the title track of their Daybreak EP, the "Ha" stab, rather than assuming its traditional role of accentuating the melody, becomes the melody across a frenzy of playful, whip-sawing crashes. Offering some respite, Bapari skillfully tempered the track with plenty of space and the occasional murmuring vocal that floats off into the ether.â€”K.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Ayesha - Potential Energy (Scuffed Recordings)
> Scuffed RecordingsAyesha - Potential Energy There are a few simple but essential ingredients needed to make the perfect Ayesha track: nimble percussion, intoxicatingly psychedelic melodies and plenty of focus on the low-end. "Potential Energy" nails all three. The first gobsmacking moment arrives with synths that ripple with the intensity of an ultraviolet wave. Then the first acid lead slithers in, a portent of the brilliance to come: a rip-roaring showcase of lumbering breakbeats and off-kilter synths, replete with Saturday morning cartoon sound effects. It's a certified energy-boosting weapon for DJs on the late-late shift.â€”K.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### A.G - always, you (Self-released)
> Self-releasedA.G - always, you Breakout artist A.G not only has a penchant for creating robust, propulsive sounds, but she's got the bravura to back it up. Last year, the East London native postedMixmag's review of her August Discwoman selections, including the tongue-in-cheek caption "heavy-bodied means I'm thick." It's quips like theseâ€”and all the offerings on her donotdisturb EPâ€”that shirk the stereotype of the introverted bedroom producer. In standout track "always, you," A.G demonstrates a magisterial command of UK drill, directing staccato hi-hats and pitched-up vocal samples to clamber over heavy bass uppercuts with a tenacity that matches her personality. When they say "confidence is everything," take this example as a case in point.â€”Whitney Wei Listen: Bandcamp / Spotify

### UNIIQU3 - Microdosing (Local Action)
> Local ActionUNIIQU3 - Microdosing When Jersey club royalty holds court, the world pays attention. Cherise Gray, otherwise known as UNIIQU3, has been championing the 135 BPM club music of her Newark home on the international stage for the better part of a decade, and this year she really came into her own. "Microdosing," the lead single off her Heartbeats EP, delves into house, rap and four-to-the-floor big room beats: "Took a tab and tripped / Drown in it / Fall into my abyss / The sticky icky wet wet." Gray details a lysergic wet dream that climaxes at peak time on the dance floor. Synth-heavy and oozing with confidence, the track holds the hip-swinging sashay of a lip glossed, sugar-coated seductionâ€”without the predictable box spring squeaks.â€”W.W. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Blawan - Under Belly (XL Recordings)
> XL RecordingsBlawan - Under Belly "Under Belly" has a little bit of everything that we've come to love about Jamie Roberts (AKA Blawan), from his early Hessle Audio days to his tech-wiz modular techno era. It also perfectly captures what has always been refreshing about his music: He never takes himself too seriously. With its groovy swing and ghost choir motif, "Under Belly" sounds like the most fun he's ever had on record. By looking back to his early days as an honorary post-dubstep protege, Roberts proves he can return to the past while still firmly developing his sound.â€”H.I. ### Anz - Unravel In The Designated Zone (OTMI)
> OTMIAnz - Unravel In The Designated Zone Anz broke out in 2020, but her career has taken off in 2021. Between her yearly all-originals mixes and an increasingly hectic DJing and radio schedule, the Manchester artist knocked out two of the year's most exciting celebrations of UK club music. While her Ninja Tune debut All Hours was a masterclass in fusing pop with electro, UK garage and jungle, "Unravel In The Designated Zone" remains the year's high water mark. It's a bit more understated, but it still feels like an instant classic from the moment the song's lead synth begins howling over her signature off-kilter percussion.â€”H.I. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / SoundCloud

### SHE Spells Doom - Rudnick (All Centre)
> All CentreSHE Spells Doom - Rudnick There was plenty of genre-bending club music released this year, but Zambia-based SHE Spells Doom's release for All Centre was a hybrid like no other. The three-track EP showcased an impressive repertoire, crossing from UK funky to Afro house. But it was the confident swagger of "Rudnick" that kept clocking up the re-listens. The track's synth work has the technicolor polish of contemporary UK techno set over the stuttering swagger of '00s hip-hop percussion. Named for the sci-fi Oedipus anti-hero in the movie Heavy Metal, the track surpasses its namesake, creating a sense of noirish anxiety without losing sight of the funk.â€”H.I. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Maara - The Forbidden Plum (Isla)
> IslaMaara - The Forbidden Plum 2021 saw a new sound emanating from Canada's dance music underground led by labels like Planet Euphorique, Isla and Acting Press. No one captured this better than Maara and her sexually charged, trance-flecked take on techno and electro. Across two breakout EPs, there was a je ne sais quoi to the Montreal producer's often illicit but lighthearted tracks. Her best song, "The Forbidden Plum" from her Potion Activated EP, had elements of both. Dark, pulsing synth bleeps, a twisted metallic bassline and a prog house throwback gated vocal sit under a repeated refrain: "Want it so badly." "The Forbidden Plum" is a cocktail of hedonistic indulgence.â€”H.I. Listen: Bandcamp

### SHERELLE - 160 DOWN THE A406 (BEAUTIFUL)
> BEAUTIFULSHERELLE - 160 DOWN THE A406 While SHERELLE expressed plenty of frustration over the pandemic in 2021â€”and even scolded the UK government in a broadcast for Newsnightâ€”her debut EP was surprisingly light. The A-side, "160 Down The A406," is pure joy, featuring an airy chord progression, dreamy mallet melodies and chipmunk vocal cries all sewn into a breakbeat reverie. Although we can't in good faith recommend doing 160 MPH on the A406, we can put our weight behind this fuzzy footwork-jungle fusion, which showcases how SHERELLE can flex in the box just as much as she can behind the decks.â€”Emeka Okonkwo Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### MC Boing (Danny L Harle) - Boing Beat (Mad Decent)
> Mad DecentMC Boing (Danny L Harle) - Boing Beat MC Boing is one of the four new aliases Danny L Harle uses on his debut album. With "Boing Beat," he channels early '00s happy hardcore with spellbinding results. As part of the LP's virtual club experienceâ€”a four-story rave complex called Harlecoreâ€”Harle's tributes border on parody at certain moments. But at others he stumbles upon gold. "Boing Beat" is unapologetic, E'd-up euphoria taken to unnatural highs with MC Boing's manic vocals and Hannah Diamond's girlish, synthetic hook.. While Boing's half-screamed deliveries can be jarring at times, with lyrics as wholesome as "Everyone here is safe and nice / Makes me wanna have a great life," how could we do anything but smile and dance?â€”E.O. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### LSDXOXO - Sick Bitch (XL Recordings)
> XL RecordingsLSDXOXO - Sick Bitch Between those buzzing synth lines and RJ Glasgow's robotic but commanding vocals, "Sick Bitch" by LSDXOXO could easily become this generation's "Satisfaction" by Benny Banassi. The Berlin-based producer and DJ pulled even fewer punches than usual on his XL Recordings debut, opting to go full thrust with lyrics so raunchy they'd leave a conservative news anchor on life support. Talk of testing gag reflexes and exploding in one's own clothes leaves nothing to the imagination and can put every room it's played in in an erotic headlockâ€”or at least a sensual trance.â€”E.O. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Calibre & DRS v Mark Ernestus - Badder (Signature Records)
> Signature RecordsCalibre & DRS v Mark Ernestus - BadderBasic Channel cofounder Mark Ernestus made a relatively rare turn to the mixing console with "Badder," linking up with drum & bass legend Calibre to craft understated and moody dub techno. The song samples the original "Badman," featuring DRS, and subtly riffs on its name. Things get hypnotic as DRS's vocal chops ripple and echo through the mix, while a snare that threatens to land never does. All the while, hi-hats tick ominously like the second hand on a watch. The shadows loom larger in this dark makeover, a bass-heavy maze rife with riveting tension.â€”E.O. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Fiyahdred - Anyway (Do It) (Hyperdub)
> HyperdubFiyahdred - Anyway (Do It)Press officers will tell you tunes are anthems when they're not. But Hyperdub wasn't messing around with "Anyway (Do It)." There's nothing more exciting than a new artist breaking through with absolute fire. On the strength of this banger and the rest of their excellent debut EP, 2022 could be a life-changing year for the burgeoning UK producer.â€”Carlos Hawthorn Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

## [The Best Albums of 2021](https://ra.co/features/3950)
Date: 2021-12-15T21:27:34.000Z

### Space Afrika - Honest Labour (Dais Records)
> Dais RecordsSpace Afrika - Honest Labour Listening to Honest Labour feels like street lights burning onto tired retinas and long nights of feeling small in a big city. On their sophomore album, producers Joshua Inyang and Joshua Reid created a series of nocturnal meditations, a series of nineteen short tracks bleeding into one another, in tribute to their hometown of Manchester. The duo's instrumentation is replete with field recordings of urban white noise, balanced by resonant cellos, hazy guitars and spectral guest performances with fragments of profound conversationsâ€”as if overheard from the night beforeâ€”resulting in the audio equivalent of subconscious dreamscape. Put simply by Inyang and Reid themselves, Honest Labour is "an album about love and loss." The track "Indigo Grit," for instance, abruptly ends just as the speaker is about to explain the difference between liking and loving someoneâ€”a fleeting snippet of wisdom lost just before listeners could grab hold of it. But as with any inquiries into lifeâ€™s most existential questions, the artists weren't intending to arrive at any conclusions. Through their album, they embraced the sheer mystery of the human experience, remaining at the mercy of their emotions just like the rest of us.â€”Emeka Okonkwo Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### AceMoMA - A Future (Haus of Altr)
> Haus of AltrAceMoMA - A Future AceMo and MoMA Ready have released a gob-stopping amount of music over the past few years, but their second album together, A Future, really put it all into perspective. The duo work in a well-worn transatlantic tradition, blending drum & bass, jungle and techno, but in their hands it feels cutting-edge as they jump from one tempo to the next with tangible excitement. In spite of its name, the album is the sound of the duo creating a better present, of reimagining Afrofuturist narratives to suit the here-and-now rather than a distant future, of AceMoMA paving the way for everyone around them in New York and beyond.â€”Andrew Ryce Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Eris Drew - Quivering In Time (T4T LUV NRG)
> T4T LUV NRGEris Drew - Quivering In Time After conquering the DJing circuit with a mix of psychedelic evangelism and irresistible old-school techno flair, Eris Drew started dipping her toes into production with vibrant results. On her debut album, Quivering In Time, she outdoes herself with nine tracks of club heat packing a festival-sized dose of euphoria into a retro sound palette of tight drum loops, breakbeats and dewy pads. She even includes a sample of psychonaut and ethnobotanist Terence McKenna to drive the point home. House music in 2021 hardly got much more ecstatic than this.â€”A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Emeka Ogboh - Beyond The Yellow Haze (A-TON)
> A-TONEmeka Ogboh - Beyond The Yellow Haze Is Beyond The Yellow Haze pretty funky for an art installation? Quite possibly. The original piece catalogs the sounds of bustling Lagosâ€”car horns, traffic, chatter. Those recordings, made into an album for A-TONâ€”Ostgut Tonâ€™s art-forward sublabelâ€”forms the foundation for ghostly broken techno that moves with the start-stop pulse of everyday life in the city. Ogboh's rich, layered atmospherics approximate fog and the motion blur of brake lights on a busy freeway, capturing the vibe of a city in the midst of immense growth, like a moment encased in amber.â€”A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Erika de Casier - Sensational (4AD)
> 4ADErika de Casier - Sensational It's difficult to think of any other record this year that united more people from across different electronic music scenes than Sensational. Building on the Danish artist's Y2K R&B obsession and backed with lush yet subdued production from collaborator Central, it is a quiet storm of plucked strings, ornate piano and pitter-patter drums. De Casier's hushed voice alternates between vulnerable and sarcastic, full of biting phrases and memorable one-liners: "You gotta be polite if you wanna roll with me." Itâ€™s the kind of music that's made for both memorable dance floor moments and cryptic Instagram captions directed at you-know-who.â€”A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### George Riley - interest rates, a tape (Self-released)
> Self-releasedGeorge Riley - interest rates, a tape It's tempting to call George Riley an old soul given her use of R&B vocals over '90s-influenced jazzy breaks, but that wouldn't do justice to her first mixtape, which felt ambitious even at its most relaxed. Her words come out in a stream-of-consciousness blur, revealing and incisive in their casual, say-whatever-comes-to mind-flow ("I don't want any man / Full stop!"). Oliver Palfreyman's beats feel dynamic and fluid, as if tailored to every twist and turn in Riley's sinuous vocal melodies. Dark, uplifting and sometimes even funny, it is one of the most striking R&B debuts of the yearâ€”Afrofuturism tuned to a very personal frequency.â€”A.R. Listen: Spotify / Apple Music

### Hoavi - Invariant (Peak Oil)
> Peak OilHoavi - Invariant With Invariant, Hoavi set a new standard for what you might call ambient jungle. Combining the luxe atmospherics of dub techno, the fidgety pulse of footwork and the acrobatic loop-de-loops of jungle, the Russian producer's album is uncommonly beautiful, blowing minds while soothing them at the same time. You can pick any track at random and find something to obsess overâ€”the breakcore-in-the-clouds of "Dver," the Balearic funk of "Streamline." But the LP is best taken as a whole, a wash of creamy chords and aerodynamic drum programming.â€”A.R. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### Virtual Dreams: Ambient Explorations In The House & Techno Age, 1993-1997 (MUSIC FROM MEMORY)
> MUSIC FROM MEMORYVirtual Dreams: Ambient Explorations In The House & Techno Age, 1993-1997 Landing at the very end of 2020, when so many of us were deep in another round of lockdowns, Music From Memory's Virtual Dreams compilation was practically made for daydreaming in your bedroom. ### Various - The Sound Of Limo (Limousine Dream)
> Limousine DreamVarious - The Sound Of Limo Gene On Earth's The Sound of Limo compilation is a roster of the artists du jour of the new minimal scene, providing documentary evidence of a vital corner of the underground while also working surprisingly well as a cohesive album. Each producer gathered here, from Sugar Free to Dyed Soundorom, has their own quirks, but certain throughlinesâ€”chunky basslines, swung drums, cascading video game bleepsâ€”define a sub-genre of a sub-genre unto themselves. ### Skee Mask - Pool (Ilian Tape)
> Ilian TapeSkee Mask - Pool Clocking in at over an hour and 45 minutes, Pool demanded a commitment to active listening when it dropped. But Skee Mask has always excelled in the album format, and the extended run time allowed him to cover more ground than ever before. Pool takes the plunge into the sui generis cannabis haze of its soundscapes, where Skee Mask put his love of ambient atmosphere and UK dance music into conversation with bits of soulful funk, jazz and some of his fastest tempos yet (Pool went north of the 170 Arctic Circle at points). But, as only Skee Mask can, he creates an immersive and singular trip where genres come second to the textural richness and detail of his soundscapes, which range from danceable to stop-you-in-your-tracks gorgeousâ€”H.I. ### Yu Su - Yellow River Blue (biÃ© RECORDS)
> biÃ© RECORDSYu Su - Yellow River Blue Yu Su's steady stream of dance-adjacent 12-inches over the past four years established a dusky and increasingly ornate twist on the Vancouver house sound, but her debut album Yellow River Blue took her somewhere entirely new, both figuratively and literally. The album functions both as a travel diary and love song. It documents a tour through her native China from Qingdao to the far-west city of Xining, recorded in different cities across the country where Yu Su both reconnected with her homeland and found a whole new community of electronic producers she was previously cut off from. The album is appropriately restless and exploratory, as Yu Su charts a path through geography and genres, from slo-mo breakbeat to Krautrock to dubby downtempo. â€”H.I. ### Perila - How Much Time It Is Between You And Me? (Smalltown Supersound)
> Smalltown SupersoundPerila - How Much Time It Is Between You And Me? Aleksandra Zakharenko, alongside similar-minded artists like Ulla and Ben Bondy, makes ambient music that breaks the mold: it's not necessarily intended to bring you solace and definitely won't make an easy soundtrack for any hotel lobbies (or elevators). How Much Time It Is Between You And Me?, is just as unsettling and eerie as it is delicate. The album uses these mixed emotionsâ€”as well as touches of post-rock melodrama and angstâ€”to create a liminal state between waking and dreaming held together by Zakharenko's voice, which guides you through labyrinths that can be nightmarish but, just as quickly, morph into luxurious daydreams. â€”H.I. ### Andy Stott - Never The Right Time (Modern Love)
> Modern LoveAndy Stott - Never The Right Time It's been a decade since Andy Stott released the pair of EPs that introduced us to the dubby world of "knackered house." Since then, the UK artist's music has incorporated decaying memories of pop, like a ghostly outline caught in a photograph, through his ongoing collaborations with Alison Skidmore. Never The Right Time polished that rusting patina into Stott's most accessible album to date. "Don't Know How" is, by his standards, nearly bubblegum. This was true across the board on the recordâ€”even the abrasive mechanical rain of "Answers" ends with an uplifting, choral melody. Stott hasnâ€™t lost his penchant for darkness, but now he isnâ€™t afraid of contrasting it with bold and bright bursts of colour either.â€”H.I. Listen: Apple Music / Spotify / SoundCloud

### Wanton Witch - Wanton Witch (Stroboscopic Artefacts)
> Stroboscopic ArtefactsWanton Witch - Wanton Witch Stroboscopic Artefacts has been a hub for no-frills experimental techno for more than a decade, modeling itself in the restrained but psychedelic-friendly image of label owner Lucy. Following a year-long hiatus in 2020â€”after Lucy released a ten-year compilation of sleek dance floor cuts by mostly old guard artistsâ€”the label returned with the surprising self-titled LP from Bangkok-based Wanton Witch. The album opens a new chapter for Stroboscopic Artefacts, not only by featuring a queer, trans outsider artist, but by presenting a volatile, rave-adjacent sound palette beyond the label's wheelhouse. ### Dawn Richard - Second Line (Merge Records)
> Merge RecordsDawn Richard - Second Line Dawn Richard's sixth albumâ€”and first for the indie giant Mergeâ€”introduces her Afrofuturist alter ego, the golden, feather-plumed cyborg King Creole, who Richard described as an "assassination of stereotypes." ### L'Rain - Fatigue (Mexican Summer)
> Mexican SummerL'Rain - Fatigue L'Rain's second album meditates on the seismic complexities of a single emotionâ€”griefâ€”and its ability to exhaust and to destabilize, but to also spur personal evolution. ### V/A - Amapiano Now (NTS)
> NTSV/A - Amapiano Now If anything's apparent from the past few years, it's that dance music is inherently political. The most exciting dance music genre in the world at the momentâ€”amapianoâ€”demonstrates this point in a strikingly literal manner. Born in the townships in Gauteng, South Africa, the fledgling post-kwaito genre is the sound of joy in the midst of struggle. Now it's sweeping the globe. Amapiano Now, the 16-track compilation from NTS, is a bluffer's guide to the new South African dance phenomenon. From established acts like Vigro Deep and Gaba Canal to upstarts like Teno Afrika, the Shannen SP and Joe Cotch-curated collection demonstrates the inherent mid-tempo sensuality of amapiano, the thrilling sound of a generation of artists discovering their powerful collective voice. â€”Matt McDermott Listen: Spotify / Soundcloud

### Floating Points, Pharoah Sanders & The London Symphony Orchestra - Promises (Luaka Bop)
> Luaka BopFloating Points, Pharoah Sanders & The London Symphony Orchestra - Promises Reading over the personnel for Promises, one might expect a grandiose statementâ€”a multigenerational spiritual jazz odyssey for the ages. Instead, Sam Shepherd and the legendary Pharoah Sanders show a staggering knack for subtlety. Building upon a searching motif of four seven-note chords, both Shepherd and Sanders play with extraordinary humility. The careful arrangements serve as a backdrop for Sanders' restrained sax soloing, but the record doesnâ€™t headline one artist over the other. Instead it reaches for an ineffable oneness, the pinnacle of improvised exploration. Each gradual change feels monumental, like the spaced-out synth exploration on "Movement 7" or the Hammond organ passed through a vibrating Leslie speaker on "Movement 8." That Promises holds its ownâ€”and even stands outâ€”within one of the most important catalogues in jazz is a remarkable achievement. â€”M.M. Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify

### DJ Manny - Signals In My Head (Planet Mu)
> Planet MuDJ Manny - Signals In My Head 2021 was a golden year for footwork. This year, Planet Mu, once responsible for thrusting the Chicago genre onto the international stage in the mid-'10s, put out a trilogy of releases from stalwarts of this syncopated world: Jana Rush, RP Boo and DJ Manny. On Manny's contribution, the veteran Chicago-born, Brooklyn-based artist sought to bring romance to a genre historically known for soundtracking dance battles. If anyone could step up to this challenge, it would be DJ Manny and his smooth production style. Signals In My Head sees him whipping up some of the most airy atmospheres footwork has ever seen. Rosy melodies swirl into delirium while R&B vocals coo, sometimes lustfully and other times longingly, mellowing out its characteristically rougher rhythms and leaving only traces of a harder past.â€”Kiana Mickles Listen: Bandcamp / Apple Music / Spotify / Soundcloud

### Dean Blunt - Black Metal 2 (Rough Trade)
> Rough TradeDean Blunt - Black Metal 2 Dean Blunt has long been an elusive character, quietly releasing oblique albums without liner notes and responding to interview questions in riddles. His most recent record riffs on its predecessor's Americana themesâ€”heart-tugging strings, whining harmonica, desert rock guitar and somber and occasionally tongue-in-cheek lyrics that allude to loss, betrayal and the white critic's flimsy observations.
